Salah — Prayer
intermediate
12 min
Sajdah al-Tilawah: Rulings, Conditions, and Dispute on Persian Recitation
Detailed rulings on Sajdah al-Tilawah including causes, conditions, timing, and intra-Hanafi dispute on Persian recitation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions and rulings of Sajdah al-Tilawah and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding Persian recitation.

Core Idea
Sajdah al-Tilawah is wajib upon recitation or hearing, but obligation hinges on qualifiers and understanding for non-Arabic recitation.

This lesson unpacks the rulings of Sajdah al-Tilawah as presented in Nur al-Idah. You will learn when the prostration is obligatory, on whom, and the nuances of performing it inside and outside prayer. A key intra-Hanafi dispute regarding Persian recitation is also examined.

Guided Path
1
Identify the cause and legal status
Determine that the cause is recitation or hearing, and that the ruling is wajib (not fard).
The evidence for wajib is from hadith ahad, making it zanni al-thubut.
2
Analyze timing and location
Note that outside prayer it is at leisure (ala al-tarakhi), but during prayer it is immediate (ala al-tadyiq).
Delaying outside prayer is makruh tanzihan; delaying in prayer until after bowing renders the prostration invalid.
3
List conditions for obligation
The reciter must be qualified (sane, adult) and the listener must be a Muslim, sane, adult, and free from menstruation/postnatal bleeding for it to be obligatory upon them.
The prostration is not obligatory upon the reciter if they are a child, madman, etc.
4
Examine the Persian recitation dispute
According to Imam Abu Hanifah, hearing Persian recitation obligates prostration even without understanding. According to the Sahibayn, it obligates only if understood. The mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's view.
There is a report of Abu Hanifah retracting to the Sahibayn's view.
5
Identify exceptions and special cases
Menstruating and postnatal women are not obligated by their own recitation/hearing. The imam and follower in prayer are exempt from hearing from others during prayer; they should prostrate after prayer.
If a follower prostrates during prayer following the imam's recitation, his prayer becomes invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب سجود التلاوة سببه التلاوة على التالي والسامع في الصحيح، وهو واجب على التراخي إن لم يكن في الصلاة، وكره تأخيره تنزيهاً، ويجب على من تلا آية، ولو بالفارسية، وقراءة حرف. سجود التلاوة: إن قيل: كان الواجب أن يقول سجود التلاوة والسماع؛ لأن السماع سبب كالتلاوة ليصير بيانا للسببين؟ قلت لما كان عند المصنف يحلليه السجدة على السامع أيضًا. سبب وجوب التلاوة كما هو ترك لفظ السماع: لئلا يقع التدافع في الكلامين الصحيح قال بعضهم: التلاوة سبب لوجود السجدة على السامع دون السماء ماع، وقيل: السماع في حقه هو السبب، وهو اختيار فخر الإسلام يلقيه، لكن الجواب عنه: أن الاصل في السببية هو التلاوة، والسماع بناء عليه؛ لأنه من المتولدات. [الكفاية: ٤٦٦/١] : وهو واجب واعلم أنه إنما تجب السجدة إذا تحققت القراءة من الأهل، وهو أن يكون عاقلاً غير محجور عليه، حتى لو علم الببغاء آية السجدة وجرى على لسانه لا تجب على السامع السجدة، وكذا لا تحب بقراءة المجنون. الكفاية: ٤٦٦/١] على التراخي: اعلم أن سجدة التلاوة واجبة على التراخي إن لم تكن صلاتية؛ لأن دلائل الوجوب مطلقة عن تعيين الوقت، فيجب في جزء من الوقت غير عين، ويتعين ذلك بتعيينه فعلاً، وإنما يتضيق عليه الوجوب في آخر عمره كما في سائر الواجبات ،الموسعة، وأما المتلوة في الصلاة فإنها تجب على سبيل التضييق؛ لقيام دليل التضييق، وهو أنها وجبت بما هو من أفعال الصلاة، وهو القراءة، فالتحقت بأقوالها وصارت جزءًا من أجزائها، ولهذا قلنا: إذا تلا آية السجدة و لم يسجد ولم يركع حتى طالت القراءة، ثم ركع ونوى السجدة لم تجز. [البحر بتغيير : ١٨٩/٢] ويجب على من إلخ: أطلقه ، وهو مقيد بما إذا كان أهلاً لوجوب الصلاة عليه إما أداء أو قضاء، فهو من أهل وجوب السجدة عليه ومن لا فلا؛ لأن السجدة جزء من أجزاء الصلاة، فيشترط لوجوبها أهلية من الإسلام والعقل والبلوغ والطهارة من الحيض والنفاس حتى لا تجب على كافر وصبي ومجنون وحائض ونفساء قرؤوا أو سمعوا وتجب على المحدث والجنب وكذا تجب على السامع بتلاوة هؤلاء إلا المجنون لعدم أهليته لانعدام التمييز كالسماع من الصدى كذا في "البدائع". [البحر الرائق: ١٩٠/٢] بالفارسية: أما في حق السامع: فإن كانت القراءة بالعربية وجب على السامع فهم أو لم يفهم إجماعاً، وإن كانت بالفارسية لزم السامع أيضاً وإن لم يفهم عند الإمام، وعندهما لا يلزم إلا إذا فهم، وروي رجوعه إليهما. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٨٠] وقراءة حرف إلخ [أي الكلمة الدالة على السجدة (حاشية الطحطاوي)] أي إذا قرء حرفاً من كلمات دلت على السجدة مع قراءة كلمة قبله أو بعده وجبت عليه سجدة التلاوة كما تحب عليه إذا قرأ الآية بتمامها. كتاب الصلاة السجدة 17. سجود التلاوة مع كلمة قبله أو بعده من آيتها كالآية في الصحيح، وآياتها أربع عشرة آية في الأعراف والرعد، والنحل، والإسراء ومريم، وأولى الحج، والفرقان، والنمل، والسجدة، وص، وحم السجدة ،والنجم وانشقت، واقرأ. ويجب السجود على من سمع وإن لم يقصد السماع إلا الحائض والنفساء والإمام والمقتدي به ولو سمعوها من غيره سجدوا بعد الصلاة، ولو سجدوا فيها لم تُجزهم ولم تفسد صلاتهم و صلبة أي المقتدون والإمام أي غير المؤتم في الصحيح وقيل لا يجب إلا أن يقرأ أكثر آية السجدة، سواء كان الأكثر قبل كلمة السجود أو بعدها أو متوسطة، وهو رواية عن محمد، واختاره الزيلعي مراقي الفلاح، حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٨١] هي في الأعراف: اعلم أن السجدة في الأعراف تجب عند قوله تعالى: يَسْجُدُونَ ، وفي الرعد عند قوله تعالى: الأصال، وفي النحل عند قوله تعالى: أَوْ يُسْلِمُونَ ، وفي النحل عند قوله تعالى: ﴿وَاعْبُدُوا، وفي الإسراء عند قوله تعالى: وخُشُوعاً، وفي مريم عند قوله تعالى وبكيا، وفي الحج عند قوله تعالى: يشاءُ، وفي الفرقان عند قوله تعالى: نُفُوراً، وفي النمل عند قوله تعالى: العظيم ، وفي السجدة عند قوله تعالى: يسْتَكْبِرُون، وفي ص عند قوله تعالى: ﴿وَحُسْنُ مَآبِ ، وفي حم السجدة عند قوله تعالى: وَاعْبُدُوا، وفي انشقت عند قوله تعالى: ولا يَسْجُدُونَ ، وفي اقرأ عند قوله تعالى: ﴿وَاقْتَرَبَ على من سمع فهم أو لم يفهم قال ابن أمير :حاج ينبغي أن يستثنى منه مثل الأعجمي الخالص الحديث العهد بالإسلام، فلا تجب عليه السجدة بتلاوة النظم القرآني ولا بسماعه إلا بعد العلم بكون المقروء سجدة تلاوة، يعني وإن لم يفهم؛ لأن التكليف بما لا علم له به محال حتى لو مات قبل الأداء والعلم بالوجوب لا إثم عليه، ولا تجب عليه إلا وقت العلم . [ مراقي الفلاح، حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٨٤] إلا الحائض والنفساء فلا تجب عليهما بتلاوتهما وسماعهما شيئاً، وتجب بالسماع منهما ومن الجنب وبسماعها من كافر وصبي مميز. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٨٤] والإمام والمقتدى به فلا تجب عليهما بالسماع من مقتد بالإمام السامع أو بإمام آخر، وتجب على من ليس في الصلاة بسماعه من المقتدي على الأصح مراقي الفلاح: ٤٨٤] . وقال الطحطاوي: هذا خلاف الأصح، والأصح الوجوب على من ليس مشاركاً له في تلك الصلاة مطلقاً، سواء كان السامع في جماعة أخرى أو منفرداً أو خارجاً بالكلية. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٨٤] ولم تفسد صلاتهم قيده في "التجنيس" وغيره بما إذا لم يتابع الإمام المصلي التالي في سجوده، فإن تابعه فسدت، ولا تجزيه السجدة عما سمع كما في "البحر" و"النهر". [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٨٥]
Chapter of Prostration of Recitation. Its cause is recitation upon the reciter and the listener according to the correct view, and it is obligatory at leisure if not in prayer, and it is disliked to delay it as tanzih. It is obligatory upon whoever recites a verse, even in Persian, and reading a letter. Prostration of recitation: If it is said: It was obligatory to say 'prostration of recitation and hearing' because hearing is a cause like recitation to make it explanatory of both causes? I say: Because according to the author, the prostration is also upon the listener. The cause of obligation is recitation, as he left out the word 'hearing' to avoid contradiction in the two correct statements. Some said: recitation is the cause for the existence of the prostration upon the listener, not hearing; and it is said: hearing in his case is the cause, and that is the choice of Fakhr al-Islam; but the answer to that: the origin in causality is recitation, and hearing is based upon it; because it is from the derivative things. [Al-Kifayah: 1/466]: And it is obligatory. Know that the prostration is only obligatory if the recitation is verified from a qualified person, meaning one who is sane and not legally interdicted, such that if a parrot was taught the verse of prostration and it came upon its tongue, the listener is not obligated to prostrate, and similarly it is not obligatory by the recitation of a madman. [Al-Kifayah: 1/466] At leisure: Know that the prostration of recitation is obligatory at leisure if it is not during prayer; because the proofs of obligation are unrestricted regarding specification of time, so it is obligatory in some part of time not specified, and it is specified by its actual specification, and it becomes restricted upon him at the end of his life as in all other expansive obligatory acts. As for the recited one in prayer, it is obligatory in a restricted manner due to the evidence of restriction, which is that it became obligatory by what is from the actions of prayer, namely recitation, so it attaches to its statements and becomes a part of its parts, and therefore we said: if he recites a verse of prostration and does not prostrate nor bow until the recitation becomes long, then bows and intends the prostration, it does not suffice. [Al-Bahr with modification: 2/189] And it is obligatory upon from etc.: He gave it unrestrictedly, and it is restricted to when [the person] is qualified for obligation of prayer upon him either as performance or makeup, so he is among those upon whom the prostration is obligatory and who is not; because the prostration is a part of the parts of prayer, so for its obligation, qualification of Islam, sanity, puberty, and purity from menstruation and postnatal bleeding is required, such that it is not obligatory upon an unbeliever, child, madman, menstruating woman, and woman with postnatal bleeding if they recited or heard, and it is obligatory upon a person in minor impurity and a person in major impurity, and similarly it is obligatory upon the listener by the recitation of these except the madman due to his lack of qualification for lack of discernment, like hearing from an echo. Likewise in 'Al-Bada'i'. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 2/190] In Persian: As for the case of the listener: if the recitation is in Arabic, it is obligatory upon the listener whether he understood or not, by consensus. If it was in Persian, it is also binding upon the listener even if he did not understand, according to Imam Abu Hanifah. According to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is not binding unless he understood. And it is reported that he (Abu Hanifah) retracted to their view. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 480] And reading a letter, etc. [i.e., the word indicating the prostration (Hashiyah al-Tahtawi)] meaning if he recited a letter from the words that indicate the prostration along with reciting a word before or after it, the prostration of recitation becomes obligatory upon him, just as it becomes obligatory upon him if he recites the entire verse. Book of Prayer, Prostration 17. Sajdah al-Tilawah with a word before or after it from its verse is like the verse according to the correct view. Its verses are fourteen verses: in Al-A'raf, Al-Ra'd, Al-Nahl, Al-Isra', Maryam, the first of Al-Hajj, Al-Furqan, Al-Naml, Al-Sajdah, Sad, Ha Mim Al-Sajdah, Al-Najm, Al-Inshiqaq, and Iqra'. It is obligatory to prostrate upon whoever hears, even if he did not intend to hear, except the menstruating woman, the one with postnatal bleeding, the imam, and the one being led (by the imam). If they hear it from someone else, they should prostrate after the prayer; if they prostrate during it, it does not suffice them nor does it invalidate their prayer. And 'saliba' means the followers and the imam means one who is not being led, according to the correct view. It was said: it is not obligatory unless he recites most of the verse of prostration, whether the majority is before the word of prostration or after it or in the middle, and this is a narration from Muhammad, and it was chosen by al-Zayla'i; [Maraqi al-Falah, Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 481]. They are: In Al-A'raf: know that the prostration in Al-A'raf is obligatory at His saying: 'yasjudoon' (they prostrate); in Al-Ra'd at His saying: 'al-asal' (the shades?) [؟]; in Al-Nahl at His saying: 'yu slimoon' (they submit?) [؟]; and in Al-Nahl at His saying: 'wa'budoo' (and worship); in Al-Isra' at His saying: 'wa khushoo'an' (and humility); in Maryam at His saying: 'wa bakiyya' (and weeping?) [؟]; in Al-Hajj at His saying: 'yasha'u' (He wills); in Al-Furqan at His saying: 'nufooran' (aversion); in Al-Naml at His saying: 'al-'azeem' (the Mighty); in Al-Sajdah at His saying: 'yastakbiroon' (they are arrogant); in Sad at His saying: 'wa husna ma'ab' (and goodly return); in Ha Mim Al-Sajdah at His saying: 'wa'budoo' (and prostrate); in Al-Inshiqaq at His saying: 'wa la yasjudoon' (and they do not prostrate); in Iqra' at His saying: 'waqtaraba' (and draw near). Upon whoever hears, whether he understood or not, Ibn Amir Haj said: An exception should be made for one like a pure non-Arab new to Islam, so prostration is not obligatory upon him by recitation of the Quranic text nor by hearing it except after knowledge that what is recited is a prostration of recitation, meaning even if he did not understand; because obligation of what one has no knowledge of is impossible, such that if he died before performance and knowledge of obligation, there is no sin upon him, and it is not obligatory upon him except at the time of knowledge. [Maraqi al-Falah, Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 484] Except the menstruating woman and the one with postnatal bleeding: it is not obligatory upon them by their recitation or hearing anything, and it is obligatory by hearing from them and from a person in major impurity, and by hearing from an unbeliever and a discerning child. [Maraqi al-Falah: 484] And the imam and the one being led: it is not obligatory upon them by hearing from a follower of the imam who is listening or from another imam, and it is obligatory upon one who is not in prayer by hearing from a follower according to the most correct view. [Maraqi al-Falah: 484] And al-Tahtawi said: This is contrary to the most correct, and the most correct is obligation upon one who is not participating with him in that prayer absolutely, whether the listener is in another congregation or alone or completely outside. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 484] And their prayer is not invalidated – it is restricted in 'al-Tajnis' and others to when he does not follow the imam who is praying and reciting in his prostration; if he follows him, it becomes invalid, and the prostration does not suffice for what he heard, as in 'al-Bahr' and 'al-Nahr'. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 485]
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah with its commentary (Bushra) presents the rulings of Sajdah al-Tilawah (prostration of recitation). The passage type is a ruling statement with some proofs and intra-Hanafi disputes. 

The chapter begins by stating the cause of the prostration: recitation (tilawah) by the reciter or hearing (sama') by the listener. The author clarifies that the cause is primarily recitation, and hearing is a derivative cause. The prostration is wajib (obligatory) and should be performed at leisure if not in prayer; delaying it is makruh tanzihan (slightly disliked). It becomes obligatory upon reciting a verse, even in Persian, or reading a letter that indicates prostration.

The commentary then addresses a potential objection: why not call it 'Sajdah al-Tilawah wa al-Sama'?' The answer is that the author considered hearing as also a cause for the listener, but left out the word 'hearing' to avoid contradiction. The original causality is recitation, and hearing is based on it.

Next, conditions for obligation are discussed: the recitation must be from a qualified person (sane, not legally interdicted). If a parrot recites, no prostration is required. The prostration is obligatory at leisure for out-of-prayer recitation, but during prayer it is obligatory immediately. If one delays it in prayer and then intends it after bowing, it does not suffice.

Qualification for obligation includes being Muslim, sane, adult, and free from menstruation/postnatal bleeding. Thus, it is not obligatory upon an unbeliever, child, madman, menstruating woman, etc. However, it is obligatory upon a person in minor or major impurity. For the listener, it is obligatory if the recitation is in Arabic, even if not understood, by consensus. If in Persian, according to Imam Abu Hanifah it is obligatory even if not understood; according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is obligatory only if understood. It is reported that Imam Abu Hanifah retracted to their view.

Reading a single letter that indicates prostration, with a word before or after from the same verse, also makes it obligatory. The verses of prostration are fourteen, listed by surah and specific word.

The passage then discusses exceptions: menstruating and postnatal women are not obligated by their own recitation or hearing, but hearing from them obligates others. The imam and follower are not obligated by hearing from someone else during prayer; they should prostrate after prayer. If they prostrate during prayer, it does not suffice but does not invalidate the prayer. However, if a person in prayer follows the reciter's prostration, his prayer becomes invalid.

Finally, a special case: a pure non-Arab new to Islam is not obligated unless he knows the recitation is a prostration verse.

Key Terms
سجود التلاوة (sujūd al-tilāwah): Prostration performed when reciting or hearing a verse of prostration in the Quran
التلاوة (al-tilāwah): Recitation of the Quran, specifically verses of prostration
السماع (al-samā‘): Hearing the recitation of a prostration verse
على التراخي (‘alā al-tarākhī): At leisure, not immediately required; opposite of ‘alā al-tadyīq (immediate)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi Hanafi position, Sajdah al-Tilawah is obligatory upon hearing Persian recitation only if:
A) The listener is an adult Muslim.
B) The listener understands the recitation.
C) The recitation is in Arabic.
D) The listener intended to hear.

Key Takeaway
Sajdah al-Tilawah is wajib upon recitation or hearing, with conditions regarding the reciter's qualification and, for non-Arabic recitation, the listener's understanding.

The 14 Verses and Obligation of Sujud al-Tilawah
Lists verses and obligation with exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the fourteen verses of sajdah and state the Hanafi ruling that sujud al-tilawah is wajib upon the hearer, with the exceptions.

Core Idea
Sujud al-tilawah is wajib upon hearing, even unintentionally — except for menstruating women, postpartum women, and those in prayer.

Sujud al-tilawah is a distinct act of worship triggered by specific verses. This ruling statement from Nur al-Idah outlines the fourteen verses and the general obligation to prostrate upon hearing them, along with key exceptions that apply during prayer and for women in states of impurity.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the 14 verses
Identify the surahs listed: al-A'raf, al-Ra'd, al-Nahl (two verses), al-Isra', Maryam, al-Hajj (first), al-Furqan, al-Naml, al-Sajdah, Sad, Ha Mim al-Sajdah, al-Najm, al-Inshiqaq, and al-'Alaq. These are foundational for recognizing when sujud al-tilawah is triggered.
Some surahs have two sajdah verses; al-Nahl is one such case.
2
State the general obligation
The text says 'yajib al-sujud 'ala man sami'a' – prostration is obligatory upon the one who hears, even if unintentionally. This includes both reciter and listener.
The hukm level is wajib, meaning omission is sinful but not as severe as fard.
3
Recognize the exceptions
Exceptions: menstruating woman (ha'id), postpartum woman (nafsa') – they are not obligated at all. Also, imam and follower (muqtadi) in prayer are not obligated during prayer if they hear from another; they must perform sujud after the prayer.
If they prostrate during prayer, it does not count and does not invalidate prayer unless they follow the imam's sujud.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Muhammad holds that obligation requires reciting most of the verse of prostration; Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold any part suffices. The relied-upon view is that obligation arises from hearing any part, but the minority view is noted.
This difference affects whether one must prostrate upon hearing the entire verse or just the word 'sajdah' itself.

Source Text

سجود التلاوة
مع كلمة قبله أو بعده من آيتها كالآية في الصحيح، وآياتها أربع عشرة آية في الأعراف والرعد، والنحل، والإسراء ومريم، وأولى الحج، والفرقان، والنمل، والسجدة، وص، وحم السجدة ،والنجم وانشقت، واقرأ. ويجب السجود على من سمع وإن لم يقصد السماع إلا الحائض والنفساء والإمام والمقتدي به ولو سمعوها من غيره سجدوا بعد الصلاة، ولو سجدوا فيها لم تُجزهم ولم تفسد صلاتهم

أي المقتدون والإمام أي غير المؤتم

في الأعراف: اعلم أن السجدة في الأعراف تجب عند قوله تعالى: يَسْجُدُونَ ، وفي الرعد عند قوله تعالى: الأصال، وفي النحل عند قوله تعالى: أَوْ يُسْلِمُونَ ، وفي النحل عند قوله تعالى: ﴿وَاعْبُدُوا، وفي الإسراء عند قوله تعالى: وخُشُوعاً، وفي مريم عند قوله تعالى وبكيا، وفي الحج عند قوله تعالى: يشاءُ، وفي الفرقان عند قوله تعالى: نُفُوراً، وفي النمل عند قوله تعالى: العظيم ، وفي السجدة عند قوله تعالى: يسْتَكْبِرُون، وفي ص عند قوله تعالى: ﴿وَحُسْنُ مَآبِ ، وفي حم السجدة عند قوله تعالى: وَاعْبُدُوا،
وفي انشقت عند قوله تعالى: ولا يَسْجُدُونَ ، وفي اقرأ عند قوله تعالى: ﴿وَاقْتَرَبَ على من سمع فهم أو لم يفهم قال ابن أمير :حاج ينبغي أن يستثنى منه مثل الأعجمي الخالص الحديث العهد بالإسلام، فلا تجب عليه السجدة بتلاوة النظم القرآني ولا بسماعه إلا بعد العلم بكون المقروء سجدة تلاوة، يعني وإن لم يفهم؛ لأن التكليف بما لا علم له به محال حتى لو مات قبل الأداء والعلم بالوجوب لا إثم عليه، ولا تجب عليه إلا وقت العلم . [ مراقي الفلاح، حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٨٤] إلا الحائض والنفساء فلا تجب عليهما بتلاوتهما وسماعهما شيئاً، وتجب بالسماع منهما ومن الجنب وبسماعها من كافر وصبي مميز. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٨٤] والإمام والمقتدى به فلا تجب عليهما بالسماع من مقتد بالإمام السامع أو بإمام آخر، وتجب على من ليس في الصلاة بسماعه من المقتدي على الأصح مراقي الفلاح: ٤٨٤] . وقال الطحطاوي: هذا خلاف الأصح، والأصح الوجوب على من ليس مشاركاً له في تلك الصلاة مطلقاً، سواء كان السامع في جماعة أخرى أو منفرداً أو خارجاً بالكلية. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٨٤] ولم تفسد صلاتهم قيده في 'التجنيس' وغيره بما إذا لم يتابع الإمام المصلي التالي في سجوده، فإن تابعه فسدت، ولا تجزيه السجدة عما سمع كما في 'البحر' و'النهر'. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٨٥]
The Book of Prayer. The Prostration. 17. Sujud al-Tilawah. With a word before or after it from its verse, it is like the verse according to the correct view. Its verses are fourteen: in al-A'raf, al-Ra'd, al-Nahl, al-Isra', Maryam, the first of al-Hajj, al-Furqan, al-Naml, al-Sajdah, Sad, Ha Mim al-Sajdah, al-Najm, Inshiqaq, and Iqra'. Sujud is obligatory upon the one who hears, even if he did not intend to hear, except a menstruating woman, a woman in postnatal bleeding, the imam, and the one following him. If they hear it from someone else, they should prostrate after the prayer; if they prostrate during it, it does not suffice them and does not invalidate their prayer. [Commentary: 'and he said' meaning the followers and the imam, meaning not the one being followed. According to the correct view, it is said it is not obligatory unless one recites most of the verse of prostration, whether the majority is before the word of prostration, after it, or in the middle; this is a narration from Muhammad, and al-Zayla'i chose it. (Marqi al-Falah, Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 481) It is: In al-A'raf: Know that the prostration in al-A'raf becomes obligatory at His saying 'yasjudun'. In al-Ra'd: at His saying 'al-asal'. In al-Nahl: at His saying 'aw yuslimun'. In al-Nahl: at His saying 'wa'budu'. In al-Isra': at His saying 'wa khushu'an'. In Maryam: at His saying 'wa bikiyan'. In al-Hajj: at His saying 'yasha''. In al-Furqan: at His saying 'nufuran'. In al-Naml: at His saying 'al-'azim'. In al-Sajdah: at His saying 'yastakbirun'. In Sad: at His saying 'wa husnu ma'ab'. In Ha Mim al-Sajdah: at His saying 'wa'budu'. In Inshiqaq: at His saying 'wa la yasjudun'. In Iqra': at His saying 'waqtaraba'. Upon the one who hears, whether he understands or not. Ibn Amir Haj said: An exception should be made for one like a pure non-Arab newly converted to Islam; the prostration is not obligatory upon him by recitation of the Quranic text nor by hearing it except after knowing that what is recited is a prostration of recitation, meaning even if he does not understand, because obligation without knowledge is impossible, such that if he dies before performing it and knowledge of the obligation, there is no sin upon him, and it is not obligatory upon him except at the time of knowledge. (Marqi al-Falah, Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 484) Except the menstruating and postnatal woman: it is not obligatory upon them by their recitation or hearing anything, and it becomes obligatory by hearing from them and from a junub, and by hearing it from a disbeliever or a discerning child. (Marqi al-Falah: 484) The imam and the one being followed: it is not obligatory upon them by hearing from a follower of the imam or from another imam, and it is obligatory upon one not in prayer by hearing it from a follower according to the most correct view. (Marqi al-Falah: 484) And al-Tahtawi said: This is contrary to the most correct, and the most correct is the obligation upon whoever is not participating with him in that prayer absolutely, whether the hearer is in another congregation, alone, or completely outside. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 484) 'And does not invalidate their prayer' is restricted in al-Tajnis and others to when he does not follow the imam who recited in his prostration; if he follows him, it becomes invalid, and the prostration does not suffice for what he heard, as in al-Bahr and al-Nahr. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 485)
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from Nur al-Idah on Sujud al-Tilawah. It begins by listing the fourteen verses of prostration: in Surahs al-A'raf, al-Ra'd, al-Nahl (two verses), al-Isra', Maryam, al-Hajj (first), al-Furqan, al-Naml, al-Sajdah, Sad, Ha Mim al-Sajdah, al-Najm, al-Inshiqaq, and al-'Alaq (Iqra'). Then it states the general obligation: sujud is wajib upon anyone who hears these verses, even if they did not intend to listen. However, there are exceptions: a menstruating woman, a woman in postnatal bleeding, the imam leading prayer, and the follower (muqtadi) are not obligated during prayer. If they hear it from someone else, they must prostrate after the prayer; if they prostrate during the prayer, it does not count for the sujud al-tilawah but also does not invalidate the prayer. The commentary clarifies that the obligation applies even if one does not understand the meaning, but a new non-Arab convert is exempt until they know it is a prostration verse. Additionally, there is an intra-Hanafi difference: according to a narration from Imam Muhammad, obligation requires reciting most of the verse of prostration. The correct view in the madhhab is that hearing even a part obligates. Also, the imam and follower in prayer are not obligated by hearing from someone else in the same prayer, but al-Tahtawi holds the more correct view that any non-participant in the same prayer is obligated. Finally, if a person in prayer follows the reciter's prostration, his prayer becomes invalid and the sujud does not fulfill the obligation.

Key Terms
سجود التلاوة (sujud al-tilawah): Prostration performed upon reciting or hearing specific verses of the Quran.
الحائض (al-ha'id): A woman experiencing menstruation; exempt from sujud al-tilawah.
النفساء (al-nafsa'): A woman in postnatal bleeding; same ruling as menstruating woman.
المقتدي (al-muqtadi): The follower in congregational prayer; not obligated during prayer if he hears from imam or another follower.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many verses of prostration are there in the Hanafi school according to this text?
A) 13
B) 14
C) 15
D) 10

Key Takeaway
Sujud al-tilawah is wajib upon any hearer of the 14 sajdah verses, with clear exceptions for menstruating/postpartum women and those in prayer (who must prostrate later).

Conditions for Obligation of Sujud al-Tilawah: Persian, Sleep, and Echo
Rulings on obligation conditions for Sujud al-Tilawah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which hearing a prostration verse in Persian obligates sujud and identify exceptions for hearing from a sleeping person, insane person, bird, or echo.

Core Idea
Sujud al-tilawah is wajib only upon hearing a valid recitation that is understood, directly from a conscious reciter.

The obligation of sujud al-tilawah is not triggered by every sound. The Hanafi school specifies conditions for the recitation to be considered valid. This lesson covers the ruling when the verse is recited in Persian, and cases where the recitation is heard from a sleeping person, an insane person, a bird, or an echo.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Sujud al-tilawah is wajib upon hearing a prostration verse. Begin by locating the core obligation statement in the text.
2
Examine the condition for Persian
The text states it is obligatory only if understood. Why? Because the obligation is linked to the listener's comprehension of the verse.
Consider the intra-Hanafi difference: Abu Hanifa vs. the Sahibayn on whether understanding is required.
3
Analyze the case of sleeping/insane reciter
The recitation from a sleeping or insane person is not considered valid due to lack of discernment, so no obligation is triggered. Note the conflicting positions attributed to Muhammad and others.
The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is that it is not obligatory.
4
Distinguish echo and bird
An echo is not a direct human recitation; a bird's mimicry is not human speech. Therefore, neither obligates sujud.
This is agreed upon across all schools.

في ظاهر الرواية وقيل: لا تفسد، ونسب إلى محمد، وفي 'غاية البيان': الأصح عدم الفساد اتفاقاً. حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٨٥] على المعتمد وهذا عندهما، وتجب عليه عند أبي حنيفة وإن لم يفهم معناها إذا أخبر بأنها آية سجدة مراقي الفلاح: ٤٨٥] واختلف التصحيح إلخ : أي صحح بعضهم قولا، وبعضهم قولا آخر، فإنه ذكر شيخ الإسلام أنه لا يجب؛ لعدم صحة التلاوة لفقد التمييز، وفي التتارخانية": سمعها من نائم،
قيل: تحب، والصحيح أنها لا تجب، وفي 'الخانية': الصحيح هو الوجوب. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٨٥] والصدى: وهو ما يجيبك مثل صوتك في الجبال والصحارى ونحوها مراقي الفلاح: ٤٨٦] وتؤدى إلخ: أي إذا قرأ المصلي آية السجدة في الصلاة، ثم ركع أو سجد، فالسجدة التلاوية تؤدى بهما.
في الصلاة هذا القيد بالنسبة إلى الركوع فقط، فلا يجزئ عنها ركوع في خارجها؛ لأن الأثر إنما ورد فيما إذا ركع فيها فقط، فيقتصر على مورد الأثر ، لكن في 'البحر' : واختار 'قاضي خان' أن الركوع خارج الصلاة ينوب عنها. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٨٦] ويجزئ عنها إلخ : وينبغي ذلك للإمام مع كثرة القوم أو حال المخافتة لا يؤدي إلى التخليط. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٨٦] وإن لم ينوها إلخ : أي ولو لم يركع حتى طالت القراءة لم يجز، وإن نواه عن السجدة، وكذا السجدة الصلاتية لا تنوب عنها إذا طالت القراءة؛ لأنها صارت ديناً لوجوبها مضيقاً،
حتى
والدين يقضى بما له لا بما عليه والركوع والسجود عليه فلا يتأدى به الدين. [البحر الرائق: ١٩٥/٢] إذا لم ينقطع: اعلم أن الفور لا ينقطع بآية بعد آيتها أو آيتين اتفاقاً، وينقطع بأربع اتفاقاً، واختلف في الثلاث: فقيل: ينقطع، واختاره خواهر زاده وقيل لا واختاره الحلواني [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٨٧] في الأظهر: اعلم أنه إذا دخل مع الإمام في الركعة الثانية، وقد فرغ الإمام من السجدة التلاوية التي سمعها هذا المسبوق ففيه اختلاف، وظاهر 'الهداية' يقتضي أن يسجد لها بعد الفراغ؛ لأنه لما لم يدرك ركعة التلاوة لم يصر مدركاً لها، وليست صلاتية فيقضى خارجها، وقيل: هي صلاتية، فلا تقضى خارجها.
According to the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwayah), and it is obligatory by hearing Persian if he understands it according to the relied-upon view. And there is difference in correction regarding its obligation by hearing from a sleeping person or an insane person, and it is not obligatory by hearing it from a bird, an echo. And it is performed by bowing (ruku') or prostration (sujud) in the prayer, other than the prayer's ruku' and sujud. And sujud is better. And the prayer's ruku' suffices for it if he intends it, and its sujud even if he did not intend it, provided the immediacy (fawr) is not interrupted by more than two verses. [Commentary] Meaning he intends to perform it in it. And the prostration of recitation by more than two verses. And if he hears from an imam and does not follow him, or follows in another rak'ah, he prostrates outside the prayer according to the most apparent. [Commentary] Related to the last issue. According to the apparent narration, it is said it does not invalidate, and it is attributed to Muhammad. In Ghayat al-Bayan, the most correct is no invalidation by agreement. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 485) According to the relied-upon, and this is with them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). And it is obligatory upon him according to Abu Hanifa even if he does not understand its meaning if he is informed that it is a verse of prostration. (Marqi al-Falah: 485) 'And there is difference in correction' etc.: meaning some scholars corrected one statement, and others another. For Shaykh al-Islam mentioned that it is not obligatory due to lack of validity of recitation due to loss of discernment. In al-Tatarkhaniyyah: he heard it from a sleeping person; it is said it is obligatory, and the correct is that it is not obligatory. In al-Khaniyyah: the correct is obligation. (Marqi al-Falah: 485) The echo: that which responds to you like your voice in mountains, deserts, and the like. (Marqi al-Falah: 486) 'And it is performed' etc.: if a praying person recites a verse of prostration in prayer, then bows or prostrates, the sujud al-tilawah is performed by them. 'In the prayer' this restriction applies only to ruku'; so ruku' outside it does not suffice because the effect (athar) is only reported when he bowed in it, so it is restricted to the case of the effect. But in al-Bahr, Qadi Khan chose that ruku' outside prayer substitutes for it. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 486) 'And it suffices' etc.: and this is recommended for the imam when there are many people or when reciting quietly so as not to lead to confusion. (Marqi al-Falah: 486) 'Even if he did not intend it' etc.: meaning if he did not bow until the recitation became long, it does not suffice, even if he intended it for the sujud. Similarly, the prayer's sujud does not substitute for it if the recitation becomes long, because it becomes a debt due to its obligation being immediate; and debt is paid with what is owed, not with what is not owed, and ruku' and sujud are not owed, so the debt is not fulfilled. (Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 2/195) 'If the immediacy is not interrupted': know that the immediacy is not interrupted by one or two verses after it by agreement, and is interrupted by four by agreement, and there is difference regarding three: it is said it is interrupted, chosen by Khwahar Zadeh, and it is said not, chosen by al-Halwani. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 487) 'In the most apparent': know that if he enters with the imam in the second rak'ah, and the imam has finished the sujud al-tilawah that this latecomer heard, there is difference. The apparent of al-Hidayah requires that he prostrates for it after finishing, because since he did not catch the rak'ah of recitation, he does not become a perceiver of it, and it is not a prayer prostration, so he makes it up outside. And it is said it is a prayer prostration, so it is not made up outside.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on Sujud al-Tilawah, focusing on conditions and performance. According to Zahir al-Riwayah, hearing the verse in Persian obligates sujud only if the listener understands it. There is disagreement on hearing from a sleeping or insane person: some say it is not obligatory because there is no valid recitation; the correct view is it is not obligatory. Hearing from a bird or echo does not obligate. In prayer, sujud al-tilawah can be performed by either bowing (ruku') or prostrating (sujud), but sujud is better. The prayer's ruku' suffices if one intends the sujud; the prayer's sujud suffices even without intention, provided that the immediacy (fawr) is not interrupted by more than two verses. If more than two verses pass, the sujud becomes a debt that must be performed later. The commentary explains that ruku' outside prayer does not suffice according to the apparent narration, but Qadi Khan allows it. For a latecomer (masbuq) who hears the imam recite a prostration verse but joins later, the apparent view in al-Hidayah is that he prostrates after the prayer, as he did not catch the rak'ah of recitation and it is not a prayer prostration.

Key Terms
الفارسية (al-farisiyyah): Persian language; hearing the verse in Persian obligates sujud only if understood.
الصدى (al-sada): Echo; hearing from echo does not obligate sujud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Only if the listener understands the meaning.
C) Only if the reciter is in a state of prayer.
D) Only if the verse is recited aloud.

Key Takeaway
The obligation of sujud al-tilawah hinges on hearing a valid recitation from a conscious reciter, with understanding required for non-Arabic recitations.

Method of Performing Sujud al-Tilawah in Prayer: Ruku', Sujud, and the Fawr Requirement
Performance method of Sujud al-Tilawah in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how sujud al-tilawah is performed in prayer via ruku' or sujud, the intention requirements, and the rule of fawr (immediacy) with its interruption limits.

Core Idea
Sujud al-tilawah in prayer can be fulfilled by ruku' with intention or sujud without intention, provided the fawr is not broken by more than two verses.

Performing sujud al-tilawah during prayer has specific rules. The text explains that the prayer's ruku' or sujud can substitute for the prostration of recitation, but with conditions on intention and timing. This lesson unpacks those details.

Guided Path
1
Identify the permissible methods
The text says sujud al-tilawah in prayer can be performed by either a separate ruku' or sujud. Which action is preferable?
Sujud is considered better (afdal).
2
Understand the substitution rule for ruku'
If the praying person bows (ruku') intending it for sujud al-tilawah, it suffices. If he prostrates, no intention is needed, provided the fawr is not broken.
Why is intention required for ruku' but not for sujud? Because sujud is more specific to the act.
3
Define fawr and its interruption
Fawr (immediacy) means the sujud must be performed without delay. If more than two verses are recited after the sajdah verse before performing sujud, the fawr is broken and sujud becomes a debt.
Agreed upon: interruption by 1-2 verses does not break fawr; 4 verses definitely breaks it; dispute on 3 verses.
4
Apply the ruling to a latecomer (masbuq) – preview
Note: a latecomer who joins after the imam's recitation will prostrate outside prayer (covered in next lesson). This highlights that the sujud here is prayer-associated but not a prayer pillar.
This step is a bridge to the next lesson.

Source Text

في ظاهر الرواية وقيل: لا تفسد، ونسب إلى محمد، وفي 'غاية البيان': الأصح عدم الفساد اتفاقاً. حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٨٥] على المعتمد وهذا عندهما، وتجب عليه عند أبي حنيفة وإن لم يفهم معناها إذا أخبر بأنها آية سجدة مراقي الفلاح: ٤٨٥] واختلف التصحيح إلخ : أي صحح بعضهم قولا، وبعضهم قولا آخر، فإنه ذكر شيخ الإسلام أنه لا يجب؛ لعدم صحة التلاوة لفقد التمييز، وفي التتارخانية": سمعها من نائم،
قيل: تحب، والصحيح أنها لا تجب، وفي 'الخانية': الصحيح هو الوجوب. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٨٥] والصدى: وهو ما يجيبك مثل صوتك في الجبال والصحارى ونحوها مراقي الفلاح: ٤٨٦] وتؤدى إلخ: أي إذا قرأ المصلي آية السجدة في الصلاة، ثم ركع أو سجد، فالسجدة التلاوية تؤدى بهما.
في الصلاة هذا القيد بالنسبة إلى الركوع فقط، فلا يجزئ عنها ركوع في خارجها؛ لأن الأثر إنما ورد فيما إذا ركع فيها فقط، فيقتصر على مورد الأثر ، لكن في 'البحر' : واختار 'قاضي خان' أن الركوع خارج الصلاة ينوب عنها. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٨٦] ويجزئ عنها إلخ : وينبغي ذلك للإمام مع كثرة القوم أو حال المخافتة لا يؤدي إلى التخليط. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٨٦] وإن لم ينوها إلخ : أي ولو لم يركع حتى طالت القراءة لم يجز، وإن نواه عن السجدة، وكذا السجدة الصلاتية لا تنوب عنها إذا طالت القراءة؛ لأنها صارت ديناً لوجوبها مضيقاً،
حتى
والدين يقضى بما له لا بما عليه والركوع والسجود عليه فلا يتأدى به الدين. [البحر الرائق: ١٩٥/٢] إذا لم ينقطع: اعلم أن الفور لا ينقطع بآية بعد آيتها أو آيتين اتفاقاً، وينقطع بأربع اتفاقاً، واختلف في الثلاث: فقيل: ينقطع، واختاره خواهر زاده وقيل لا واختاره الحلواني [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٨٧] في الأظهر: اعلم أنه إذا دخل مع الإمام في الركعة الثانية، وقد فرغ الإمام من السجدة التلاوية التي سمعها هذا المسبوق ففيه اختلاف، وظاهر 'الهداية' يقتضي أن يسجد لها بعد الفراغ؛ لأنه لما لم يدرك ركعة التلاوة لم يصر مدركاً لها، وليست صلاتية فيقضى خارجها، وقيل: هي صلاتية، فلا تقضى خارجها.
According to the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwayah), and it is obligatory by hearing Persian if he understands it according to the relied-upon view. And there is difference in correction regarding its obligation by hearing from a sleeping person or an insane person, and it is not obligatory by hearing it from a bird, an echo. And it is performed by bowing (ruku') or prostration (sujud) in the prayer, other than the prayer's ruku' and sujud. And sujud is better. And the prayer's ruku' suffices for it if he intends it, and its sujud even if he did not intend it, provided the immediacy (fawr) is not interrupted by more than two verses. [Commentary] Meaning he intends to perform it in it. And the prostration of recitation by more than two verses. And if he hears from an imam and does not follow him, or follows in another rak'ah, he prostrates outside the prayer according to the most apparent. [Commentary] Related to the last issue. According to the apparent narration, it is said it does not invalidate, and it is attributed to Muhammad. In Ghayat al-Bayan, the most correct is no invalidation by agreement. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 485) According to the relied-upon, and this is with them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). And it is obligatory upon him according to Abu Hanifa even if he does not understand its meaning if he is informed that it is a verse of prostration. (Marqi al-Falah: 485) 'And there is difference in correction' etc.: meaning some scholars corrected one statement, and others another. For Shaykh al-Islam mentioned that it is not obligatory due to lack of validity of recitation due to loss of discernment. In al-Tatarkhaniyyah: he heard it from a sleeping person; it is said it is obligatory, and the correct is that it is not obligatory. In al-Khaniyyah: the correct is obligation. (Marqi al-Falah: 485) The echo: that which responds to you like your voice in mountains, deserts, and the like. (Marqi al-Falah: 486) 'And it is performed' etc.: if a praying person recites a verse of prostration in prayer, then bows or prostrates, the sujud al-tilawah is performed by them. 'In the prayer' this restriction applies only to ruku'; so ruku' outside it does not suffice because the effect (athar) is only reported when he bowed in it, so it is restricted to the case of the effect. But in al-Bahr, Qadi Khan chose that ruku' outside prayer substitutes for it. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 486) 'And it suffices' etc.: and this is recommended for the imam when there are many people or when reciting quietly so as not to lead to confusion. (Marqi al-Falah: 486) 'Even if he did not intend it' etc.: meaning if he did not bow until the recitation became long, it does not suffice, even if he intended it for the sujud. Similarly, the prayer's sujud does not substitute for it if the recitation becomes long, because it becomes a debt due to its obligation being immediate; and debt is paid with what is owed, not with what is not owed, and ruku' and sujud are not owed, so the debt is not fulfilled. (Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 2/195) 'If the immediacy is not interrupted': know that the immediacy is not interrupted by one or two verses after it by agreement, and is interrupted by four by agreement, and there is difference regarding three: it is said it is interrupted, chosen by Khwahar Zadeh, and it is said not, chosen by al-Halwani. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 487) 'In the most apparent': know that if he enters with the imam in the second rak'ah, and the imam has finished the sujud al-tilawah that this latecomer heard, there is difference. The apparent of al-Hidayah requires that he prostrates for it after finishing, because since he did not catch the rak'ah of recitation, he does not become a perceiver of it, and it is not a prayer prostration, so he makes it up outside. And it is said it is a prayer prostration, so it is not made up outside.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on Sujud al-Tilawah, focusing on conditions and performance. According to Zahir al-Riwayah, hearing the verse in Persian obligates sujud only if the listener understands it. There is disagreement on hearing from a sleeping or insane person: some say it is not obligatory because there is no valid recitation; the correct view is it is not obligatory. Hearing from a bird or echo does not obligate. In prayer, sujud al-tilawah can be performed by either bowing (ruku') or prostrating (sujud), but sujud is better. The prayer's ruku' suffices if one intends the sujud; the prayer's sujud suffices even without intention, provided that the immediacy (fawr) is not interrupted by more than two verses. If more than two verses pass, the sujud becomes a debt that must be performed later. The commentary explains that ruku' outside prayer does not suffice according to the apparent narration, but Qadi Khan allows it. For a latecomer (masbuq) who hears the imam recite a prostration verse but joins later, the apparent view in al-Hidayah is that he prostrates after the prayer, as he did not catch the rak'ah of recitation and it is not a prayer prostration.

Key Terms
الفور (al-fawr): Immediacy; the time within which sujud must be performed after recitation, before interruption by more than two verses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a person recites a prostration verse in prayer, then recites exactly two more verses before performing the sujud, what is the status of the fawr?
A) The fawr is broken, and the sujud must be made up later.
B) The fawr is not broken, and the sujud can still be performed immediately.
C) It is invalid to recite any verses after the sajdah verse.
D) The prayer itself becomes invalid.

Key Takeaway
Sujud al-tilawah in prayer can be performed by ruku' (with intention) or sujud (without intention), but must be done before reciting more than two verses after the sajdah verse.

Salah — Prayer
advanced
6 min
Sujud al-Tilawah for the Latecomer (Masbuq): Prostrating Outside Prayer
Ruling on Sujud al-Tilawah for the latecomer (masbuq)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine when a latecomer (masbuq) must perform sujud al-tilawah outside the prayer and explain the disagreement on whether it is considered a prayer prostration.

Core Idea
A latecomer who missed the rak'ah containing the sajdah verse prostrates outside prayer because he did not perceive the recitation in the same prayer unit.

When a person joins the congregation after the imam has recited a prostration verse and performed the sujud, the issue arises: should the latecomer perform this sujud later? The Hanafi school has a detailed ruling based on the nature of the tilawah prostration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The text describes a masbuq (latecomer) who enters the prayer in the second rak'ah, having heard the imam recite a sajdah verse in the first rak'ah. The imam already performed sujud al-tilawah in that rak'ah.
2
Apply the rule: not a prayer prostration
The apparent view in al-Hidayah is that sujud al-tilawah is not part of the prayer itself (it is not a 'prayer prostration'). Therefore, since the latecomer did not catch the rak'ah of recitation, he did not become a 'perceiver' (mudrik) of the sujud. He must make it up after the prayer ends.
The alternative view (qil) considers it a prayer prostration, so it would not be made up outside.
3
Note the ikhtilaf
There is a difference: some scholars say the masbuq should prostrate after the prayer; others say it is not necessary because the sujud is absorbed into the prayer. The text prefers the former as 'azhar' (most apparent).
4
Understand the rationale
Because sujud al-tilawah is not an integral part of the prayer structure (it is an external obligation that can be performed in prayer), the latecomer's prayer is not deficient if he misses the imam's sujud. He can fulfill it separately.

Obligation of Sujud al-Tilawah upon Hearing
Ruling on obligation of prostration upon hearing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which sujud al-tilawah becomes wajib upon hearing, and identify the relied-upon Hanafi position regarding hearing from a sleeper or insane person.

Core Idea
Sujud al-tilawah is wajib upon hearing, but only from valid recitation or understood translation.

This lesson examines when the prostration of recitation (sujud al-tilawah) becomes obligatory upon a listener. The source text from Nur al-Idah clarifies that in the authoritative narration (Zahir al-Riwayah), hearing the Arabic verse triggers the obligation, and even hearing a Persian translation obligates if understood. However, there is internal Hanafi disagreement on hearing from a sleeper or insane person, and no obligation from bird or echo. We will break down the ruling and the relied-upon view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is sujud al-tilawah upon hearing a verse of prostration. The hukm level is wajib (obligatory) in the Hanafi school based on Zahir al-Riwayah.
Recall that wajib is less than fard; the evidence is from ahad hadith.
2
Analyze the condition of language
The text states that hearing the verse in Persian (translation) obligates sujud only if the listener understands the meaning. This is the relied-upon view (al-mu'tamad). Study the phrase: 'يجب بسماع الفارسية إن فهمها' – the condition is understanding.
This shows that the obligation is tied to comprehension, not just auditory reception.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute
The text mentions ikhtilaf regarding hearing from a sleeping person or an insane person. According to the relied-upon view, such hearing does not obligate sujud because the recitation is not considered valid (the sleeper/madman lacks intention). This is the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. Abu Hanifa held that it obligates if the hearer is informed it is a verse of sajda.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the mufta bihi follows the Sahibayn.
4
Identify cases where sujud is not obligatory
The text explicitly states that hearing from a bird (i.e., a non-human mimicking) or an echo does not obligate sujud. These are not considered valid recitation.
The underlying principle: only human recitation with the potential for valid tilawah triggers the obligation.
5
Connect to the cross-madhhab difference
The Hanafi school considers sujud al-tilawah wajib, while the Shafi'i school considers it sunnah. This difference stems from different interpretations of the evidence (ahad hadith vs. general commands).
This is an example of a legitimate ikhtilaf (mukhtalaf fih).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سجود التلاوة في ظاهر الرواية، ويجب بسماع الفارسية إن فهمها على المعتمد، واختلف السجود التصحيح في وجوبها بالسماع من نائم أو مجنون ولا تجب بسماعها من الطير على السامع السجدة، والصدى
Prostration of recitation: in the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwayah), it is obligatory by hearing the Persian [translation] if he understands it according to the relied-upon [view]. And there is disagreement/verification regarding its obligation by hearing from a sleeping person or an insane person. And it is not obligatory by hearing it from a bird upon the listener. The prostration, and the echo.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on when sujud al-tilawah becomes wajib (obligatory). The relied-upon position (al-mu'tamad) is that hearing the verse in Persian obligates sujud if the listener understands the meaning. There is ikhtilaf on whether hearing it from a sleeping person or an insane person obligates sujud; some scholars say it does not because the recitation is not valid (due to lack of discernment). There is no obligation when hearing from a bird or an echo. The text references Zahir al-Riwayah as the basis.

Key Terms
سجود التلاوة (sujud al-tilawah): Prostration required upon reciting or hearing a verse of prostration (ayatu sajdah).
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The apparent/authoritative narrations from the founding imams, particularly the six books of Imam Muhammad.
المعتمد (al-mu'tamad): The relied-upon position in the madhhab, often after weighing evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Anyone who hears it, regardless of understanding.
B) Only if the listener understands the Persian translation.
C) Only if the reciter is a Muslim.
D) It is never obligatory from Persian.

Key Takeaway
Sujud al-tilawah is wajib upon hearing a valid recitation of a verse of prostration, but not from sources lacking valid human recitation.

Substituting Prayer Movements for Sujud al-Tilawah
Ruling on fulfilling the obligation of tilawah prostration through prayer's ruku' or sujud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on substituting the prayer's ruku' or sujud for sujud al-tilawah and identify the conditions for its validity.

Core Idea
Sujud al-tilawah can be fulfilled by the prayer's ruku' or sujud under conditions of intention and immediacy.

When reciting a sajda verse during prayer, a person may wonder whether the normal ruku' or sujud of the prayer can count for the tilawah prostration. This lesson clarifies the Hanafi ruling: it is permissible but with specific conditions. Understanding these conditions helps avoid unnecessary repetition or invalid prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Sujud al-tilawah is wajib upon reciting a sajda verse. Determine whether the text affirms this obligation and the two methods of performance.
The text states it is performed by bowing or prostrating.
2
Distinguish the two methods
Separate the independent performance (a specific ruku' or sujud for tilawah) from substitution using the prayer's own ruku' or sujud.
A separate sujud is considered better.
3
Analyze the condition for ruku' substitution
The prayer's ruku' suffices only if the person intends it for the tilawah (نواها). Without intention, it does not suffice.
Intention is essential for ruku' substitution.
4
Analyze the condition for sujud substitution
The prayer's sujud suffices even without intention, provided that the immediacy (fawr) of the recitation is not broken by more than two verses.
If more than two verses intervene, the obligation remains and must be fulfilled separately.
5
Note the preferred method
Performing a separate sujud specifically for tilawah is better (afḍal) than relying on substitution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتؤدّى بركوع أو سجود في الصلاة غير ركوع الصلاة وسجودها، والسجود أفضل ويجزئ عنها ركوع الصلاة إن نواها وسجودها وإن لم ينوها إذا لم ينقطع فور التلاوة بأكثر من آيتين
And it is performed by bowing or prostrating in prayer, other than the prayer's bowing and prostrating [i.e., the tilawah sujud is performed independently]. And prostration is better. And the prayer's bowing suffices for it if he intends it, and its prostration [suffices] even if he does not intend it, provided the immediacy of the recitation is not broken by more than two verses.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage explains how to perform sujud al-tilawah when one is already in prayer. The proper way is to make a separate ruku' or sujud specifically for the tilawah, and performing a separate sujud is better. However, if a person recites the verse and then continues his prayer, the ruku' of his prayer (if intended for tilawah) or the prayer's sujud (even without intention) will suffice, provided that he does not read more than two verses after the verse of sajda (which would break the immediacy). The commentary adds that this is especially useful for an imam leading a large congregation or when reciting quietly, to avoid confusion.

Key Terms
فور التلاوة (fawr al-tilawah): The immediacy/continuity after reciting the verse of sajda; if broken by more than two verses, the tilawah sujud becomes a debt that must be performed separately.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) No, because ruku' requires intention for tilawah.
C) Yes, if the prayer's sujud suffices without intention, so does ruku'.
D) No, one must always perform a separate sujud.

Key Takeaway
The prayer's ruku' suffices for sujud al-tilawah only if intended, while the prayer's sujud suffices even without intention, provided the immediacy of recitation is not broken by more than two verses.

Breaking the Fawr of Sujud al-Tilawah by Intervening Verses
Ruling on the effect of intervening verses on the immediacy of sujud al-tilawah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when sujud al-tilawah's fawr is broken by intervening verses and explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on three verses.

Core Idea
The fawr of sujud al-tilawah is only broken after four verses; three is disputed, but the mufta bihi is that three do not break it.

This lesson clarifies the concept of fawr (immediacy) in sujud al-tilawah. The issue is whether reciting additional verses after a sajda verse breaks the immediacy, requiring the sujud to be performed separately later. While one or two verses do not break it by consensus, and four do, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding three verses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the disputed ruling
Sujud al-tilawah is required instantly after reciting or hearing a sajda verse. The dispute concerns whether reciting other verses between the sajda verse and the sujud breaks this immediacy (fawr).
2
State the agreed cases
Consensus: one or two verses after the sajda verse do not break fawr; four verses do break it.
3
Present the dispute on three verses
Kharzad held that three verses break fawr; Halwani held they do not. This ikhtilaf is recorded in the text.
4
Analyze the basis of each view
Both views are based on qiyas: Kharzad compared three verses to four (significant interruption), while Halwani compared it to one or two (minor interruption).
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that three verses do not break fawr, as adopted by later Hanafi authorities and indicated by the earlier phrasing 'if not broken by more than two.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذا لم ينقطع: اعلم أن الفور لا ينقطع بآية بعد آيتها أو آيتين اتفاقاً، وينقطع بأربع اتفاقاً، واختلف في الثلاث: فقيل: ينقطع، واختاره خواهر زاده وقيل لا واختاره الحلواني
When it is not broken: Know that the immediacy is not broken by one verse after it, or by two verses, by consensus. And it is broken by four verses, by consensus. And there is disagreement regarding three verses: some say it is broken, and Kharzad chose this; others say no, and Halwani chose this.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage clarifies the ruling on the immediacy (fawr) required for sujud al-tilawah. If after reciting a verse of sajda, one recites one or two more verses, the fawr remains intact and one can still perform sujud through the prayer's ruku' or sujud. Reciting four verses definitely breaks it, requiring a separate sujud later. For three verses, there is a known intra-Hanafi dispute: Kharzad held it breaks, Halwani held it does not. The text does not explicitly side with one, but the context suggests the relied-upon view is that three verses do not break, as mentioned earlier 'if not broken by more than two'.

Key Terms
الفور (al-fawr): Immediacy; the required prompt performance of sujud al-tilawah after recitation/hearing; if delayed beyond permissible limit, it becomes qada (debt).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following statements about the fawr of sujud al-tilawah is correct?
A) One verse breaks the fawr.
B) Two verses break the fawr.
C) Four verses break the fawr by consensus.
D) Three verses never break the fawr.

Key Takeaway
The fawr of sujud al-tilawah is broken by consensus after four intervening verses; for three, the mufta bihi view is that it does not break.

Sujud al-Tilawah: Repetition in One Sitting and Following the Imam
Rulings on sujud al-tilawah: following imam and repetition in one sitting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sujud al-tilawah when a verse is repeated in one sitting and distinguish when multiple sujud are required due to a change of majlis.

Core Idea
One sujud suffices for multiple tilawah in one sitting; moving three steps breaks the sitting.

Sujud al-tilawah becomes wajib when one recites or hears a verse of sajda. But what if you recite multiple sajda verses in the same session? Do you need multiple prostrations? This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position: one sujud suffices as long as you remain in the same majlis. We also explore a related issue: if you hear the imam recite a sajda verse but join the prayer later, you perform sujud outside the prayer in the most apparent view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage covers: (1) hearing sajda from an imam but not following him, or joining in a later rak'ah; (2) reciting a sajda verse multiple times in the same or different sittings.
Focus on the second scenario for the repetition ruling.
2
Understand the principle of one sujud for multiple recitations
If you recite a sajda verse multiple times in one sitting without prostrating between them, one prostration suffices (Zahir al-Riwayah). If you already prostrated and then repeat, a new prostration is required.
The key is whether you have already prostrated before the second recitation.
3
Define change of majlis
The sitting (majlis) changes when you physically move from your place. Examples include walking three steps, moving from one branch of a tree to another, or swimming across a large river or basin.
The Hanafi definition of majlis is location-based, not time-based.
4
Apply to the examples
If you are on land, moving three steps ends the majlis. If you are climbing a tree, moving to a different branch constitutes a new majlis. Similarly, crossing a large body of water by swimming breaks the majlis.
Small movements (e.g., shifting posture) do not break it.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
There is a narration in Nawadir requiring a separate sujud for the first recitation at the end of prayer, but the mufta bihi is the Zahir al-Riwayah position that one sujud suffices.
The strength of transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah) determines the operative ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو سمع من إمام فلم يأتم به أو ائتم في ركعة أخرى سجد خارج الصلاة في الأظهر .. ومثله ما لو سمع السامع السجدة وأصلاً ولم تقض الصلاتية خارجها، ولو تلا خارج الصلاة فسجد ثم أعاد فيها سجد أخرى، وإن لم يسجد أولا كفته واحدة في ظاهر الرواية كمن كررها في مجلس واحد لا مجلسين يتبدل المجلس بالانتقال منه، ولو مسديا إلى غصن، وبالانتقال من غصن إلى غصن، وعوم في نهر أو حوض كبير في الأصح
And if he heard from an imam but did not follow him, or followed in another rak'ah, he prostrates outside the prayer in the most apparent [view]. And likewise if he hears the prostration [from someone], essentially, and the prayer's prostration is not repeated outside it. And if he recited outside prayer and prostrated, then repeated [the verse] in it, he prostrates another [time]. And if he did not prostrate first, one [prostration] suffices him in the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwayah), like one who repeats it in one sitting, not two sittings. The sitting changes by moving from it, and even if he is weaving [moving] to a branch, and by moving from branch to branch, and swimming in a river or a large basin in the most correct [view].
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage covers two issues. First: if a person hears a verse of sajda from an imam but does not follow him (e.g., is not in that prayer), or follows him in a different rak'ah (a latecomer), then in the most apparent view, he should prostrate outside the prayer. The commentary explains that if he catches the imam before the imam's sujud, he prostrates with him; if after, he does not prostrate because he did not witness the cause. Second: if a person recites a verse of sajda outside prayer and prostrates, then recites the same verse again (within prayer or outside), he must prostrate again. But if he had not prostrated for the first recitation, a single prostration suffices for multiple recitations if they are in one sitting (majlis). The definition of one sitting is based on physical location: moving from a place by walking three steps changes the sitting; this applies to land, trees, and water.

Key Terms
المجلس (al-majlis): The session or sitting during which multiple recitations occur; it is considered one as long as the person does not physically move away (by three steps or similar).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person recites a verse of sajda three times in the same sitting before prostrating, how many prostrations are required?
A) Three prostrations.
B) One prostration suffices.
C) Two prostrations.
D) None, because he delayed.

Key Takeaway
One sujud al-tilawah suffices for multiple recitations in the same sitting; changing the sitting (by moving three steps, etc.) requires a new sujud.
