Sajdat al-Tilawah: Multiple Recitations and Change of Assembly
Detailed fiqh of sajdat al-tilawah including repetition and majlis change.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on multiple recitations in one assembly and apply the definition of 'change of assembly' to determine when separate prostrations are required.

Core Idea
One sajdat al-tilawah suffices for repeated recitation in one assembly; change of assembly requires three steps or equivalent.

The obligation of sajdat al-tilawah becomes complex when the same verse is recited multiple times. This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position: one prostration covers repeated recitations within a single assembly (majlis). We also examine how the assembly is defined and what actions count as a change, based on the detailed rules in Nur al-Idah and its commentaries.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is sajdat al-tilawah (prostration of recitation). In the Hanafi school, it is wajib (between fard and sunnah). The ruling at hand is sufficiency of one prostration for multiple recitations.
The hukm level is wajib, not fard, because the dalil is zanni al-thubut (ahad hadith).
2
Distinguish the two intra-Hanafi positions
The apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) holds that one prostration suffices for multiple recitations in one assembly. A rare narration (nawadir) says he must prostrate for the first recitation after finishing the prayer.
The mufta bihi is the apparent narration from the six core books of Imam Muhammad.
3
Define 'change of assembly'
The assembly changes by departing from the place with three steps or moving to a distinct location. Mere standing, leaning, or minor movements do not change it.
The text gives examples: weaving (not changing), moving from branch to branch (changes), swimming (changes).
4
Apply the definition to various scenarios
Test scenarios: moving from one corner of a mosque to another does not change assembly; moving from a boat to land changes it; one or two steps do not change, three do.
The correct view in al-Khaniyya is that prostration is repeated if assembly changes.
5
State the mufta bihi and its authority
The relied-upon position is zahir al-riwayah: one prostration for multiple recitations in one assembly. Change of assembly requires three steps or equivalent. This is affirmed by later Hanafi authorities.
This ruling is based on ease and common practice, not on rigorous ihtiyat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة
سجود التلاوة
وإن ائتم قبل سجود إمامه لها سجد معه، فإن اقتدى به بعد سجودها في ركعتها صار للسجدة أصلاً ولم تقض الصلاتية خارجها، ولو تلا خارج الصلاة فسجد ثم أعاد فيها سجد أخرى، وإن لم يسجد أولا كفته واحدة في ظاهر الرواية كمن كررها في مجلس واحد لا مجلسين يتبدل المجلس بالانتقال منه، ولو مسديا إلى غصن، وبالانتقال من غصن إلى غصن، وعوم في نهر أو حوض كبير في الأصح، بالفتح سباحة حكماً كما إذا أدرك الإمام في ركوع ثالثة الوتر، فإنه يكون مدركاً للقنوت. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٩٢] أصلاً: أي مطلقاً لا في الصلاة ولا خارجها. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٩٢] الصلاتية: أي كل سجدة وجبت في الصلاة فلم يسجدها فيها لم تقض خارج الصلاة، وفي "البحر": قيد المصنف بكونها لا تقضى خارجها؛ لأنه لو أخرها من ركعة إلى ركعة فإنها تقضى ما دام في الصلاة؛ لأن الصلاة واحدة لكن لا يلزم جواز التأخير، بل المراد الإجزاء؛ لما في "البدائع" أنها واجبة على الفور، وأنه إذا أخرها حتى طالت القراءة تصير قضاء ويأثم. [البحر الرائق: ۱۹۲/۲] كفته واحدة أي إن لم يسجدها خارج الصلاة حتى دخل فيها فتلاها، فسجد لها أجزأته الصلاتية عن التلاوتين. [تبيين الحقائق: ٥٠٣/١] من ظاهر الرواية وفي رواية النوادر : يسجد للأولى إذا فرغ من الصلاة. [تبيين الحقائق: ٥٠٣/١] كمن الخ: أي أجزأته سجدة واحدة وهي الصلاتية كما تجزئ من كررها في مجلس واحد، ولا يجعل كمن كررها في مجلسين. [تبيين الحقائق: ٥٠٣/١] كررها إلخ أطلقه فشمل ما إذا تلا مراراً ثم سجد وما إذا تلا وسجد ثم تلا بعده مراراً في مجلس واحد. [البحر الرائق: ۱۹۸/۲] في مجلس : أطلق في المجلس فشمل ما إذا طال. (البحر الرائق) يتبدل المجلس أي لا يخلو إما أن يكون في البر أو البحر، وعلى الأول: إما أن يكون على الأرض أو ما في معناها كالسقف وغيره وإما أن يكون على الشجر، فعلى الأول: يتبدل المجلس بالانتقال منه ولا يتبدل بمجرد القيام ولو كان في حالة الإسداء بأن يذهب وبيده السدى ويلقيه على أعواد مضروبة في الحائط والأرض، وعلى الثاني: بالانتقال من غصن إلى غصن وعلى الثالث بالعوم فيه من مراقي الفلاح : ٤٩٥] بالانتقال: أطلقه، وهو مقيد بالانتقال بخطوات ثلاث، فلا يتبدل المجلس بخطوة أو خطوتين. في الأصح يرجع إلى المسائل كلها، فإنه قيل في المسألة الأولى : لا يختلف المكان بالتسدية، وفي الثانية لا يتبدل المجلس بالانتقال من غصن إلى غصن، وفي الثالثة عن محمد إذا كان طول الحوض وعرضه مثل طول المسجد وعرضه تكفيه سجدة، وفي "الخانية": الصحيح أنه يتكرر.

ولا يتبدل بزوايا البيت والمسجد ولو كبيراً، ولا بسير سفينة، ولا بركعة المجلس
وصلية
ولا بركعتين، وشربة وأكل لقمتين ومشي خطوتين ولا باتكاء، وقعود، وقيام، وركوب، ونزول في محل تلاوته، ولا بسير دابته مصلياً، ويتكرر الوجوب على السامع بتبديل مجلسه وقد اتحد مجلس التالي لا بعكسه على الأصح، وكره أن يقرأ سورة ويدع آية السجدة لا عكسه، وندب ضم آية أو أكثر إليها، وندب إخفاؤها عن غير متأهب لها، وندب القيام ثم السجود لها، ولا يرفع السامع رأسه منها قبل تاليها، ولا يؤمر التالي بالتقدم ولا السامعون بالاصطفاف فيسجدون كيف كانوا، وشرط لصحتها شرائط الصلاة إلا التحريمة وكيفيتها أن يسجد سجدة واحدة بين تكبيرتين هما سنتان بلا رفع يد ولا تشهد ولا تسليم.
ولا يتبدل إلخ أي لا يختلف المجلس بمجرد الانتقال من زاوية إلى زاوية في بيت، أو مسجد ولو كان كبيراً. ويتكرر الوجوب إلخ : مثاله : قرأ أحد آية السجدة وسمعها منه أحد، وانتقل السامع إلى مكان آخر، ثم قرأ ذلك الرجل وسمع السامع الأول منه. على الأصح أي لو تبدل مجلس السامع دون التالي تكرر الوجوب على السامع، واختلفوا في عكسه، والأصح أنه لا يتكرر على السامع؛ لأن السبب في حقه السماع، ولم يتبدل مجلسه فيه، وعلى ما صححه المصنف رحمه الله في "الكافي" من أن السبب في حقه التلاوة والسماع شرط، يتكرر الوجوب عليه. [البحر الرائق: ١٩٩/٢] لا عكسه: أي لا يكره عكسه وهو أن يقرأ آية السجدة ويدع ما سواها [تبيين الحقائق: ٥٠٥/١] وندب إخفاؤها إلخ : قال في "المحيط: إن كان التالي وحده يقرأ كيف شاء من جهر وإخفاء، وإن كان معه جماعة قال مشايخنا: إن كان القوم متهيئين للسجود ويقع في قلبه أنه لا يشق عليهم أداء السجود ينبغي أن يقرأها جهراً حتى يسجد القوم معه؛ لأن في هذا حثا لهم على الطاعة، وإن كانوا محدثين أو وقع في قلبه أنه يشق عليهم ذلك، ينبغي أن يقرأها في نفسه ولا يجهر محترزاً عن تأثيم المسلم، وذلك مندوب إليه، وإذا لم يعلم بحالهم ينبغي إخفاؤها، والراجح: الوجوب على نفسه متشاغل بعمل و لم يسمعها زجراً له : تشاغله عن كلام الله تعالى فنزل سامعاً. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٩٧] شرائط الصلاة من الطهارة من الحدث وغيرها [مراقي الفلاح ٤٩٨] تكبيرتين: تكبيرة للوضع، وتكبيرة للرفع. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٩٨]
The Book of Prayer: Prostration of Recitation. If he follows the imam before his prostration for it, he prostrates with him. If he follows him after his prostration in that rak'ah, he becomes a 'finding' of the prostration in origin, and the 'prayer-related' prostration is not made up outside it. And if he recited outside the prayer and prostrated, then repeated it inside, he prostrates another. And if he did not prostrate initially, one suffices him according to apparent narration, like one who repeats it in one assembly, not two assemblies; the assembly changes by departing from it, even if he goes to a branch, and by moving from branch to branch, and by swimming in a river or a large basin according to the most correct, with 'subaha' meaning swimming, as a ruling, like when he catches the imam in the third rak'ah's bowing of witr, then he is a 'finder' of the qunut. [Margin: origin: absolutely, not in prayer nor outside it. Prayer-related: any prostration that became obligatory in prayer and he did not perform it therein is not made up outside prayer. In 'al-Bahr': the author restricted it by not being made up outside because if he delays it from one rak'ah to another, it is made up as long as he is in prayer; because prayer is one, but delay is not permissible, rather the intended meaning is sufficiency; because in 'al-Bada'i' it is obligatory immediately, and if he delays until the recitation becomes long, it becomes qada and he sins. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 2/192] One suffices: i.e., if he did not prostrate outside prayer until he entered it and recited, then prostrated for it, his prayer-related prostration suffices for the two recitations. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 1/503] From apparent narration: and in the narration of al-Nawadir: he prostrates for the first when he finishes prayer. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 1/503] Like one...: i.e., one prostration suffices him, which is the prayer-related one, just as it suffices for one who repeats it in one assembly, and it is not like one who repeats it in two assemblies. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 1/503] 'He repeated it etc.' he made it absolute, so it includes when he recites repeatedly then prostrates, and when he recites and prostrates then recites repeatedly afterward in one assembly. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 2/198] 'In an assembly': he made it absolute regarding the assembly, so it includes even if it was lengthy. (al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) 'The assembly changes': i.e., it is either on land or sea; on the first: either on the ground or what is like it such as a roof etc., or on a tree; on the first: the assembly changes by departing from it, and does not change by merely standing even if it is in the state of weaving where he goes with the warp in his hand and throws it on sticks placed in the wall and ground; on the second: by moving from branch to branch; on the third: by swimming in it. [Maraqi al-Falah: 495] 'By departing': he made it absolute, but it is restricted to departure with three steps, so it does not change with one or two steps. In the most correct, it refers to all the issues; for it is said in the first issue: the place does not differ with weaving; in the second: the assembly does not change by moving from branch to branch; in the third, from Muhammad: if the length and width of the basin are like the length and width of the mosque, one prostration suffices; and in 'al-Khaniyya': the correct is that it is repeated. And it does not change by corners of the house and mosque, even if large, nor by the movement of a ship, nor by one rak'ah, nor by two rak'ahs, nor by a drink, nor by eating two mouthfuls, nor by walking two steps, nor by leaning, nor by sitting, nor by standing, nor by riding, nor by dismounting in his recitation place, nor by the movement of his mount while praying. And the obligation is repeated upon the listener by changing his assembly while the reciter's assembly remains one, not the opposite according to the most correct. And it is disliked that he recite a surah and leave out the verse of prostration, not the opposite. And it is recommended to add one or more verses to it. And it is recommended to conceal it from those not prepared for it. And it is recommended to stand then prostrate for it. And the listener should not raise his head from it before the reciter. And the reciter is not commanded to go forward, nor the listeners to line up; they prostrate as they are. And the conditions for its validity are the conditions of prayer except for the opening takbir. And its manner is that he prostrates one prostration between two takbirs, both of which are sunnah, without raising hands, without tashahhud, and without taslim. [Commentary continues on the same rulings.]
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage is an expansive treatment of sajdat al-tilawah (prostration of recitation) from Nur al-Idah with interwoven commentary from later sources. The author begins with the ruling on a person who follows an imam who has already performed the prostration: if he catches the imam after the prostration in the same rak'ah, he is considered to have 'found' the prostration in its full sense, meaning he does not need to make it up later. This is analogous to catching the imam in the third rak'ah of witr, where one is considered to have found the qunut. The text then addresses a scenario where a person recites outside prayer, prostrates, then recites the same verse again inside the prayer: if he prostrates again, two prostrations are required; if he did not prostrate initially, one suffices according to the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah). This is compared to repeating the recitation multiple times in a single assembly (majlis), where one prostration suffices. The commentary clarifies that 'apparent narration' is from the six core books of Imam Muhammad; a rare narration (nawadir) holds that he must prostrate for the first after finishing the prayer. The definition of 'change of assembly' is then taken up in detail. The assembly changes by departing from the place, but not by merely standing or with minor movements. For a person weaving cloth, the assembly changes if he goes to a different spot; for a person on a tree, moving from branch to branch changes the assembly; for swimming in a river or large basin, swimming changes it. The correct view is that moving three steps constitutes a change; one or two steps do not. The commentary then addresses specific cases: for weaving, the place does not change; for tree branches, moving from branch to branch does not change the assembly (some say); for a basin, if it is as large as a mosque, one prostration suffices (from Imam Muhammad), but the correct view in al-Khaniyya is that prostration is repeated. The passage then lists what does NOT change the assembly: moving within corners of a house or mosque, even a large one; movement of a ship; one or two rak'ahs; drinking; eating two mouthfuls; walking two steps; leaning; sitting; standing; riding; dismounting at the same recitation spot; or moving while riding an animal while praying. The obligation of prostration is repeated upon the listener if his assembly changes while the reciter's assembly remains the same, but not vice versa. The text then covers recommended and disliked acts: it is disliked to skip the verse of prostration while reciting other verses; it is recommended to include it; it is recommended to recite it quietly if listeners are not ready for prostration, or loudly if they are; standing before prostrating is recommended. The listener should not raise his head before the reciter. There is no command for the reciter to move forward or for listeners to line up; they prostrate where they are. Finally, the conditions for validity are those of prayer (e.g., purity) except for the opening takbir. The manner is one prostration between two takbirs (both sunnah), without raising hands, tashahhud, or taslim.

Key Terms
سجود التلاوة (sajdat al-tilawah): A prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of the Quran that requires prostration.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The apparent/well-known narrations from the founding imams, especially the six books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.
المجلس (al-majlis): The place/assembly where one is sitting or standing; its change affects the obligation of prostration for repeated recitation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi Hanafi position, what constitutes a change of assembly for sajdat al-tilawah?
A) Any physical movement
B) Moving three steps or more
C) Moving to a different room
D) Both B and C

Key Takeaway
One sajdat al-tilawah suffices for multiple recitations in the same assembly; assembly changes only with significant relocation (three steps or equivalent).

Salah — Prayer

The Manner and Conditions of Sajdat al-Tilawah
Rulings on disciples and mustahabbat of sajdat al-tilawah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the disliked and recommended acts regarding sajdat al-tilawah, and apply the conditions and manner for its validity.

Core Idea
Sajdat al-tilawah is wajib, performed as one prostration between two takbirs, with conditions like salah but no takbir tahrimah.

This lesson covers the detailed rulings on sajdat al-tilawah beyond the basic obligation. It addresses what is disliked (makruh) and recommended (mandub) when reciting the prostration verse, and the precise conditions (shurut) and manner (kayfiyyah) for performing this act. The text provides guidance on concealing the verse, standing before prostration, and the etiquette for the listener.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts that are disliked and recommended in relation to reciting the prostration verse
Read the passage and note that it is disliked to recite a surah and skip the verse of prostration, but the opposite (reciting only the verse) is not disliked. It is recommended to add one or more verses to the prostration verse and to conceal it from those unprepared.
The distinction between what is makruh and what is mandub is based on the text's explicit wording.
2
Understand the conditions for validity of sajdat al-tilawah
The text states that the conditions are the same as for salah: purity from hadath and najasah, covering the awrah, facing the qiblah, avoiding nullifiers. The exception is that the opening takbir (tahrimah) is not required.
This makes sajdat al-tilawah a simplified act compared to the full prayer.
3
Learn the manner of performing it
The manner is to perform one prostration between two takbirs – one for placing (takbir al-wad') and one for raising (takbir al-raf'). There is no raising of the hands, no tashahhud, and no taslim. Standing before prostrating is recommended.
The two takbirs are sunnah, not fard.
4
Examine additional sunan and etiquette
The listener should not raise his head from the prostration before the reciter. The reciter is not required to step forward, nor the listeners to line up; they prostrate as they are. It is also discussed whether to recite aloud or quietly based on the audience's preparedness.
The commentary adds that if the audience is unprepared, it is recommended to recite quietly to avoid causing them difficulty.

[البحر الرائق: ١٩٩/٢] لا عكسه: أي لا يكره عكسه وهو أن يقرأ آية السجدة ويدع ما سواها [تبيين الحقائق: ٥٠٥/١] وندب إخفاؤها إلخ : قال في "المحيط: إن كان التالي وحده يقرأ كيف شاء من جهر وإخفاء، وإن كان معه جماعة قال مشايخنا: إن كان القوم متهيئين للسجود ويقع في قلبه أنه لا يشق عليهم أداء السجود ينبغي أن يقرأها جهراً حتى يسجد القوم معه؛ لأن في هذا حثا لهم على الطاعة، وإن كانوا محدثين أو وقع في قلبه أنه يشق عليهم ذلك، ينبغي أن يقرأها في ولا يجهر محترزاً عن تأثيم المسلم، وذلك مندوب إليه ، وإذا لم يعلم بحالهم ينبغي إخفاؤها، والراجح: الوجوب على

Prostration of recitation. It does not change by [moving to] corners of the house and the mosque, even if large, nor by moving a ship, nor by a rak'ah, nor by two rak'ahs, nor by a drink and eating two mouthfuls and walking two steps, nor by leaning, sitting, standing, riding, and dismounting in the place of his recitation, nor by the movement of his animal while praying. And the obligation repeats for the listener by changing his gathering while the reciter's gathering remains the same, but not vice versa according to the most correct view. It is disliked to recite a surah and leave out the verse of prostration, not the opposite. It is recommended to add one or more verses to it. It is recommended to conceal it from those not prepared for it. It is recommended to stand then prostrate for it. The listener should not raise his head from it before the reciter. The reciter is not commanded to go forward, nor the listeners to line up; they prostrate as they are. The conditions for its validity are the conditions of prayer except the takbir al-tahrimah. Its manner is to perform one prostration between two takbirs, both of which are sunnah, without raising the hands, tashahhud, or salutation. 'It does not change' etc., meaning the gathering does not differ merely by moving from one corner to another in a house or mosque, even if large. 'And the obligation repeats' etc.: Example: someone recited a verse of prostration and another heard it, then the listener moved to another place, then that man recited again and the first listener heard him. According to the most correct view, if the listener's gathering changes without the reciter's, the obligation repeats for the listener. They differed about the opposite; the most correct is that it does not repeat for the listener, because the cause for him is hearing, and his gathering did not change. According to what the author in 'al-Kafi' corrected, that the cause for him is recitation and hearing is a condition, the obligation repeats upon him. [al-Bahr al-Raiq 2/199] 'Not the opposite': i.e., the opposite is not disliked, which is to recite the verse of prostration and leave out the rest. [Tabyin al-Haqaiq 1/505] 'And it is recommended to conceal it' etc.: He said in 'al-Muhit': If the reciter is alone, he recites however he wishes, aloud or quietly. If he is with a group, our scholars said: If the people are prepared for prostration and he does not think it will be burdensome for them to perform the prostration, he should recite it aloud so that they prostrate with him, because this encourages them to obedience. If they are in a state of ritual impurity or he thinks it will be burdensome for them, he should recite it quietly, avoiding causing them sin, and that is recommended. If he does not know their state, he should conceal it. The preponderant view: obligation upon a person busy with work and did not hear it, as a deterrent for his preoccupation with the words of Allah, so he is considered a listener. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 497] 'Conditions of prayer' from purity from hadath and others. [Maraqi al-Falah: 498] 'Two takbirs': one for placing, one for raising. [Maraqi al-Falah: 498]
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the prostration of recitation (sajdat al-tilawah). It begins by stating that moving within a house or mosque does not count as changing the gathering (majlis) for the purpose of repeating the obligation. It lists actions that do not break the gathering: moving from corner to corner, moving a ship, performing one or two rak'ahs, drinking, eating two mouthfuls, walking two steps, leaning, sitting, standing, riding, dismounting in the recitation spot, or moving one's animal while praying. Then it addresses the repetition of obligation for the listener: if the listener changes his gathering while the reciter remains in the same place, the obligation repeats; if the opposite (reciter changes but listener does not), it does not repeat according to the most correct view. The commentary gives an example: a reciter recites a verse of prostration, a listener hears it, then the listener moves to another place, then the same reciter recites again and the listener hears again—the obligation repeats because the listener's gathering changed. The text then states that it is disliked to recite a surah and skip the verse of prostration, but not vice versa. It is recommended to add another verse or more to the verse of prostration. It is recommended to conceal the verse from those not prepared to prostrate (e.g., in a state of impurity). It is recommended to stand before prostrating. The listener should not raise his head before the reciter finishes. The reciter is not ordered to go forward, nor the listeners to line up; they prostrate wherever they are. The conditions for validity are the same as for salah (purity, facing qiblah, covering awrah) except for the opening takbir (tahrimah). The manner is one prostration between two takbirs, both of which are sunnah; there is no raising of hands, no tashahhud, and no taslim. The commentary elaborates that the takbirs are one for going down and one for coming up. It also discusses the recommendation to recite aloud or quietly based on the audience, and notes that a person busy with work who does not hear the verse is still obligated to prostrate as a deterrent.

Key Terms
سجود التلاوة (sujūd al-tilāwah): Prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of prostration in the Quran.
آية السجدة (āyat al-sajdah): A verse of prostration; there are 14 in the Quran according to the Hanafi school.
التحريمة (al-taḥrīmah): The opening takbir of prayer that renders prohibited (haram) what was permissible.
الوضع (al-wad‘): The act of placing; here refers to the takbir for going down into prostration.
الرفع (al-raf‘): The act of raising; here refers to the takbir for rising from prostration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Purity from hadath
B) Facing the qiblah
C) Performing the opening takbir (tahrimah)
D) Covering the awrah

Key Takeaway
Sajdat al-tilawah is a simplified wajib act: one prostration between two sunnah takbirs, with conditions like salah except no takbir tahrimah, and with sunan that include concealing the verse from those unprepared and standing before prostrating.

Changing the Gathering and Repetition of Obligation for Sajdat al-Tilawah
Rulings on the effect of changing the gathering on wajib of sajdat al-tilawah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify what actions do/do not change the gathering (majlis) for sajdat al-tilawah, and apply the ruling on when the obligation repeats for the listener and reciter.

Core Idea
The obligation of sajdat al-tilawah repeats for the listener only if he changes his gathering; changing the reciter's gathering alone does not repeat it.

This lesson focuses on the concept of the 'gathering' (majlis) and its effect on the obligation of sajdat al-tilawah. The text lists various actions that do not constitute a change of gathering, and then discusses the critical difference of opinion regarding repetition of wujub when the reciter or listener changes their gathering. Understanding this is crucial for knowing when multiple prostrations become wajib upon hearing the same verse multiple times.

Guided Path
1
Understand the concept of majlis in this context
The 'gathering' (majlis) refers to the place where one is present when hearing or reciting the prostration verse. Moving within certain boundaries does not constitute a change of gathering.
The text gives examples of what does not change the gathering: moving from corner to corner in a house or mosque, moving a ship, performing a rak'ah, etc.
2
List the actions that do not change the gathering
The text enumerates actions that do not break the gathering: moving from corner to corner in a house/mosque, moving a ship, performing one or two rak'ahs, drinking, eating two mouthfuls, walking two steps, leaning, sitting, standing, riding, dismounting in the recitation spot, moving one's animal while praying.
These are all examples of minor movements that do not constitute a change of place that would count as a new gathering.
3
Learn the rule for repetition for the listener
The obligation repeats for the listener if his gathering changes while the reciter remains in the same place. An example is given: a reciter recites, a listener hears and moves to another location, then the same reciter recites again; the obligation repeats for the listener.
The cause (sabab) for the listener is hearing, and changing his gathering constitutes a new cause.
4
Explore the intra-Hanafi dispute about the opposite scenario
If the reciter changes his gathering but the listener does not, there is a difference of opinion. The most correct view (al-asahh) is that the obligation does not repeat for the listener because his hearing cause has not changed. However, the author of al-Kafi held that the cause for the listener is the recitation itself, with hearing as a condition, so the obligation repeats if the reciter's gathering changes.
The commentary from al-Bahr al-Raiq supports the first view. This dispute is within the Hanafi school.

Source Text

ولا يتبدل إلخ أي لا يختلف المجلس بمجرد الانتقال من زاوية إلى زاوية في بيت، أو مسجد ولو كان كبيراً. ويتكرر الوجوب إلخ : مثاله : قرأ أحد آية السجدة وسمعها منه أحد، وانتقل السامع إلى مكان آخر، ثم قرأ ذلك الرجل وسمع السامع الأول منه. على الأصح أي لو تبدل مجلس السامع دون التالي تكرر الوجوب على السامع، واختلفوا في عكسه، والأصح أنه لا يتكرر على السامع؛ لأن السبب في حقه السماع، ولم يتبدل مجلسه فيه، وعلى ما صححه المصنف الله في "الكافي" من أن السبب في حقه التلاوة والسماع شرط، يتكرر الوجوب عليه. [البحر الرائق: ١٩٩/٢] لا عكسه: أي لا يكره عكسه وهو أن يقرأ آية السجدة ويدع ما سواها [تبيين الحقائق: ٥٠٥/١] وندب إخفاؤها إلخ : قال في "المحيط: إن كان التالي وحده يقرأ كيف شاء من جهر وإخفاء، وإن كان معه جماعة قال مشايخنا: إن كان القوم متهيئين للسجود ويقع في قلبه أنه لا يشق عليهم أداء السجود ينبغي أن يقرأها جهراً حتى يسجد القوم معه؛ لأن في هذا حثا لهم على الطاعة، وإن كانوا محدثين أو وقع في قلبه أنه يشق عليهم ذلك، ينبغي أن يقرأها في ولا يجهر محترزاً عن تأثيم المسلم، وذلك مندوب إليه ، وإذا لم يعلم بحالهم ينبغي إخفاؤها، والراجح: الوجوب على
نفسه
متشاغل بعمل و لم يسمعها زجراً له : تشاغله عن كلام الله تعالى فنزل سامعاً. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٩٧] شرائط الصلاة من الطهارة من الحدث وغيرها [مراقي الفلاح ٤٩٨] تكبيرتين: تكبيرة للوضع، وتكبيرة للرفع. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٩٨]
Prostration of recitation. It does not change by [moving to] corners of the house and the mosque, even if large, nor by moving a ship, nor by a rak'ah, nor by two rak'ahs, nor by a drink and eating two mouthfuls and walking two steps, nor by leaning, sitting, standing, riding, and dismounting in the place of his recitation, nor by the movement of his animal while praying. And the obligation repeats for the listener by changing his gathering while the reciter's gathering remains the same, but not vice versa according to the most correct view. It is disliked to recite a surah and leave out the verse of prostration, not the opposite. It is recommended to add one or more verses to it. It is recommended to conceal it from those not prepared for it. It is recommended to stand then prostrate for it. The listener should not raise his head from it before the reciter. The reciter is not commanded to go forward, nor the listeners to line up; they prostrate as they are. The conditions for its validity are the conditions of prayer except the takbir al-tahrimah. Its manner is to perform one prostration between two takbirs, both of which are sunnah, without raising the hands, tashahhud, or salutation. 'It does not change' etc., meaning the gathering does not differ merely by moving from one corner to another in a house or mosque, even if large. 'And the obligation repeats' etc.: Example: someone recited a verse of prostration and another heard it, then the listener moved to another place, then that man recited again and the first listener heard him. According to the most correct view, if the listener's gathering changes without the reciter's, the obligation repeats for the listener. They differed about the opposite; the most correct is that it does not repeat for the listener, because the cause for him is hearing, and his gathering did not change. According to what the author in 'al-Kafi' corrected, that the cause for him is recitation and hearing is a condition, the obligation repeats upon him. [al-Bahr al-Raiq 2/199] 'Not the opposite': i.e., the opposite is not disliked, which is to recite the verse of prostration and leave out the rest. [Tabyin al-Haqaiq 1/505] 'And it is recommended to conceal it' etc.: He said in 'al-Muhit': If the reciter is alone, he recites however he wishes, aloud or quietly. If he is with a group, our scholars said: If the people are prepared for prostration and he does not think it will be burdensome for them to perform the prostration, he should recite it aloud so that they prostrate with him, because this encourages them to obedience. If they are in a state of ritual impurity or he thinks it will be burdensome for them, he should recite it quietly, avoiding causing them sin, and that is recommended. If he does not know their state, he should conceal it. The preponderant view: obligation upon a person busy with work and did not hear it, as a deterrent for his preoccupation with the words of Allah, so he is considered a listener. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 497] 'Conditions of prayer' from purity from hadath and others. [Maraqi al-Falah: 498] 'Two takbirs': one for placing, one for raising. [Maraqi al-Falah: 498]
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the prostration of recitation (sajdat al-tilawah). It begins by stating that moving within a house or mosque does not count as changing the gathering (majlis) for the purpose of repeating the obligation. It lists actions that do not break the gathering: moving from corner to corner, moving a ship, performing one or two rak'ahs, drinking, eating two mouthfuls, walking two steps, leaning, sitting, standing, riding, dismounting in the recitation spot, or moving one's animal while praying. Then it addresses the repetition of obligation for the listener: if the listener changes his gathering while the reciter remains in the same place, the obligation repeats; if the opposite (reciter changes but listener does not), it does not repeat according to the most correct view. The commentary gives an example: a reciter recites a verse of prostration, a listener hears it, then the listener moves to another place, then the same reciter recites again and the listener hears again—the obligation repeats because the listener's gathering changed. The text then states that it is disliked to recite a surah and skip the verse of prostration, but not vice versa. It is recommended to add another verse or more to the verse of prostration. It is recommended to conceal the verse from those not prepared to prostrate (e.g., in a state of impurity). It is recommended to stand before prostrating. The listener should not raise his head before the reciter finishes. The reciter is not ordered to go forward, nor the listeners to line up; they prostrate wherever they are. The conditions for validity are the same as for salah (purity, facing qiblah, covering awrah) except for the opening takbir (tahrimah). The manner is one prostration between two takbirs, both of which are sunnah; there is no raising of hands, no tashahhud, and no taslim. The commentary elaborates that the takbirs are one for going down and one for coming up. It also discusses the recommendation to recite aloud or quietly based on the audience, and notes that a person busy with work who does not hear the verse is still obligated to prostrate as a deterrent.

Key Terms
المجلس (al-majlis): The place or gathering where one is present when hearing or reciting the prostration verse.
السبب (al-sabab): The cause or occasion that triggers the legal obligation; the text discusses whether the sabab for the listener is hearing or the recitation itself.
التبدل (al-tabaddul): Change or alteration; in this context, change of the gathering (majlis).
الأصح (al-aṣaḥḥ): The most correct view; used to indicate the preferred position in a dispute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the most correct view in the passage, when does the obligation of sajdat al-tilawah repeat for the listener?
A) When the reciter changes his gathering
B) When the listener changes his gathering while the reciter remains
C) When both the reciter and listener change their gatherings
D) When the reciter recites the verse again in the same gathering

Key Takeaway
The obligation of sajdat al-tilawah repeats for the listener only when his own gathering changes; the reciter's change of gathering does not affect the listener's obligation according to the most correct Hanafi view.

The Dispute on Sajdat al-Shukr: Makruh or Mustahabb?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the ruling of sajdat al-shukr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on sajdat al-shukr, analyze the evidence for each, and apply the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Sajdat al-shukr is mustahabb per the fatwa, but Imam Abu Hanifa disliked it—a dispute resolved by later tarjih.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the prostration of thanks. Imam Abu Hanifa considered it makruh, while his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, held it to be a desirable act of worship. Understanding the evidence of each and how the later scholars settled on the operative ruling (fatwa) is essential for correct practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Carefully read the opening sentence. State the ruling according to Imam Abu Hanifa and according to the Sahibayn. Note the term 'qurbah' used by the Sahibayn.
The ruling is makruh (Imam) vs mustahabb (Sahibayn). The Sahibayn call it a qurbah (meritorious act).
2
Analyze Imam Abu Hanifa's rationale
Read the interpretation of Imam's view: he did not negate its legitimacy as worship, but rather denied its obligation. His reasoning: thanks cannot be fully given; complete thanks is in two rak'ats (as the Prophet did at the Conquest of Mecca).
The Imam's view is that it is not obligatory, and because of potential overuse, it becomes disliked.
3
Examine the Sahibayn's evidence
The Sahibayn rely on the hadith of Abu Bakr that the Prophet would prostrate upon receiving good news. This hadith is narrated by six except al-Nasa'i.
This dalil is a hadith (khabar) that indicates desirability.
4
Understand the tarjih (preponderance)
The passage states that the fatwa is on the Sahibayn's view. Later works like al-Durr al-Mukhtar and Ibn Amir Haj confirm this because 'many hadiths' support it.
The tarjih mechanism: abundance of textual evidence overrides the Imām's caution.
5
Note the practical exception
The passage adds that sajdat al-shukr is disliked after the obligatory prayer to prevent ignorant people from treating it as sunnah or wajib.
This exception balances the ruling to avoid harm (sadd al-dhari'ah).

الله تعالى
عند الإمام: قيل: إنه لم يرد به نفي شرعيتها قربة، بل أراد نفي وجوبها شكراً؛ لعدم إحصاء نعم فتكون مباحة أو لا يراها شكراً تاماً وتمام الشكر في صلاة ركعتين كما فعل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يوم فتح مكة.
مراقي الفلاح: ٤٩٩] وقالا إلخ أي محمد وأبو يوسف في إحدى الروايتين عنه. [مراقي الفلاح: ٥٠٠] يثاب عليها: لما روى الستة إلا النسائي عن أبي بكر أن النبي كان إذا أتاه أمر يسره أو بشر به خر ساجدا. مراقي الفلاح: ٥٠٠]، والفتوى على ما قالاه وفي "الدر" وبه يفتى، وفي ابن أمير حاج": وهو الظاهر، وكيف لا وقد جاء فيها غير ما حديث، وفي "الدر" وسجدة الشكر ،مستحبة به يفتى، لكنها تكره بعد الصلاة؛ لأن الجهلة يعتقدون أنها سنة أو واجبة وكل مباح يؤدي إليه فهو مكروه. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥٠٠]
Prostration of thanks. Chapter on the prostration of thanks. The prostration of thanks is disliked according to Imam [Abu Hanifa]; he is not rewarded for it, and it is better to leave it. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It is an act of worship for which one is rewarded. Its manner is like the prostration of recitation. And on it is the fatwa. Important benefit to repel every important difficulty: Imam al-Nasafi said in al-Kafi: Whoever recites all the verses of prostration in one gathering and prostrates for each, Allah will suffice him from what concerns him. According to Imam: it is said that he did not intend to negate its legitimacy as an act of worship, but rather he intended to negate its obligation as thanks, because blessings cannot be counted, so it is permissible, or he does not consider it complete thanks; complete thanks is in praying two rak'ahs as the Messenger of Allah did on the day of the conquest of Mecca. [Maraqi al-Falah: 499] 'And the two said' etc., i.e., Muhammad and Abu Yusuf in one of two narrations from him. [Maraqi al-Falah: 500] 'They are rewarded for it': because the six [hadith collectors] except al-Nasa'i narrated from Abu Bakr that the Prophet, when a matter pleased him came to him or he was given glad tidings, he would fall down in prostration. [Maraqi al-Falah: 500] And the fatwa is on what they said, and in al-Durr: with it fatwa is given, and in Ibn Amir Haj: and it is apparent, and how not, when many hadiths have come regarding it. And in al-Durr: Sajdat al-Shukr is mustahabb, with it fatwa is given, but it is disliked after prayer because the ignorant think it is sunnah or wajib, and every permissible act that leads to that is disliked. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 500]
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the prostration of thanks (sajdat al-shukr). It begins by stating the positions: Imam Abu Hanifa considers it makruh (disliked) and holds that one is not rewarded for it and it is better to omit it. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) consider it a desirable act of worship (qurbah) for which one receives reward. Its manner is the same as sajdat al-tilawah (one prostration without tashahhud or taslim). The commentary explains that the fatwa (operative ruling) is on the view of the Sahibayn. It then quotes a benefit from Imam al-Nasafi's al-Kafi: reciting all verses of prostration in one gathering and prostrating for each suffices one from his concerns. The commentary further interprets Imam Abu Hanifa's position: he did not deny its legitimacy as a form of worship, but rather denied its obligation as an expression of thanks, because one cannot fully count Allah's blessings—thus it is either simply permissible (mubah) or not considered complete thanks; complete thanks is in praying two rak'ahs, as the Prophet did at the conquest of Mecca. The Sahibayn's evidence is the hadith narrated by Abu Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him) that the Prophet would prostrate upon receiving good news. The fatwa is on the Sahibayn's view, as stated in al-Durr al-Mukhtar and other later works. However, it is disliked after the obligatory prayer because ignorant people may believe it is sunnah or wajib, and any permissible act that leads to such misconception becomes disliked.

Key Terms
سجدة الشكر (sajdat al-shukr): Prostration performed to express gratitude to Allah upon receiving a blessing or good news.
قربة (qurbah): An act that brings one closer to Allah; a meritorious act of worship.
الفتوى (al-fatwā): The operative legal ruling that is given in answer to questions; the relied-upon position.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon (fatwa) position regarding sajdat al-shukr according to this passage?
A) It is makruh and should be left
B) It is obligatory (wajib)
C) It is mustahabb (desirable) and rewarded
D) It is haram

Key Takeaway
Sajdat al-shukr is mustahabb per the Hanafi fatwa, but it is disliked after the obligatory prayer to prevent misconception among the common people.

Six Conditions for Validity of Friday Prayer
List of six conditions with brief commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six conditions for the validity of Friday prayer in the Hanafi school and identify which condition, if missing, invalidates the prayer.

Core Idea
Six conditions must be met for Friday prayer to be valid; missing any one invalidates it.

The Friday prayer is a distinct obligation with unique requirements beyond the general conditions of prayer. This passage from Nur al-Idah enumerates the six conditions that must be present for the Friday prayer to be valid. Understanding these conditions is essential for correctly performing and leading the Friday congregation.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the six conditions
Commit to memory the list: city/outskirts, ruler/deputy, Zuhr time, khutbah before prayer with intention, at least one qualified hearer, general permission.
Use the acronym C-R-T-K-A-P as a mnemonic.
2
Understand each condition's rationale
For each condition, ask: why is it required? What happens if it is missing?
E.g., the city condition ensures Friday is a public urban congregation.
3
Identify Hanafi-specific definitions
Learn what counts as a city (misr), what qualifies as its outskirts (fina'), who is the ruler (sultan), and what is general permission (idhn 'aam).
Fina': area where one who leaves with intention of travel becomes a traveler.
4
Note the consequence of absence
Any missing condition renders the Friday prayer invalid (batil). No compensation; the act must be repeated as Zuhr.
This is unlike wajibat where compensation (sajdah al-sahw) may suffice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويشترط لصحتها ستة أشياء: المصر أو فناؤه، والسلطان فلا تجب على مقطوعهما أي لصحة صلاة الجمعة أو نائبه، ووقت الظهر فلا تصح قبله وتبطل بخروجه والخطبة قبلها بقصدها في وقتها، وحضور أحد لسماعها ممن تنعقد بهم الجمعة، ولو واحدا في الصحيح، والإذن العام .
And for its validity six things are required: the city or its outskirts, and the ruler so it is not obligatory upon the one with severed legs? or his deputy, and the time of Zuhr - it is not valid before it and becomes invalid with its exit, and the sermon before it with the intention in its time, and the presence of one to hear it from those with whom Friday is valid, even one according to the correct view, and general permission.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage lists the six conditions for the validity of Friday prayer. The first condition is that it must be held in a city (misr) or its outskirts (fina'). The second condition is the presence of the ruler (sultan) or his deputy, meaning the one authorized to lead the prayer. The third condition is that it must be performed within the time of Zuhr; performing before Zuhr time is invalid, and if the time passes, the prayer becomes invalid even if one had sat for the tashahhud. The fourth condition is that the sermon (khutbah) must be delivered before the prayer, with the intention of it being part of the Friday service. The fifth condition is the presence of at least one person who is qualified to perform Friday prayer (i.e., free, adult, male, resident) to hear the sermon; according to the correct view, even one person suffices. The sixth condition is general permission (idhn 'aam) for the public to attend; if the ruler closes the doors, the prayer is not valid unless the people are allowed in.

Key Terms
فناؤه (fina'uh): The outskirts or suburban area attached to the city, considered part of the city for the validity of Friday prayer.
الإذن العام (al-idhn al-'aam): General permission for all people to attend; the prayer is invalid if the ruler restricts access to a select few.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens if the time of Zuhr exits while a person is performing Friday prayer?
A) The prayer becomes qada'
B) The prayer becomes invalid even if one had sat for tashahhud
C) The prayer remains valid and is completed
D) The prayer is converted to Zuhr

Key Takeaway
Friday prayer is invalid if any of the six conditions (city, ruler, time, khutbah, audience, permission) is missing; each condition has a specific rationale in the Hanafi school.

The Six Conditions for Valid Friday Prayer (Jumu'ah)
States six conditions for Jumu'ah validity with commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six conditions for the validity of Friday prayer and distinguish between conditions of obligation and conditions of validity.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah requires six specific conditions for validity; missing any one invalidates the prayer.

Friday prayer is a unique communal obligation with strict conditions. In this lesson, we analyze the six conditions for its validity as laid out in Nur al-Idah, along with their implications. Understanding these conditions ensures that your Jumu'ah is performed correctly and accepted by Allah.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish obligation from validity
The text first mentions conditions for obligation (health, safety, sound eyes and legs) then lists six for validity. These are separate sets; you must identify which conditions affect whether the prayer is required of you and which affect whether the prayer is valid.
2
List the six validity conditions
From the text, enumerate: (1) being in a misr or its outskirts, (2) presence of sultan or his deputy, (3) time of Zuhr, (4) khutbah before prayer with intention, (5) presence of at least one listener from those for whom Jumu'ah is valid, (6) general public permission.
3
Understand each condition's details
Read the commentary to clarify what 'misr' entails, what happens if time exits, who qualifies as a listener, and the implication of 'general permission'. Note the exception: a deaf or sleeping person still counts as a listener.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The text mentions a narration from Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn that Jumu'ah is valid even if no one attends, but the relied-upon position (al-sahih) requires at least one. Understand why the tarjih settles on the latter.
5
Apply to practical scenarios
Use the conditions to evaluate real situations: e.g., a prayer in a small town without a ruler, or an imam locking the door. Determine validity based on the six conditions.

وصلية
فيما هو إلخ أي الإقامة في محل هو داخل في حد الإقامة بالمصر، وهو المكان الذي من فارقه بنية السفر يصير مسافراً، ومن وصل إليه يصير مقيماً، كربض المصر وفنائه الذي لم ينفصل عنه بغلوة، ولا يجب على من كان خارجه، ولو سمع النداء من المصر، سواء كان سواده قريباً من المصر أو بعيداً على الأصح، فلا عليك من غيره، وإن ذكر تصحيحه فمنه ما في "البدائع" أنه إن مكن أن يحضر الجمعة من غير تكلف يجب عليه إلخ. [حاشية الطحطاوي، مراقي الفلاح: ٥٠٤]
ويبيت
بأهله
مخالفة
من ظالم فلا يجب على من لم يأمن الظالم إذا خرج لصلاة الجمعة أو فناؤه : سواء كان مصلى العيد أو غيره. مراقي الفلاح: ٥٠٦] والسلطان: أي والثاني من شروط الصحة: أن يصلي بهم السلطان إماماً فيها أو نائبه، يعني من أمره بإقامة الجمعة [مراقي الفلاح ٥٠٧] وفي مفتاح السعادة" عن "مجمع الفتاوى": غلب على المسلمين ولاة الكفار يجوز للمسلمين إقامة الجمع والأعياد ويصير القاضي قاضياً بتراضي المسلمين، ويجب عليهم أن يلتمسوا واليا .مسلماً [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥٠٧]
وتبطل بخروجه أي تبطل صلاة الجمعة بخروج وقت الظهر ولو بعد القعود قدر التشهد، فلا يبنى الظهر لاختلاف الصلاتين قدراً وحالاً واسماً، أطلقه فشمل كل مصل البحر الرائق: ۲۲۸/۲] بقصدها: حتى لو عطس الخطيب فحمد العطاسه لا ينوب عن الخطبة مراقي الفلاح ۵۰۹] في وقتها : فلو خطب قبله وصلى فيه لا تصح؛ لأنه من جملة الخصوصيات المقيدة بها. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥۰۹ وحضور أحد إلخ أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان الحاضر أصم أو نائماً أو بعيداً، وأفاد بقوله: "ممن تنعقد إلخ" أنه يكفي حضور مريض أو عبد أو مسافر ولو كان جنباً، فإذا حضر غيره أو تطهر بعد الخطبة تصح الجمعة به، ولا يكفي حضور صبي أو امرأة فقط. ولو واحدا إلخ أي ولو كان الحاضر واحداً، وروي عن الإمام وصاحبيه صحتها، وإن لم يحضره أحد. مراقي الفلاح: ٥١٠] والإذن العام حتى لو غلق الإمام باب قصره أو المحل الذي يصلي فيه بأصحابه لم يجز،
وإن أذن للناس بالدخول فيه ،صحت، ولكن لم يقض حق المسجد الجامع فيكره. [مراقي الفلاح: ٥١٠]
The Book of Prayer. Section on Friday Prayer. Or what is within the boundary of residence in the city according to the most correct view, health, safety from an oppressor, and soundness of eyes, soundness of legs. So it is not obligatory upon a sick person, or one blind in both eyes, or one with both legs amputated. For the validity of Friday prayer, six things are required: the city (misr) or its outskirts, the sultan or his deputy (so it is not obligatory upon one missing both legs), the time of Zuhr (so it is not valid before it and becomes invalid with its exit), the khutbah before it with the intention of the khutbah (i.e., before the prayer) during its time, the presence of one person to listen from among those for whom Friday is valid, even if one person according to the correct view, and general public permission. Commentary: 'within the boundary' means residence in a place that is within the boundary of residence in the city, which is a place from which if one departs with the intention of travel he becomes a traveler, and if one arrives he becomes a resident, like the suburbs and outskirts of the city that are not separated by a distance of one bowshot. It is not obligatory upon one outside it, even if he hears the call from the city, whether its built-up area is near or far according to the most correct view. So no obligation upon others, and some have corrected it as in al-Bada'i' that if one can attend Friday without hardship, it becomes obligatory upon him. ... (continued) ...
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn of Nur al-Idah on the conditions for Friday prayer, with commentary from Bushra and marginal notes. It first mentions conditions for obligation: health, safety from oppressor, sound eyes and legs. Then it lists six conditions for validity: (1) being in a city (misr) or its outskirts, (2) presence of a ruler (sultan) or his deputy, (3) time of Zuhr, (4) khutbah delivered before the prayer, (5) presence of at least one person from those for whom Friday is valid to hear the khutbah, (6) general permission for people to attend. The commentary expands on each: defines 'misr' and its boundary, clarifies that the sultan or his deputy must lead or authorize, notes that exit of Zuhr time invalidates the prayer, emphasizes that the khutbah must be with intention and in its time, explains that one listener suffices even if deaf or sleeping, and that general permission is required such that closing the door to the mosque invalidates the prayer unless permission is granted. There is an intra-Hanafi narration from Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn that Friday is valid even if no one attends, but the relied-upon position is that at least one person is needed.

Key Terms
المصر (al-misr): A large town or city with a ruler, judge, and mufti who enforce laws and hadd penalties; its built-up area must be extensive according to the apparent narration.
السلطان (al-sultan): The ruler or his deputy who leads the Friday prayer or authorizes someone else.
الإذن العام (al-idhn al-amm): General permission for the public to attend the Friday prayer; if the imam locks the door, even if he later opens it, it is disliked but valid if opened.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a condition for the validity of Friday prayer according to the text?
A) The prayer must be in a city or its outskirts.
B) The presence of the sultan or his deputy.
C) At least forty men attending.
D) The khutbah must be delivered before the prayer.

Key Takeaway
Friday prayer is valid only when all six conditions are met; the minimum congregation is one person besides the imam.

Congregation Size and Definition of a City for Friday Prayer
Specifies congregation size and city definition for Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for the validity of Jumu'ah regarding congregation size and define a misr according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah requires three men besides the imam; a city must have a judge capable of enforcing hudud.

This passage from Nur al-Idah specifies the exact number of men needed for the Jumu'ah congregation and defines the type of settlement (misr) where Friday prayer is valid. Understanding these conditions is crucial for determining where and when Jumu'ah can be held.

Guided Path
1
Identify the congregation condition
Note that three men besides the imam are required. The text says 'three men besides the imam' (thalathatu rijaalin ghayr al-imam). Consider who can be counted: slaves, travelers, sick are included; women and boys are excluded.
The congregation must be present from the beginning until the imam prostrates.
2
Understand the timing of congregation dispersal
If the congregation disperses after the imam's prostration, the imam may complete the prayer as Jumu'ah alone according to Abu Hanifa. If they disperse before, the prayer becomes invalid and must be made up as Zuhr.
This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa; the Sahibayn may differ.
3
Define a city (misr) for Jumu'ah
According to the Hanafi school, a misr is a place that has a mufti (or a judge who is also a mufti), an amir (ruler), and a judge who has the capacity to implement legal rulings and establish hadd penalties. The built-up area should be extensive, comparable to Mina.
Capacity to enforce, not actual enforcement, is required.
4
Apply the definition to a modern context
Consider whether a small town with a Muslim judge qualifies as a misr. If the judge has the authority to enforce hudud (even if rarely done), it may suffice. If there is no such authority, Jumu'ah may not be valid in that place.
This definition is unique to the Hanafi school; other schools have different criteria.

The Book of Prayer. Section on Friday Prayer. And the congregation: they are three men besides the imam, even if they are slaves, travelers, or sick. The condition is that they remain with the imam until he prostrates. If they disperse after his prostration, he completes it alone as Friday prayer according to Imam Abu Hanifa. If they disperse before his prostration, it becomes invalid. It is not valid with a woman or a boy along with two men. A slave and a sick person may lead the prayer. The city (misr) is every place that has a mufti, an amir, and a judge who implements legal rulings and establishes hadd penalties, and whose buildings reach (the extent of) Mina according to the apparent narration. If the judge or amir is a qualified mufti, that suffices and one need not have separate individuals. Friday prayer at Mina during the pilgrimage season is permissible for the caliph or the amir of Hajj. (Commentary) The congregation: the condition for its validity is that three or more pray with the imam, based on the consensus of scholars that congregation is necessary. They only differed on its number. The text generalizes three, so it includes slaves, travelers, sick, illiterate, and mute. Because they are fit to lead Friday prayer either absolutely or for those like them in illiteracy and muteness. So they may follow someone above them. Women and boys are excluded; Friday is not valid with them alone because they are not fit to lead it at all. The word 'three' implies men, and 'boy' is not a complete man. ... (continued) ...
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage continues the rules of Jumu'ah, now addressing the congregation size and the definition of a city (misr). The matn states that the congregation must consist of three men besides the imam, and they can be slaves, travelers, or sick. If they leave after the imam's prostration, he may complete it alone as Jumu'ah according to Abu Hanifa; if they leave before, it becomes invalid. Women and boys cannot constitute the congregation even if with two men. A slave or sick person may lead the prayer. Then the definition of a misr: it must have a mufti (or judge who is also a mufti), an amir, and a judge who can implement rulings and hadd penalties. The commentary clarifies that capacity to enforce is meant, not actual enforcement, citing that the Companions prayed behind al-Hajjaj despite his injustice. A woman can be a ruler but cannot lead Friday prayer herself; she may appoint a male imam. Also, the judge alone suffices if he is qualified to give fatwa. The example of Mina is given: it is a place near Mecca where Jumu'ah is allowed during Hajj season for the caliph or amir of Hajj.

Key Terms
الجماعة (al-jama'ah): For Jumu'ah, the congregation is three men besides the imam; they must remain until the imam prostrates.
المصر (al-misr): A place with a mufti (or judge who is also mufti), an amir, and a judge who has the capacity to implement legal rulings and hadd penalties; its built-up area should be extensive like Mina according to the apparent narration.
الحدود (al-hudud): The fixed corporal punishments (e.g., for theft, adultery) that the judge must be capable of enforcing to qualify the place as a misr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The prayer becomes invalid and must be made up as Zuhr
C) The prayer is still valid if the imam completes it
D) The congregation must return and repeat the prayer

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah requires a congregation of three men besides the imam who stay until prostration, and it must be held in a city (misr) with the capacity for legal enforcement.

The Minimum Congregation for Jumu'ah and the Condition of Staying Until Sujud
Ruling with proof on congregation size and condition of staying

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum number of men required for Jumu'ah, explain the condition that they must remain until prostration, and distinguish between Imam Abu Hanifa's view and the Sahibayn's view on early dispersal.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah requires three men who must stay with the imam until sujud; dispersal before that invalidates the prayer.

Friday prayer (Jumu'ah) is not like other prayers; it has unique conditions for validity. In this lesson, we examine the key condition of the congregation size and their obligation to remain with the imam until he prostrates. An important intra-Hanafi difference emerges regarding what happens if the congregation disperses after sujud but before salam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the required number and types of participants
The text states that the congregation must be three men besides the imam, and it expressly includes slaves, travelers, and the sick. Women and boys are excluded. Note the absolute term 'three' includes various categories of men.
The term 'three men' uses the masculine plural, excluding women.
2
Understand the condition of staying until sujud
The congregation must remain with the imam until he prostrates. If they disperse after his prostration, the imam can complete the prayer alone as Jumu'ah according to Abu Hanifa. If they disperse before prostration, the prayer is invalid and must be repeated as Zuhr.
This condition is unique to Jumu'ah and is based on the need for a stable congregation.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi disagreement
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that if the congregation leaves after sujud, the imam continues alone. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that if they leave before salam, the prayer becomes Zuhr. Understand the practical difference in ruling.
The mufta bihi opinion is to rely on the condition of staying until sujud, but the Sahibayn's view is also strong.
4
Apply the rule to a scenario
Consider a situation where three men attend Jumu'ah, but after the imam's prostration, two leave. According to Abu Hanifa, the imam completes Jumu'ah alone. According to the Sahibayn, it becomes Zuhr and must be prayed as such.
The difference hinges on whether the dispersal is before or after sujud, and whether the prayer reverts to Zuhr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة
أحكام الجمعة
والجماعة، وهم ثلاثة رجال غير الإمام، ولو كانوا عبيدا أو مسافرين أو مرضى، والشرط بقاؤهم مع الإمام حتى يسجد فإن نفروا بعد سجوده أتمها وحده جمعة، عند الإمام وإن نفروا قبل سجوده بطلت ولا تصح بامرأة أو صبي مع رجلين، وجاز للعبد والمريض أن يؤم فيها، والمصر كل موضع له مفت وأمير وقاض ينفذ الأحكام ويقيم الحدود، وبلغت أبنيته منى في ظاهر الرواية، وإذا كان القاضي أو الأمير مفتيا أغنى عن التعداد، وجازت الجمعة بمنى في الموسم، للخليفة أو أمير الحجاز، والجماعة أي شرط صحتها أن يصلي مع الإمام ثلاثة فأكثر ؛ لإجماع العلماء على أنه لابد فيها من الجماعة، وإنما اختلفوا في مقدارها، أطلق الثلاثة فشمل العبيد والمسافرين والمرضى والأميين والخرسى؛ لصلاحيتهم للإمامة في الجمعة إما لكل واحد أو لمن هو مثل حالهم في الأمي والأخرس، فصلحا أن يقتديا من فوقهما، ولا يرد عليه النساء والصبيان، فإن الجمعة لا تصح بهم وحدهم، لعدم صلاحيتهم للإمامة فيها بحال؛ لأن النساء خرجن بالتاء في ثلاثة، أي ثلاثة رجال، وكذا الصبي؛ لأنه ليس برجل كامل والمطلق ينصرف إلى الكامل. البحر الرائق بحذف: ٢٣٤/٢] ينفذ الأحكام المراد به القدرة على ذلك كما صرح به في "التحفة" عن الإمام، فتزييف صدر الشريعة له بظهور التواني في الأحكام لا سيما في إقامة الحدود في الأمصار مزيف كما في "الحلبي"، فالمراد: الشأن لا الحصول بالفعل، قال العلامة نوح: دفع الظلم عن المظلومين ليس بشرط في تحقق المصرية، بل الشرط في تحققها القدرة على الدفع، ومما يدل على عدم اشتراط الدفع بالفعل أن جماعة من الصحابة صلوها خلف الحجاج، وهو أظلم خلق الله تعالى. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥١٣] ويقيم الحدود احترز به عن المحكم والمرأة إذا كانت قاضية؛ فإنهما لا يقيمان الحدود وإن نفذا الأحكام، واكتفى بذكر الحدود عن القصاص؛ لأن من ملك إقامتها ملكه كذا في "فتح القدير"، وظاهره أن البلدة إذا كان قاضيها أو أميرها امرأة لا يكون مصراً، فلا تصح إقامة الجمعة فيها، والظاهر خلافه، قال في "البدائع": وأما والصبي العاقل، فلا تصح منهما إقامة الجمعة؛ لأنهما لا يصلحان للإمامة في سائر الصلوات، ففي الجمعة أولى، إلا أن المراة إذا كانت سلطاناً، فأمرت رجلاً صالحاً للإمامة حتى يصلي بهم الجمعة جاز؛ لأن المرأة تصلح سلطاناً أو قاضية في الجملة، فتصح إنابتها. [البحر الرائق: ٢٣٠/٢] المرأة
وإذا كان القاضي إلخ : أي إذا كان القاضي عالماً يصلح للإفتاء لا يجب أن يكون رجل قاضياً وآخر مفتياً، بل يكفي وجود القاضي وحده. بمنى هي بالكسر والقصر، موضع على فرسخين من مكة، [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥١٣]. والمفهوم من "البحر" أن بين مكة ومنى أربعة فراسخ.
Book of Prayer. Rulings of Friday. And the congregation: they are three men besides the imam, even if they are slaves, travelers, or sick. And the condition is that they remain with the imam until he prostrates; if they disperse after his prostration, he completes it alone as Jumu'ah according to Imam Abu Hanifa. If they disperse before his prostration, it is invalid. And it is not valid with a woman or a boy along with two men. And it is permissible for a slave and a sick person to lead the prayer in it. And a misr (city) is every place that has a mufti, an amir, and a judge who executes rulings and establishes hudud punishments, and its buildings reach Mina according to the apparent narration. And if the judge or amir is a mufti, it suffices without the count. And Jumu'ah is permissible in Mina during the season for the caliph or the amir of Hijaz. And the congregation means the condition of its validity is that he prays with three or more behind the imam, due to the consensus of scholars that congregation is necessary in it, and they only differed on its amount. He used the word 'three' absolutely, so it includes slaves, travelers, the sick, the illiterate, and the mute, because they are fit to lead Jumu'ah either for everyone or for those like them in the case of the illiterate and mute, so they are fit to be followed by those above them. And women and boys are not included, because Jumu'ah is not valid with them alone, due to their lack of fitness to lead Jumu'ah in any case, because women are excluded by the feminine ending in 'three', i.e., three men; likewise a boy because he is not a complete man, and the absolute is restricted to the complete. [Bahr al-Ra'iq abridged: 2/234] 'Executes rulings' means the ability to do so, as stated in al-Tuhfah from the Imam. So the refutation of Sadr al-Shari'ah due to apparent negligence in rulings, especially in establishing hudud in cities, is weak as in al-Halabi. So what is meant is the capacity, not actual occurrence. Allamah Nuh said: 'Removing oppression from the oppressed is not a condition for being a misr; rather the condition is the ability to remove it.' And evidence that actual removal is not required is that a group of Companions prayed behind al-Hajjaj, who was the most oppressive of Allah's creation. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 513] 'And establishes hudud' excludes the hakam (arbitrator) and a woman if she is a judge, because they do not establish hudud even if they execute rulings. And he sufficed by mentioning hudud over qisas, because whoever has the authority to establish them has that authority. Such is in Fath al-Qadir. Its apparent meaning is that if the judge or amir of a town is a woman, it is not a misr, so Jumu'ah is not valid there. But the apparent contrary is the case. He said in al-Bada'i': 'As for a woman and a sane boy, Jumu'ah is not valid from them because they are not fit to lead in other prayers, so in Jumu'ah it is more so. However, if a woman is a ruler, she can order a man fit to lead them in Jumu'ah; it is permissible, because a woman can be a ruler or a judge in general, so her deputation is valid.' [Bahr al-Ra'iq: 2/230] Woman. And 'if the judge etc.' means if the judge is knowledgeable enough to give fatwa, it is not necessary that one person be judge and another mufti; rather the existence of the judge alone suffices. Mina is with kasra and qasr (shortening), a place two farsakhs from Mecca [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 513]. And what is understood from al-Bahr is that between Mecca and Mina is four farsakhs.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah, with expansions from Bahr al-Ra'iq, Hashiyat al-Tahtawi, and others, lays out the conditions for the validity of Friday prayer (Jumu'ah) according to the Hanafi school. The passage type is a ruling with proof, where the core ruling is that Jumu'ah requires a minimum of three men (not counting the imam) to be present throughout the prayer. The author first states the condition: the congregation (al-jama'ah) is three men besides the imam, even if they are slaves, travelers, or sick. Then he adds a critical condition: they must remain with the imam until he prostrates. Here an intra-Hanafi difference appears: according to Imam Abu Hanifa (عند الإمام), if they disperse after the imam's prostration, he can complete the prayer alone as Jumu'ah; but if they disperse before his prostration, the prayer is invalid and must be made up as Zuhr. The text then notes that Jumu'ah is not valid if a woman or a boy is included as part of the three, even if there are two real men. It also allows a slave or a sick person to lead the prayer. Next, the definition of a misr (city) for Jumu'ah is given: a place with a mufti, amir, and judge who can execute rulings and establish hudud punishments, and its buildings must reach Mina (a place near Mecca) according to the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah). If the judge or amir is also a mufti, that suffices. Jumu'ah is permissible in Mina during the pilgrimage season for the caliph or the amir of Hijaz. The passage then provides the proof for the number: consensus (ijma') of scholars that congregation is necessary, though they differed on the exact number. The absolute term 'three' includes various types of men who are fit to lead (except women and boys). The reason women and boys are excluded is that women are excluded by the feminine ending in the word 'three' (ثلاثة), and a boy is not a complete man. The commentary clarifies that the phrase 'executes rulings' refers to ability, not actual action, and that actual removal of oppression is not required for a place to be a city. It also discusses the case of a woman judge: if the judge or amir is a woman, the place is not a city and Jumu'ah cannot be held there, but if a woman is a ruler, she can deputize a man to lead the prayer. Finally, it notes that Mina is two farsakhs from Mecca (or four according to al-Bahr).

Key Terms
الجمعة (al-jumu'ah): The Friday congregational prayer that replaces Zuhr, valid only with specific conditions including a minimum of three men besides the imam.
سجوده (sujud): Prostration in prayer; here, the critical point until which the congregation must stay.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) 40 men
B) 12 men
C) 3 men
D) 2 men

Key Takeaway
The validity of Jumu'ah depends on the presence of at least three men besides the imam who remain until the imam's prostration.

intermediate

Definition of a City (Misr) for the Validity of Jumu'ah
Definition and conditions of a misr for Jumu'ah validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define a misr for Jumu'ah according to the Hanafi school, list its required authorities, explain the condition of hudud enforcement, and evaluate the ruling when the judge is a woman.

Core Idea
A misr requires a mufti, amir, and judge with the ability to execute rulings and establish hudud; actual enforcement is not necessary.

Jumu'ah prayer has a unique condition tied to locality: it must be performed in a recognized city (misr) or its vicinity. In this lesson, we unpack the Hanafi definition of a misr, the required officials, and the debate over whether the ability to enforce hudud is sufficient or actual enforcement is needed.

Guided Path
1
List the three required authorities for a misr
The text states a misr must have a mufti (one who gives legal rulings), an amir (governor), and a judge (qadi) who can execute rulings and establish hudud punishments. Understand each role.
If one person holds multiple roles, that suffices.
2
Clarify the condition of hudud enforcement
The phrase 'establishes hudud' is interpreted as the ability to do so, not actual enforcement. The commentary emphasizes that capacity is sufficient, citing the example of Companions praying behind the oppressive ruler al-Hajjaj.
This is a key nuance: ability vs. actuality.
3
Consider the case of a woman as judge or amir
The text initially suggests that if the judge or amir is a woman, the place is not a misr. However, later commentary allows that a woman ruler can deputize a man to lead Jumu'ah. Understand the ikhtilaf within the school.
The practical outcome: Jumu'ah can still be held under a female ruler by proxy.
4
Apply the misr definition to a modern scenario
Consider a modern city with a mayor, a mufti, and a judge who can pass sentences. Does it qualify? Also consider a village with only a judge but no amir.
The condition is not about size but about the presence of these authorities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة
أحكام الجمعة
والجماعة، وهم ثلاثة رجال غير الإمام، ولو كانوا عبيدا أو مسافرين أو مرضى، والشرط بقاؤهم مع الإمام حتى يسجد فإن نفروا بعد سجوده أتمها وحده جمعة، عند الإمام وإن نفروا قبل سجوده بطلت ولا تصح بامرأة أو صبي مع رجلين، وجاز للعبد والمريض أن يؤم فيها، والمصر كل موضع له مفت وأمير وقاض ينفذ الأحكام ويقيم الحدود، وبلغت أبنيته منى في ظاهر الرواية، وإذا كان القاضي أو الأمير مفتيا أغنى عن التعداد، وجازت الجمعة بمنى في الموسم، للخليفة أو أمير الحجاز، والجماعة أي شرط صحتها أن يصلي مع الإمام ثلاثة فأكثر ؛ لإجماع العلماء على أنه لابد فيها من الجماعة، وإنما اختلفوا في مقدارها، أطلق الثلاثة فشمل العبيد والمسافرين والمرضى والأميين والخرسى؛ لصلاحيتهم للإمامة في الجمعة إما لكل واحد أو لمن هو مثل حالهم في الأمي والأخرس، فصلحا أن يقتديا من فوقهما، ولا يرد عليه النساء والصبيان، فإن الجمعة لا تصح بهم وحدهم، لعدم صلاحيتهم للإمامة فيها بحال؛ لأن النساء خرجن بالتاء في ثلاثة، أي ثلاثة رجال، وكذا الصبي؛ لأنه ليس برجل كامل والمطلق ينصرف إلى الكامل. البحر الرائق بحذف: ٢٣٤/٢] ينفذ الأحكام المراد به القدرة على ذلك كما صرح به في "التحفة" عن الإمام، فتزييف صدر الشريعة له بظهور التواني في الأحكام لا سيما في إقامة الحدود في الأمصار مزيف كما في "الحلبي"، فالمراد: الشأن لا الحصول بالفعل، قال العلامة نوح: دفع الظلم عن المظلومين ليس بشرط في تحقق المصرية، بل الشرط في تحققها القدرة على الدفع، ومما يدل على عدم اشتراط الدفع بالفعل أن جماعة من الصحابة صلوها خلف الحجاج، وهو أظلم خلق الله تعالى. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥١٣] ويقيم الحدود احترز به عن المحكم والمرأة إذا كانت قاضية؛ فإنهما لا يقيمان الحدود وإن نفذا الأحكام، واكتفى بذكر الحدود عن القصاص؛ لأن من ملك إقامتها ملكه كذا في "فتح القدير"، وظاهره أن البلدة إذا كان قاضيها أو أميرها امرأة لا يكون مصراً، فلا تصح إقامة الجمعة فيها، والظاهر خلافه، قال في "البدائع": وأما والصبي العاقل، فلا تصح منهما إقامة الجمعة؛ لأنهما لا يصلحان للإمامة في سائر الصلوات، ففي الجمعة أولى، إلا أن المراة إذا كانت سلطاناً، فأمرت رجلاً صالحاً للإمامة حتى يصلي بهم الجمعة جاز؛ لأن المرأة تصلح سلطاناً أو قاضية في الجملة، فتصح إنابتها. [البحر الرائق: ٢٣٠/٢] المرأة
وإذا كان القاضي إلخ : أي إذا كان القاضي عالماً يصلح للإفتاء لا يجب أن يكون رجل قاضياً وآخر مفتياً، بل يكفي وجود القاضي وحده. بمنى هي بالكسر والقصر، موضع على فرسخين من مكة، [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥١٣]. والمفهوم من "البحر" أن بين مكة ومنى أربعة فراسخ.
Book of Prayer. Rulings of Friday. And the congregation: they are three men besides the imam, even if they are slaves, travelers, or sick. And the condition is that they remain with the imam until he prostrates; if they disperse after his prostration, he completes it alone as Jumu'ah according to Imam Abu Hanifa. If they disperse before his prostration, it is invalid. And it is not valid with a woman or a boy along with two men. And it is permissible for a slave and a sick person to lead the prayer in it. And a misr (city) is every place that has a mufti, an amir, and a judge who executes rulings and establishes hudud punishments, and its buildings reach Mina according to the apparent narration. And if the judge or amir is a mufti, it suffices without the count. And Jumu'ah is permissible in Mina during the season for the caliph or the amir of Hijaz. And the congregation means the condition of its validity is that he prays with three or more behind the imam, due to the consensus of scholars that congregation is necessary in it, and they only differed on its amount. He used the word 'three' absolutely, so it includes slaves, travelers, the sick, the illiterate, and the mute, because they are fit to lead Jumu'ah either for everyone or for those like them in the case of the illiterate and mute, so they are fit to be followed by those above them. And women and boys are not included, because Jumu'ah is not valid with them alone, due to their lack of fitness to lead Jumu'ah in any case, because women are excluded by the feminine ending in 'three', i.e., three men; likewise a boy because he is not a complete man, and the absolute is restricted to the complete. [Bahr al-Ra'iq abridged: 2/234] 'Executes rulings' means the ability to do so, as stated in al-Tuhfah from the Imam. So the refutation of Sadr al-Shari'ah due to apparent negligence in rulings, especially in establishing hudud in cities, is weak as in al-Halabi. So what is meant is the capacity, not actual occurrence. Allamah Nuh said: 'Removing oppression from the oppressed is not a condition for being a misr; rather the condition is the ability to remove it.' And evidence that actual removal is not required is that a group of Companions prayed behind al-Hajjaj, who was the most oppressive of Allah's creation. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 513] 'And establishes hudud' excludes the hakam (arbitrator) and a woman if she is a judge, because they do not establish hudud even if they execute rulings. And he sufficed by mentioning hudud over qisas, because whoever has the authority to establish them has that authority. Such is in Fath al-Qadir. Its apparent meaning is that if the judge or amir of a town is a woman, it is not a misr, so Jumu'ah is not valid there. But the apparent contrary is the case. He said in al-Bada'i': 'As for a woman and a sane boy, Jumu'ah is not valid from them because they are not fit to lead in other prayers, so in Jumu'ah it is more so. However, if a woman is a ruler, she can order a man fit to lead them in Jumu'ah; it is permissible, because a woman can be a ruler or a judge in general, so her deputation is valid.' [Bahr al-Ra'iq: 2/230] Woman. And 'if the judge etc.' means if the judge is knowledgeable enough to give fatwa, it is not necessary that one person be judge and another mufti; rather the existence of the judge alone suffices. Mina is with kasra and qasr (shortening), a place two farsakhs from Mecca [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 513]. And what is understood from al-Bahr is that between Mecca and Mina is four farsakhs.

Key Terms
المصر (al-misr): A city where Jumu'ah is valid; defined as a place with a mufti, amir, and judge who can execute rulings and establish hudud, and whose buildings reach Mina.
الحدود (al-hudud): Fixed punishments for major crimes like theft and adultery, whose establishment requires a qualified judge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the key nuance in the condition that the judge 'establishes hudud'?
A) He must actually execute hudud punishments regularly
B) He must have the ability and authority to do so, even if not carried out
C) He must be a male
D) He must be a mufti as well

Key Takeaway
A valid misr for Jumu'ah requires the presence of a mufti, amir, and judge who have the ability to execute rulings and establish hudud, not necessarily the actual execution.
