The Eighteen Sunnas of the Friday Khutbah
Lists and explains the 18 sunnah acts of the Friday sermon

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the eighteen sunnah acts of the Friday khutbah and explain the ruling if any is omitted.

Core Idea
The khutbah has 18 sunnah acts; omitting them is disliked but the khutbah remains valid.

The Friday khutbah is a condition for Jumu'ah. While its core is obligatory, there are many recommended acts (sunan) that perfect it. This passage enumerates 18 such acts and clarifies that missing them does not invalidate the khutbah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overall ruling
The 18 items are sunnah, not wajib. Omitting a sunnah is makruh tanzihi (disliked) but the khutbah remains valid.
This is the key principle: the khutbah is not invalidated by leaving a sunnah.
2
Categorize the sunnas
Group them into preparatory acts (taharah, covering awrah, sitting, adhan), delivery acts (standing, facing people, etc.), and content acts (praise, shahadah, etc.).
This helps memorization and understanding their roles.
3
Note the disputes
There is intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether sitting before the khutbah is for rest (and thus not sunnah for Eid) and on leaning on a sword versus a staff.
The relied-upon view: leaning on a sword is only for towns conquered by force.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
If a khatib omits a sunnah (e.g., does not say alhamdulillah), the khutbah is valid but disliked. If he is in a state of impurity, it is valid but disliked; repeating is recommended if he was junub.
The validity of the khutbah depends on its essential elements, not the sunnan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصح الاقتصار في الخطبة على نحو تسبيحة أو تحميدة مع الكراهة. وسنن الخطبة ثمانية عشر شيئاً: الطهارة، وستر العورة، والجلوس على المنبر قبل الشروع في الخطبة، والأذان بين يديه كالإقامة ثم قيامه والسيف بيساره متكنا عليه في كل بلدة فتحت عنوة، وبدونه في بلدة فتحت صلحا، واستقبال القوم بوجهه، وبداءته بحمد الله، والثناء عليه بما هو أهله والشهادتان، والصلاة على النبي والعظة والتذكير وقراءة آية من القرآن وخطبتان، والجلوس بين الخطبتين، وإعادة الحمد والثناء، والصلاة على النبي في ابتداء الخطبة الثانية والدعاء فيها للمؤمنين بالاستغفار لهم،
ثمانية عشر : هذا قول تقريبي؛ فإنه يزاد عليها أن يكون جلوس الخطيب في مخدعه عن يمين المنبر أو جهته لا بساً السواد أو البياض. الطهارة: فلو خطب محدثاً أو جنباً جاز ويكره، ويستحب إعادتها إذا كان جنباً إلا أذانه، وإن لم يعد أجزأه إن لم يطل الفصل بأجنبي. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥١٤] وستر العورة: هو من سنن الخطبة إجماعاً وإن كان فرضاً في حد ذاته، حتى لو خطب بدونه أجزاً. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥١٥] والجلوس: اختلف فيه هل هو للاستراحة، وعلى الأول لا يسن في العيد؛ لأنه لا أذان له [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥١٥] ثم قيامه أي بعد الأذان في الخطبتين، ولو قعد فيهما أو في أحدهما أجزأ، وكره من غير عذر، وإن خطب مضطجعاً أجزا. [مراقي الفلاح ٥١٥] والسيف إلخ : أي إذا قام يكون السيف بيساره متكئاً عليه في كل بلدة فتحت عنوة؛ ليريهم أنها فتحت بالسيف، فإذا رجعتم عن الإسلام فذلك باق بأيدي المسلمين، يقاتلونكم به حتى ترجعوا إلى الإسلام، مراقي الفلاح ٥١٥] . وفيه إشارة إلى أنه يكره الاتكاء على غيره كعصا وقوس؛ لأنه خلاف السنة، وناقش فيه ابن أمير حاج بأنه ثبت أنه قام خطيباً بالمدينة متكناً على عصا أو قوس كما في "أبي داود". [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥١٥] واستقبال القوم إلخ : فإن ولاهم ظهره كره، قال شمس الأئمة: من كان أمام الإمام استقبل بوجهه، ومن يمين الإمام أو يساره انحرف إلى الإمام، وقال السرخسي: الرسم في زماننا استقبال القوم القبلة وترك استقبالهم الخطيب؛ لما يلحقهم من الحرج بتسوية الصفوف بعد فراغ الخطيب من خطبته لكثرة الزحام [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥١٥] وبداءته: أي بعد التعوذ في نفسه سراً.
And it is valid to limit the khutbah to something like a tasbih or tahmid, but with dislike (karahah). And the sunnas of the khutbah are eighteen things: purity (taharah), covering the awrah, sitting on the minbar before starting the khutbah, the adhan before him like the iqamah, then standing while the sword is in his left hand leaning on it in every town conquered by force, and without it in a town conquered by peace, facing the people with his face, beginning with praise of Allah, extolling Him as He deserves, the two shahadahs, sending blessings upon the Prophet, admonition and reminder, recitation of a verse from the Quran, two khutbahs, sitting between the two khutbahs, repeating praise and extolling, sending blessings upon the Prophet at the beginning of the second khutbah, and supplication for the believers asking forgiveness for them. 'Eighteen' is an approximate statement, for additional acts are that the khatib sit in his private room to the right of the minbar or its direction, dressed in black or white. Taharah: if he delivers the khutbah while in a state of minor or major impurity, it is permissible but disliked, and it is recommended to repeat it if he is in major impurity except for his adhan, and if he does not repeat, it suffices if the interval is not long with something extraneous. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 514] Covering the awrah: it is among the sunnas of the khutbah by consensus, even though it is obligatory in itself, so if he delivers the khutbah without covering it, it is valid. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 515] Sitting: there is disagreement whether it is for rest, and on the first view it is not sunnah for the Eid khutbah because there is no adhan for it. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 515] Then his standing i.e. after the adhan for the two khutbahs, and if he sits in both or one of them, it suffices, but it is disliked without excuse; if he delivers the khutbah lying down, it suffices. [Maraqi al-Falah: 515] The sword etc.: meaning when he stands, the sword is in his left hand leaning on it in every town conquered by force, to show them that it was conquered by the sword, and if you revert from Islam, that remains with the Muslims, they fight you with it until you return to Islam. [Maraqi al-Falah: 515] And in it is an indication that leaning on other than it, like a staff or bow, is disliked because it is contrary to the Sunnah. Ibn Amir Hajj objected that it is established that the Prophet stood as a khatib in Medina leaning on a staff or bow as in Abu Dawud. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 515] Facing the people etc.: if he turns his back to them, it is disliked. Shams al-A'immah said: whoever is in front of the imam faces him with his face, and whoever is to the right or left of the imam turns toward the imam. Al-Sarakhsi said: the custom in our time is that the people face the qiblah and leave facing the khatib, due to the difficulty of straightening rows after the khatib finishes his khutbah because of crowding. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 515] And his beginning: after seeking refuge (ta'awwudh) silently within himself.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah, with commentary from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi and Maraqi al-Falah, details the sunnan (recommended acts) of the Friday khutbah (sermon). The passage type is a definition-ruling that enumerates and explains the eighteen sunnas. It begins by noting that it is permissible to shorten the khutbah to a single tasbih or tahmid, but that is disliked. Then it lists eighteen specific sunnas: 1) purity (taharah) – though the khutbah is valid even without it, but disliked; 2) covering the awrah – obligatory in itself but a sunnah of the khutbah; 3) sitting on the minbar before starting; 4) the adhan before the khatib (like the iqamah); 5) standing while leaning on a sword in the left hand in towns conquered by force, and without it in towns conquered peacefully; 6) facing the people; 7) beginning with praise of Allah; 8) extolling Him; 9) the two shahadahs; 10) sending blessings upon the Prophet; 11) admonition and reminder; 12) reciting a Quranic verse; 13) delivering two khutbahs; 14) sitting between them; 15) repeating praise and extolling in the second; 16) sending blessings upon the Prophet at the beginning of the second; 17) supplicating for the believers asking forgiveness. The commentary clarifies that the number 18 is approximate, and additional sunnas include the khatib sitting in a private room to the right of the minbar dressed in black or white. It explains that if the khatib is impure, the khutbah is valid but disliked, and it is recommended to repeat it if he was in major impurity unless the interval is long. Covering the awrah is a sunnah by consensus, even though it is an obligation in itself. Sitting before the khutbah: some say it is for rest, and on that view it is not sunnah for Eid. Standing after the adhan is sunnah; if he sits, it is disliked but valid. Leaning on a sword is specific to towns conquered by force. Facing the people is sunnah, but if the khatib turns his back, it is disliked. The custom in later times is for the people to face the qiblah due to crowding. Beginning the khutbah is after silently seeking refuge (ta'awwudh).

Key Terms
الخطبة (al-khutbah): The Friday sermon delivered by the khatib before the prayer, consisting of two parts separated by a sitting.
سنن الخطبة (sunan al-khutbah): The recommended acts during the Friday sermon; omitting them is not sinful but disliked.

Key Takeaway
The eighteen sunnas of the Friday khutbah are recommended; omitting them does not invalidate the khutbah but is disliked.

The Eighteen Sunnah Acts of the Friday Sermon
Lists and explains the eighteen sunan of the Friday sermon.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the eighteen sunan of the Friday khutbah and state the ruling when any sunnah is omitted.

Core Idea
The eighteen sunan of the Friday sermon are recommended; omitting any is disliked but does not invalidate.

The Friday sermon (khutbah) is a condition for the validity of Jumu'ah prayer. While a minimal sermon suffices, the Prophet ﷺ established specific sunan that perfect the act. This passage enumerates eighteen such sunan, covering purity, posture, content, and delivery. Understanding these helps the khatib maximize reward and avoid dislike.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on minimal sermon
The passage begins by stating that a very short sermon is valid but disliked. This sets the baseline: the sunan are not obligatory.
The minimal is a single tasbih or tahmid.
2
Memorize the list of eighteen sunan
Enumerate the eighteen items in order: purity, covering awrah, sitting on minbar, adhan, standing, sword in left hand (if conquered by force), facing people, beginning with praise, shahadas, salawat, admonition, recitation of a verse, two sermons, sitting between them, repeating praise and salawat in second sermon, supplication.
The list is a mnemonic for the khatib's actions.
3
Analyze the legal effect of omitting each sunnah
For each sunnah, note whether omission invalidates the sermon. The passage clarifies that even major omissions (like impurity or missing a part) result in validity with dislike, except when the omitted act is itself obligatory (e.g., covering awrah is fard but its omission from sermon is only makruh).
The sermon remains valid but the khatib loses reward.
4
Understand the historical context of the sword
Leaning on a sword is specific to towns conquered by force, symbolizing that Islam was established by struggle. In towns conquered peacefully, no sword is used.
This sunnah commemorates early Islamic history.
5
Apply the sunan to modern practice
Identify which sunan are still observed today (e.g., sitting on minbar, facing the congregation) and which may be adapted (e.g., leaning on a staff instead of sword is discussed).
The passage includes disagreement on leaning on a staff.

أحكام الجمعة
وصح الاقتصار في الخطبة على نحو تسبيحة أو تحميدة مع الكراهة. وسنن الخطبة ثمانية عشر شيئاً: الطهارة، وستر العورة، والجلوس على المنبر قبل الشروع في الخطبة، والأذان بين يديه كالإقامة ثم قيامه والسيف بيساره متكنا عليه في كل بلدة فتحت عنوة، وبدونه في بلدة فتحت صلحا، واستقبال القوم بوجهه، وبداءته بحمد الله، والثناء عليه بما هو أهله والشهادتان، والصلاة على [النبي؟] والعظة والتذكير وقراءة آية من القرآن وخطبتان، والجلوس بين الخطبتين، وإعادة الحمد والثناء، والصلاة على النبي في ابتداء الخطبة الثانية والدعاء فيها للمؤمنين بالاستغفار لهم.
ثمانية عشر : هذا قول تقريبي؛ فإنه يزاد عليها أن يكون جلوس الخطيب في مخدعه عن يمين المنبر أو جهته لابساً السواد أو البياض. الطهارة: فلو خطب محدثاً أو جنباً جاز ويكره، ويستحب إعادتها إذا كان جنباً إلا أذانه، وإن لم يعد أجزأه إن لم يطل الفصل بأجنبي. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥١٤] وستر العورة: هو من سنن الخطبة إجماعاً وإن كان فرضاً في حد ذاته، حتى لو خطب بدونه أجزأ. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥١٥] والجلوس: اختلف فيه هل هو للاستراحة، وعلى الأول لا يسن في العيد؛ لأنه لا أذان له [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥١٥] ثم قيامه أي بعد الأذان في الخطبتين، ولو قعد فيهما أو في أحدهما أجزأ، وكره من غير عذر، وإن خطب مضطجعاً أجزأ. [مراقي الفلاح ٥١٥] والسيف إلخ : أي إذا قام يكون السيف بيساره متكئاً عليه في كل بلدة فتحت عنوة؛ ليريهم أنها فتحت بالسيف، فإذا رجعتم عن الإسلام فذلك باق بأيدي المسلمين، يقاتلونكم به حتى ترجعوا إلى الإسلام. [مراقي الفلاح ٥١٥] . وفيه إشارة إلى أنه يكره الاتكاء على غيره كعصا وقوس؛ لأنه خلاف السنة، وناقش فيه ابن أمير حاج بأنه ثبت أنه [؟] قام خطيباً بالمدينة متكناً على عصا أو قوس كما في "أبي داود". [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥١٥] واستقبال القوم إلخ : فإن ولاهم ظهره كره، قال شمس الأئمة: من كان أمام الإمام استقبل بوجهه، ومن يمين الإمام أو يساره انحرف إلى الإمام، وقال السرخسي: الرسم في زماننا استقبال القوم القبلة وترك استقبالهم الخطيب؛ لما يلحقهم من الحرج بتسوية الصفوف بعد فراغ الخطيب من خطبته لكثرة الزحام [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥١٥] وبداءته: أي بعد التعوذ في نفسه سراً.
وأن يسمع القوم الخطبة، وتخفيف الخطبتين بقدر سورة من طوال المفصل، ويكره التطويل وترك شيء من السنن
Rulings of Friday. It is valid to limit the sermon to something like a tasbih or tahmid, but with dislike. The sunan of the sermon are eighteen things: purity, covering the awrah, sitting on the minbar before beginning the sermon, the adhan before him like the iqamah, then his standing, and the sword in his left hand leaning on it in every town conquered by force, and without it in a town conquered by peace, and facing the people with his face, and beginning with praise of Allah, and extolling Him as He deserves, and the two shahadas, and sending blessings on the Prophet, and admonition and reminder, and reciting a verse from the Qur'an, and two sermons, and sitting between the two sermons, and repeating praise and extolling, and sending blessings on the Prophet at the beginning of the second sermon, and supplication in it for the believers asking forgiveness for them. Eighteen: this is an approximate statement; for added to it is that the khatib sit in his chamber to the right of the minbar or its direction, dressed in black or white. Purity: if he delivers the sermon while in a state of minor or major ritual impurity, it is permissible but disliked, and it is recommended to repeat it if he was junub, except for his adhan, and if he does not repeat it, it suffices him if the interval is not long with something extraneous. Covering the awrah: it is from the sunan of the sermon by consensus, even though it is obligatory in itself, so if he delivers the sermon without it, it suffices. Sitting: there is disagreement whether it is for rest, and on the first view it is not sunna on Eid because there is no adhan for it. Then his standing, i.e. after the adhan in the two sermons, and if he sits in them or in one of them, it suffices, but it is disliked without excuse, and if he delivers the sermon lying down, it suffices. The sword etc.: i.e. when he stands, the sword is in his left hand, leaning on it, in every town conquered by force, to show them that it was conquered by the sword, so if you revert from Islam, that remains in the hands of the Muslims, they will fight you with it until you return to Islam. This contains an indication that it is disliked to lean on something else like a staff or bow because it is contrary to the Sunnah, and Ibn Amir Hajj objected that it is established that he [the Prophet] stood as a khatib in Medina leaning on a staff or bow as in Abu Dawud. Facing the people etc.: if he turns his back to them, it is disliked. Shams al-A'imma said: whoever is in front of the imam faces him, and whoever is to the right or left of the imam turns towards the imam. Al-Sarakhsi said: the custom in our time is for the people to face the qibla and stop facing the khatib due to the difficulty they experience in straightening the rows after the khatib finishes his sermon because of the great crowding. And his beginning: i.e. after seeking refuge inwardly secretly. And that the people hear the sermon, and shortening the two sermons to the extent of a surah from the lengthy mufassal, and it is disliked to lengthen and to omit any of the sunan.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement explaining the eighteen sunnah acts of the Friday sermon according to the Hanafi school. It begins by noting that a minimal sermon consisting of a single tasbih or tahmid is valid but disliked. The eighteen sunan are then listed, covering purity, covering the awrah, sitting on the minbar, the adhan, standing, leaning on a sword (in towns conquered by force), facing the congregation, beginning with praise of Allah, the two shahadas, blessings on the Prophet, admonition, recitation of a Quranic verse, giving two sermons, sitting between them, and repeating praise and blessings, and supplication. The commentary then expands on each item. For purity, it clarifies that delivering the sermon in a state of minor or major impurity is valid but disliked, though it is recommended to repeat if one was junub. Covering the awrah is a sunnah of the sermon by consensus, even though it is obligatory in itself; omission does not invalidate. Sitting on the minbar before the sermon is for rest, and it is not sunnah for the Eid sermon since there is no adhan before it. Standing after the adhan is required; sitting without excuse is disliked, but the sermon is still valid. Leaning on a sword is specific to towns conquered by force; leaning on a staff or bow is disliked. Facing the congregation is sunnah; turning one's back is disliked. The passage concludes by emphasizing that the people should hear the sermon, and shortening the sermon to the length of a medium surah (like from the lengthy mufassal) is recommended, while lengthening or omitting any sunnah is disliked. The overall tone is instructional, providing practical fiqh for the khatib.

Key Terms
الخطبة (al-khutbah): The Friday sermon, an obligatory part of the Friday prayer, consisting of two speeches separated by a sitting.
سنن الخطبة (sunan al-khutbah): The recommended acts (sunnah) of the Friday sermon; omission is disliked but does not invalidate the sermon.
المنبر (al-minbar): The pulpit from which the khatib delivers the sermon.

Obligations and Prohibitions for Friday Prayer: The Adhan Dispute
States obligations, prohibitions, and a disputed ruling on the adhan trigger

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligations and prohibitions of Friday prayer according to the Hanafi school and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding which adhan triggers the prohibition of sale and travel.

Core Idea
The first adhan triggers the prohibition of sale and travel; al-Tahawi's contrary view is considered weak.

Friday prayer carries a unique set of rules: walking to the mosque is obligatory, and once the first adhan is called, certain worldly activities become prohibited. A dispute exists within the Hanafi school about which adhan triggers these prohibitions—a distinction with practical consequences for timing. This lesson will walk you through the key rulings and the reasoning behind the preferred view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the obligations of Friday prayer
From the matn, list the obligatory actions: walking (sa'y) to the mosque, leaving sale after the first adhan, and maintaining proper conduct during the khutbah. Note the ruling level: these are wajib (obligatory) in the Hanafi school.
The text uses 'يجب' for sa'y and 'ترك البيع' (leaving sale) is also wajib by implication.
2
Trace the prohibitions during the imam's emergence
Once the imam comes out, all prayer, speech, returning salaam, and responding to sneezes are forbidden until the prayer ends. Understand the scope: this includes make-up prayers, funeral prayers, and supererogatory prayers, with exceptions for those who are in the middle of a missed wajib prayer.
The commentary expands on 'فلا صلاة' to include various types, showing the comprehensive prohibition.
3
Locate the intra-Hanafi dispute on the adhan
The text states 'بالأذان الأول في الأصح' (the first adhan in the correct view). Recognize that al-Tahawi held the second adhan (at the minbar) as the trigger. Examine the evidence: al-Tahawi relied on the practice of the Prophet and the two shaykhs, but al-Bahr deems this weak.
The dispute is over the timing of the prohibition of sale and travel.
4
Analyze the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If the first adhan triggers prohibition, sale and travel become unlawful earlier. If the second adhan, they become unlawful only later when the imam ascends the minbar. This affects the validity of transactions and the permissibility of travel.
The Hanafi mufta bihi is the first adhan, making the prohibition start earlier.
5
Apply the exemption rules
List those exempt from Friday prayer: sick, traveler, slave, woman, blind, crippled. Understand that if an exempt person performs Friday prayer, it fulfills the obligation of the time (zuhr), but Friday is not a substitute; rather, the duty of zuhr is dropped.
This clarifies the nature of Friday as a distinct obligation that lifts the zuhr duty.

ويجب السعي للجمعة، وترك البيع بالأذان الأول في الأصح، وإذا خرج الإمام فلا صلاة ولا كلام ولا يرد سلاماً، ولا يُشَمِّتُ عاطساً دنيويا أو دينيا حتى يفرغ من صلاته وكره الحاضر الخطبة الأكل والشرب والعبث والالتفات وقال الكمال: يحرم ولا يسلم الخطيب على القوم إذا استوى على المنبر، وكره الخروج من المصر بعد النداء ما لم يصل، ومن لا جمعة عليه إن أدّاها جاز عن فرض الوقت، بمعنى ما دام يسمع القوم: ويجهر في الثانية دون الأولى. ويجب السعي إلخ أراد الذهاب ماشياً بالسكينة والوقار لا الهرولة؛ لأنها تذهب بهاء المؤمن والمشي أفضل لمن يقدر عليه [مراقي الفلاح: ٥١٦] . واختلفوا في الرجوع، فقيل: هو كالذهاب إليها فالمشي أفضل، وقيل: هو كالخروج إلى سائر الحاجات، وهو الأصح. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥١٦] الأصح وقال الطحاوي: المعتبر هو الأذان الثاني عند المنبر ؛ لأنه الذي كان في زمنه والشيخين بعده، قال في "البحر" : وهو ضعيف. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥١٨] وإذا خرج إلخ : أي من حجرته إن كانت وإلا فقيامه للصعود قاطع فيثبت المنع بمجرد ظهوره ولو قبل صعوده المنبر، وقيل: إذا صعد، ونفى الصلاة فشمل ما إذا كانت قضاء فائتة أو صلاة جنازة أو سجدة تلاوة أو منذورة أو نفلاً، إلا إذا تذكر فائتة ولو وتراً وهو صاحب ترتيب فلا يكره الشروع فيهما حينئذ، بل يجب لضرورة صحة الجمعة، وأفاد أنه لا يكره الشروع قبل الخروج، فيتم ما شرع فيه ولو خطب الإمام من غير كراهة مطلقاً، إلا إذا كان في نفل؛ فإنه يتم شفعاً ثم يقطع، ولو كان خروجه بعد القيام للثالثة أتم أيضاً؛ لأنه وجب عليه الشفع الثاني بالقيام إليه، واختلف في سنة الجمعة، فقيل: يقطع على رأس الركعتين كالنفل المطلق، والصحيح أنه يتمها؛ لأنه كصلاة واجبة. [حاشية الطحطاوي ومراقي الفلاح بتغيير: ٥١٨] ولا يرد سلاماً : أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان بلسانه أو بقلبه قبل الفراغ أو بعده، ويرتكب بسلامه إثماً. وكره الخروج [أي لمن تجب عليه الجمعة أطلق الكراهة فتكون تحريمية وأخرجنا من لا تجب عليه الجمعة، فلا كراهة في خروجه بعد النداء: أي الأذان الأول، وقيل: الثاني. [مراقي الفلاح: ٥٢٠]
ومن لا جمعة عليه كمريض ومسافر ورقيق وامرأة وأعمى ومقعد. [مراقي الفلاح: ٥٢٠]
فرض الوقت: قال القهستاني: الكلام مشير إلى أن فرض الوقت هو الظهر في حق المعذور وغيره، لكنه مأمور بإسقاطه بأداء الجمعة حتماً، والمعذور له رخصة، فالجمعة ليست بدلاً عن الظهر؛ لأن حقيقة البدل ما يصار إليه
And walking to Friday prayer is obligatory, and leaving sale after the first adhan is the correct view. And when the imam comes out, there is no prayer, no speech, nor returning salaam, nor responding to a sneeze, whether worldly or religious, until he finishes his prayer. And it is disliked for one attending the sermon to eat, drink, play, or turn away, and al-Kamal said: it is forbidden. And the khatib should not greet the people when he ascends the minbar. And it is disliked to exit the city after the call unless one has prayed. And whoever is not obligated to attend Friday prayer, if he performs it, it suffices for the obligatory prayer of the time, meaning as long as he hears the people: and he recites aloud in the second [rak'ah] but not in the first. And walking to Friday etc. meant going on foot with calmness and dignity, not rushing, because it removes the dignity of the believer, and walking is better for one who can do it. And they differed regarding returning: it is said it is like going to it, so walking is better; and it is said it is like going out for other needs, and this is the correct view. And al-Tahawi said: the considered [adhan] is the second adhan at the minbar, because that was in his time and the time of the two shaykhs after him. He said in al-Bahr: it is weak. And when he comes out etc.: i.e. from his room if there is one, otherwise his standing for ascent is decisive, so the prohibition is established as soon as he appears, even before he ascends the minbar; and it is said: when he ascends. And he negated prayer, which includes if it is a make-up prayer, a funeral prayer, a prostration of recitation, a vowed prayer, or a supererogatory prayer, except if one remembers a missed prayer, even witr, and he is one who observes order, then starting them is not disliked at that time, rather it is obligatory for the necessity of the validity of Friday. And it indicates that starting before the imam comes out is not disliked, so he completes what he started even if the imam delivers the sermon without any dislike absolutely, except if it is a supererogatory prayer; then he completes two rak'ahs then stops. And if the imam's coming out is after his standing for the third, he also completes it because the second two rak'ahs become obligatory by standing for them. And there is disagreement about the sunnah of Friday: it is said he stops after two rak'ahs like an absolute supererogatory, and the correct view is that he completes it because it is like an obligatory prayer. And not returning salaam: he made it absolute, so it includes whether by tongue or heart, before or after the imam finishes, and by greeting he commits a sin. And it is disliked to exit [for one upon whom Friday is obligatory, he made the dislike general so it is prohibitively disliked, and we excluded those upon whom Friday is not obligatory, so there is no dislike in their exit after the call: i.e. the first adhan, and it is said: the second. And those upon whom Friday is not obligatory are: the sick, the traveler, the slave, the woman, the blind, and the cripple. The obligatory prayer of the time: al-Qahistani said: the discourse indicates that the obligatory prayer of the time is zuhr for the excused and others, but he is commanded to drop it by performing Friday necessarily, and the excused has a concession, so Friday is not a substitute for zuhr, because the reality of substitute is that which is resorted to
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage covers the obligations and prohibitions related to attending Friday prayer. It states that walking to the mosque for Friday prayer is obligatory (wajib), and after the first adhan, selling is prohibited. Once the imam emerges, all prayer, speech, returning greetings, and responding to sneezes are forbidden until the prayer ends. Those attending the sermon should not eat, drink, or engage in distracting actions; al-Kamal even says it is haram. The khatib should not greet the people when he mounts the minbar. It is disliked to leave the city after the call unless one has prayed. For those not obligated (such as the sick, traveler, slave, woman, blind, crippled), if they perform Friday prayer, it counts for the obligatory time (zuhr). The commentary then expands: the proper manner is to walk calmly, not rush. There is a dispute about the way of returning; the correct view is that it is like going out for other needs. A key intra-madhhab dispute concerns which adhan triggers the prohibition: al-Tahawi considers the second adhan at the minbar as the criterion, but this is deemed weak. The text details when the prohibition of starting additional prayers begins—upon the imam's appearance, or when he ascends—and what types of prayers are included. It also discusses the sunnah of Friday prayer: the correct view is that one completes the two rak'ahs (like a normal sunnah) rather than cutting them short. Finally, those exempt from Friday prayer are listed, and it is clarified that Friday prayer is not a substitute for zuhr; rather, the obligation of zuhr is dropped by performing Friday.

Key Terms
السعي (al-sa'y): Walking to the Friday prayer; it is obligatory to attend.
الأذان الأول (al-adhan al-awwal): The first call to prayer on Friday, which triggers the prohibition of sale and travel.
الجمعة (al-jumu'ah): The Friday congregational prayer; obligatory on those who meet specific conditions.
الأصح (al-ashahh): The more correct view; used to indicate the relied-upon opinion within the school.
النداء (al-nida'): The call to prayer (adhan) on Friday; here it refers to the first adhan or second depending on the view.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does the prohibition of sale on Friday begin in the relied-upon Hanafi view?
A) When the imam ascends the minbar
B) With the first adhan
C) With the second adhan
D) At the start of the khutbah

Key Takeaway
The first adhan triggers the prohibition of sale and travel; al-Tahawi's view favoring the second adhan is considered weak, and the mufta bihi is the first adhan.

Salah — Prayer

Rulings and Etiquettes of Jumu'ah Prayer
Lists obligations and prohibitions for Friday prayer and khutbah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligations, prohibitions, and etiquettes of Jumu'ah prayer, and identify the Hanafi position on which adhan triggers the prohibition of buying and selling.

Core Idea
Striving to attend Jumu'ah is wajib; after the first adhan, worldly activities are prohibited until the prayer ends.

The Friday prayer (Jumu'ah) has specific obligatory and prohibited actions that differ from other prayers. Understanding these rules ensures that the congregation observes the proper etiquettes and avoids invalidating the prayer or incurring sin. This lesson covers the main rulings from the Hanafi school, including the debate over which adhan marks the start of the prohibition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the obligations (wajibat) of Jumu'ah
List the actions that are required: hearing the khutbah, shortening it, and striving (sa'y) to attend.
These are stated at the beginning of the passage.
2
Identify the prohibitions (muharramat) of Jumu'ah
List what is forbidden: buying/selling after the first adhan, speech and any prayer after the imam emerges, eating/drinking during the khutbah, etc.
Note the dispute on the adhan discussed later.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on which adhan is considered
Contrast the two views: the first adhan (al-ashah) versus the second adhan (al-Tahawi). Understand the practical difference.
The preferred view is the first adhan.
4
Synthesize the etiquettes (adab) of attending Jumu'ah
Note the recommended behaviours: walking calmly with dignity, completing supererogatory prayers before imam appears, and proper conduct during khutbah.
Also covers returning from Jumu'ah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحكام الجمعة وأن يسمع القوم الخطبة، وتخفيف الخطبتين بقدر سورة من طوال المفصل، ويكره التطويل وترك شيء من السنن، ويجب السعي للجمعة، وترك البيع بالأذان الأول في الأصح، وإذا خرج الإمام فلا صلاة ولا كلام ولا يرد سلاماً، ولا يُشَمِّتُ عاطساً دنيويا أو دينيا حتى يفرغ من صلاته وكره الحاضر الخطبة الأكل والشرب والعبث والالتفات وقال الكمال: يحرم ولا يسلم الخطيب على القوم إذا استوى على المنبر، وكره الخروج من المصر بعد النداء ما لم يصل، بمعى ما دام يسمع القوم: ويجهر في الثانية دون الأولى. ويجب السعي إلخ أراد الذهاب ماشياً بالسكينة والوقار لا الهرولة؛ لأنها تذهب بهاء المؤمن والمشي أفضل لمن يقدر عليه مراقي الفلاح: ٥١٦] . واختلفوا في الرجوع، فقيل: هو كالذهاب إليها فالمشي أفضل، وقيل: هو كالخروج إلى سائر الحاجات، وهو الأصح. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥١٦] الأصح وقال الطحاوي: المعتبر هو الأذان الثاني عند المنبر ؛ لأنه الذي كان في زمنه والشيخين بعده، قال في "البحر" : وهو ضعيف. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥١٨] وإذا خرج إلخ : أي من حجرته إن كانت وإلا فقيامه للصعود قاطع فيثبت المنع بمجرد ظهوره ولو قبل صعوده المنبر، وقيل: إذا صعد، ونفى الصلاة فشمل ما إذا كانت قضاء فائتة أو صلاة جنازة أو سجدة تلاوة أو منذورة أو نفلاً، إلا إذا تذكر فائتة ولو وتراً وهو صاحب ترتيب فلا يكره الشروع فيهما حينئذ، بل يجب لضرورة صحة الجمعة، وأفاد أنه لا يكره الشروع قبل الخروج، فيتم ما شرع فيه ولو خطب الإمام من غير كراهة مطلقاً، إلا إذا كان في نفل؛ فإنه يتم شفعاً ثم يقطع، ولو كان خروجه بعد القيام للثالثة أتم أيضاً؛ لأنه وجب عليه الشفع الثاني بالقيام إليه، واختلف في سنة ،الجمعة، فقيل: يقطع على رأس الركعتين كالنفل المطلق، والصحيح أنه يتمها؛ لأنه كصلاة واجبة. [حاشية الطحطاوي ومراقي الفلاح بتغيير: ٥١٨] ولا يرد سلاماً : أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان بلسانه أو بقلبه قبل الفراغ أو بعده، ويرتكب بسلامه إثماً. وكره الخروج [أي لمن تجب عليه الجمعة أطلق الكراهة فتكون تحريمية وأخرجنا من لا تجب عليه الجمعة، فلا كراهة في خروجه بعد النداء: أي الأذان الأول، وقيل: الثاني. [مراقي الفلاح: ٥٢٠]
The rulings of Jumu'ah: And that the people hear the khutbah, and shortening the two khutbahs to the extent of a surah from the long ones of al-Mufassal, and it is disliked to lengthen them and to omit any of the sunan. And striving to attend Jumu'ah is obligatory, and leaving buying and selling at the first adhan in the most correct view. And when the imam comes out, there is no prayer, no speech, and he does not return a greeting, nor does he say yarhamuk Allah to a sneezer, whether worldly or religious, until he finishes his prayer. And it is disliked for the attendee of the khutbah to eat, drink, play, and turn away, and al-Kamal said: it is forbidden. And the khatib should not greet the people when he ascends the minbar. And it is disliked to leave the city after the call to prayer as long as he has not prayed. 'As long as the people hear' and he makes it audible in the second but not the first. And 'striving to attend' means going walking with calmness and dignity, not rushing, because it removes the dignity of the believer, and walking is better for one who is able. 'Maraqi al-Falah: 516'. And they differed regarding the return: it is said it is like going to it so walking is better, and it is said it is like going out for other needs, and that is the most correct. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 516] The most correct: And al-Tahawi said: the consideration is the second adhan at the minbar because it was during his time and the two shaykhs after him. He said in 'al-Bahr': it is weak. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 518] And 'when the imam comes out' etc.: meaning from his room if he has one, otherwise his standing to ascend is a preventer, so the prohibition is established merely by his appearance even before ascending the minbar, and it is said: when he ascends. And 'no prayer' includes whether it is a make-up of a missed prayer, a funeral prayer, a prostration of recitation, a vowed prayer, or a supererogatory prayer, except if he remembers a missed prayer even witr while he is one who observes order, then it is not disliked to begin them at that time, rather it is obligatory due to the necessity of the validity of Jumu'ah. And it indicates that it is not disliked to begin before his coming out, so he completes what he has begun even if the imam is giving the khutbah without any dislike absolutely, except if it is a supererogatory prayer; then he completes two rak'ahs and then cuts off. And if his coming out is after standing for the third, he also completes because the second two rak'ahs became obligatory upon him by standing for them. And they differed regarding the sunnah of Jumu'ah: it is said he cuts off at the completion of two rak'ahs like an absolute supererogatory prayer, and the correct view is that he completes it because it is like an obligatory prayer. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi and Maraqi al-Falah with modification: 518] And 'he does not return a greeting': He made it general, including whether it is with his tongue or his heart before or after finishing, and by his greeting he commits a sin. And 'it is disliked to leave' [meaning for the one upon whom Jumu'ah is obligatory, he made the dislike unrestricted so it is prohibitively disliked, and we exclude those upon whom Jumu'ah is not obligatory, so there is no dislike in their leaving after the call: meaning the first adhan, and it is said the second. [Maraqi al-Falah: 520]
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_statement from the matn of Nur al-Idah, expanded by commentary from Maraqi al-Falah and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi. It covers the key obligations and etiquettes of Friday prayer. The author begins by stating that the congregation must hear the khutbah, and the imam should keep the two khutbahs short, about the length of a medium surah. Lengthening or omitting sunan is disliked. The obligation to strive (sa'y) for Jumu'ah is emphasized; this means walking with calmness and dignity, not rushing. Then the prohibition of buying and selling after the first adhan is mentioned, though there is a dispute about which adhan is considered. When the imam emerges, all prayers, speech, and even returning greetings are prohibited. The commentary clarifies that 'no prayer' includes all types, but if one has started a supererogatory prayer, he should complete two rak'ahs then stop. The dispute about the sunnah of Jumu'ah is resolved by the correct view that it should be completed. Leaving the city after the adhan is disliked for those obligated, but not for others. The ruling that it is forbidden (haram) to eat, drink, etc. during the khutbah is attributed to al-Kamal ibn al-Humam. The passage then details the prohibition of the khatib greeting when he ascends the minbar. The madhhab adopts the view that the second adhan at the minbar is the one that matters, though this is considered weak by some.

Key Terms
الجمعة (al-jumu'ah): The Friday congregational prayer that replaces the noon (zuhr) prayer on Fridays, obligatory upon free, adult, resident, male Muslims.
السعي (al-sa'y): Striving or proceeding to the Friday prayer, with calmness and dignity, not rushing.
الأذان (al-adhan): The call to prayer. In the context of Jumu'ah, there are two adhans: the first is the general call before the khutbah, the second is at the minbar just before the khutbah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The second adhan at the minbar
C) Both adhans equally
D) Neither, buying and selling is always permitted

Key Takeaway
The first adhan triggers the prohibition of worldly transactions; from the moment the imam appears until the prayer ends, all speech, prayers, and unnecessary actions are prohibited.

Jumu'ah and Dhuhr: An Independent Obligation, Not a Substitute
Defining the legal relationship between Jumu'ah and Dhuhr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafis consider Jumu'ah as an independent fard rather than a substitute for Dhuhr, and apply this distinction to identify when Dhuhr becomes obligatory.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah is an independent obligation that drops Dhuhr; Dhuhr remains the fard of the time.

This passage from Nur al-Idah, with commentary by al-Qahistani, clarifies a key Hanafi principle: Jumu'ah is not a mere replacement (badal) for Dhuhr, but an independent fard that, when validly performed, lifts the Dhuhr obligation. Understanding this distinction affects rulings for those who are excused from Jumu'ah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the matn's ruling
Read the matn: 'وَمَنْ لَا جُمُعَةَ عَلَيْهِ إِنْ أَدَّاهَا جَازَ عَنْ فَرْضِ الْوَقْتِ' – that is, if someone not obligated performs Jumu'ah, it suffices for the fard of the time.
The fard of the time is the obligatory prayer at that moment.
2
Recognize the conceptual question
The passage asks: Is Jumu'ah a substitute (badal) for Dhuhr? Al-Qahistani explains why it is not.
3
Analyze the definition of badal
Al-Qahistani defines badal as something resorted to when the original is impossible. But here, Jumu'ah is not resorted to because Dhuhr is impossible; both are possible, but Jumu'ah is commanded for those with capacity.
Thus Jumu'ah is not a replacement; it is an independent obligation.
4
Understand the relationship
Dhuhr is the fard al-waqt (the underlying obligation). Jumu'ah, when performed, drops (yusqitu) the Dhuhr obligation. It is a distinct fard that fulfills the time's requirement.
The benefit: if someone cannot do Jumu'ah, they fall back on Dhuhr.
5
Apply to the excused case
For those excused (traveler, sick, etc.), if they choose to do Jumu'ah, it counts as fulfilling the fard of the time. If not, they pray Dhuhr as usual.
This shows Jumu'ah is not a substitute; the default is Dhuhr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن لا جمعة عليه إن أدّاها جاز عن فرض الوقت. فرض الوقت: قال القهستاني: الكلام مشير إلى أن فرض الوقت هو الظهر في حق المعذور وغيره، لكنه مأمور بإسقاطه بأداء الجمعة حتماً، والمعذور له رخصة، فالجمعة ليست بدلاً عن الظهر؛ لأن حقيقة البدل ما يصار إليه = عند تعذر الأصل، وليس هذا كذلك، وليس الظهر بدلاً عنها؛ لأنه هو فرض الوقت، بل هي فرض مستقل في ذلك اليوم يسقط به الظهر، وفائدة هذا الوجوب جواز المصير إليه عند العجز عن الجمعة حاشية الطحطاوي بحذف: ٥٢١]
And whoever is not obligated to attend Jumu'ah, if he performs it, it suffices for the fard of the time. The fard of the time: al-Qahistani said: The speech indicates that the fard of the time is Dhuhr for the excused and others, but he is commanded to drop it by performing Jumu'ah necessarily, and the excused has a concession. So Jumu'ah is not a replacement for Dhuhr, because the reality of a replacement is to resort to it when the original is inaccessible, and this is not so. And Dhuhr is not a replacement for it, because it is the fard of the time, but it (Jumu'ah) is an independent obligation on that day by which Dhuhr is dropped, and the benefit of this obligation is the permissibility of resorting to it (Dhuhr) when unable to perform Jumu'ah. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi with deletion: 521]
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof based on rational argument (talil). It clarifies the legal relationship between Jumu'ah and Dhuhr. The matn states that if someone not obligated to attend Jumu'ah (like a traveler, sick person, slave, woman, blind, disabled) chooses to pray Jumu'ah, it suffices for the fard of that time. The commentator al-Qahistani explains that the fard of the time is actually Dhuhr for everyone, but for those with the capacity, they are commanded to perform Jumu'ah instead, which drops the obligation of Dhuhr. The excused have a license to pray Dhuhr. Jumu'ah is not a 'badal' (replacement/substitute) for Dhuhr, because a substitute is resorted to when the original is impossible—here, Jumu'ah is not a substitute but an independent obligation. Dhuhr is not a substitute for Jumu'ah either; it remains the original fard of the time. The key point is that Jumu'ah is a distinct fard that, when performed, fulfills the requirement for that time slot. The benefit of this distinction is that if someone who is obligated becomes unable to attend Jumu'ah, he falls back on Dhuhr (which was always the underlying fard).

Key Terms
فرض الوقت (fard al-waqt): The obligatory prayer at a given time; here it means that the fundamental obligation for the Friday time slot is Dhuhr, but it is lifted by performing Jumu'ah.
بدل (badal): A replacement or substitute for an original obligation when the original is impossible to perform.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi text, if a traveler (who is not obligated for Jumu'ah) chooses to perform Jumu'ah, what is the legal effect?
A) His Jumu'ah is invalid because he is not obligated.
B) It suffices for the fard of that time, i.e., he does not need to pray Dhuhr.
C) He must still pray Dhuhr because Jumu'ah does not count for him.
D) His Jumu'ah becomes a supererogatory prayer.

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah is an independent fard that drops Dhuhr, but Dhuhr remains the fard of the time; Jumu'ah is not a badal.

When Does Dhuhr Become Invalid After Setting Out for Jumu'ah?
Ruling with proof explaining when Dhuhr is invalidated.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which a Dhuhr prayer becomes invalid when one later goes to Jumu'ah, and explain the Hanafi ruling on the definition of 'sa'y'.

Core Idea
Dhuhr becomes invalid only when one physically leaves home for Jumu'ah with hope of catching it.

This lesson explores a nuanced ruling in Hanafi fiqh about the invalidation of a Dhuhr prayer when the worshipper later decides to attend Jumu'ah. The key is understanding the precise moment of invalidation and the definition of 'sa'y' (striving). We'll examine the chosen view from the text and its application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act: praying Dhuhr alone before Jumu'ah, then setting out for Jumu'ah. The ruling: Dhuhr becomes invalid (batil) under certain conditions.
2
Define the key term 'sa'y'
The text resolves the intra-Hanafi dispute: the chosen view is that sa'y means leaving one's home.
It is not merely intending or arriving.
3
State the condition for invalidation
Invalidation occurs when one leaves home hoping to catch Jumu'ah, regardless of whether he actually catches it.
The text says: 'بأن كان يرجو إدراكها' (hoping to catch it).
4
Note the exceptions
If you are still in the mosque, or go out for another purpose, or after the imam finished, Dhuhr remains valid.
These are explicit in the text.
5
Consider the follower's case
If the imam sets out but the follower does not, the follower's Dhuhr stays valid; the imam's invalidation does not transfer.
Because the imam's Dhuhr became invalid after completion, the follower's prayer is independent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن سعى إليها: اختلفوا في معنى السعي إليها، والمختار أنه الانفصال عن داره حتى لا يبطل قبله على المختار، وقيد بقوله "سعى"؛ لأنه لو كان جالساً في المسجد بعد ما صلى الظهر، فإنه لا يبطل حتى يشرع مع الإمام اتفاقاً، وقيد بقوله "إليها"؛ لأنه لو خرج لحاجة أو خرج وقد فرغ الإمام لم يبطل ظهره إجماعاً، فالبطلان به مقيد بما إذا كان يرجو إدراكها بأن خرج والإمام فيها أو لم يكن ،شرع أطلق فشمل ما إذا لم يدركها لبعد مع كون الإمام فيها وقت الخروج أو لم يكن شرع. ثم اعلم أن الضمير المستتر في قوله: "سعى" يعود إلى مصلي الظهر لا إلى من لا عذر له ليكون أفيد وأشمل، فإنه لا فرق بين المعذور وغيره في بطلان ظهره ،بسعيه وقيد بسعي المصلي؛ لأن المأموم لو لم يسع إليها وسعى إمامه، فإنه لا يبطل ظهر المأموم وإن بطل ظهر إمامه؛ لأن بطلانه في حق الإمام بعد الفراغ، فلا يضر المأموم. البحر الرائق بحذف: ۲۳۹/٢]
Then if he strives to it (Jumu'ah): They differed regarding the meaning of striving to it, and the chosen view is that it is separating from his home, so that it does not become invalid before that according to the chosen view. And it is restricted by his saying 'strive' because if he was sitting in the mosque after praying Dhuhr, then it does not become invalid until he begins with the imam, by agreement. And it is restricted by his saying 'to it' because if he went out for a need or went out after the imam had finished, his Dhuhr does not become invalid by consensus. So invalidity by it is conditional on his hoping to catch it, i.e., he went out while the imam was still in it, or had not begun. So it is absolute, including if he does not catch it due to distance while the imam was in it at the time of going out, or had not begun. Then know that the implicit pronoun in his saying 'strive' refers to the person praying Dhuhr, not to the one who has no excuse, to be more beneficial and general. For there is no difference between the excused and the non-excused in the invalidity of his Dhuhr by his striving. And it is restricted by the striving of the pray-er, because if the follower did not strive to it but his imam strove, then the follower's Dhuhr does not become invalid, even if the imam's Dhuhr becomes invalid, because its invalidity in the imam's case is after completion, so it does not harm the follower. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq with deletion: 239/2]
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (talil) and includes an intra-Hanafi dispute. It explains the scenario where a person prays Dhuhr individually before the Friday prayer, then decides to go to the mosque for Jumu'ah. The key issue is: when does his Dhuhr become invalid? The text resolves the disagreement on the meaning of 'sa'y' (striving): the chosen view is that it means leaving his home (i.e., starting to go). If he is still sitting in the mosque after praying Dhuhr, his Dhuhr remains valid until he actually begins to follow the imam in Jumu'ah prayer. The invalidity only occurs if he sets out with the hope of catching the Jumu'ah. If he goes out for a different purpose or after the imam has finished, his Dhuhr remains valid. This ruling applies equally to those who are obligated and those who are excused (like a traveler) if they had prayed Dhuhr first. However, the invalidity is tied to the individual's own action; if a follower does not himself set out but his imam does, the follower's Dhuhr is not invalidated because the imam's prayer becomes invalid only after completion and does not affect the follower. This is based on the principle that the follower's prayer is independent once he has prayed.

Key Terms
السعي (al-sa'y): Leaving one's home to go to the Friday prayer; the chosen view defines it as separating from the house.
بطلان الظهر (butlan al-zuhr): Invalidation of the Dhuhr prayer that was already performed; it becomes as if it was not performed, requiring a new prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the chosen view in the text, when does the Dhuhr prayer become invalid for someone who prayed it and later goes to Jumu'ah?
A) When he intends to go to Jumu'ah
B) When he leaves his house to go to Jumu'ah
C) When he reaches the mosque and joins the imam
D) When he finishes the Jumu'ah prayer

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling: a Dhuhr prayer becomes invalid if one leaves his home intending to catch Jumu'ah, even if he does not actually catch it.

Dislike of Congregational Dhuhr for the Excused and Sujud al-Sahw in Jumu'ah
Ruling on it being disliked for the excused to pray Dhuhr in congregation on Friday, and on sujud al-sahw in Jumu'ah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on congregational Dhuhr for the excused on Friday and explain the Hanafi position on sujud al-sahw in Jumu'ah and Eid.

Core Idea
For the excused, praying Dhuhr in congregation on Friday is severely disliked; sujud al-sahw in Jumu'ah and Eid should be left to avoid fitnah.

This passage from Nur al-Idah presents two distinct rulings related to Friday prayers. First, it addresses those who are excused from Jumu'ah (such as the sick, traveler, or slave) and prisoners, stating that if they perform the Dhuhr prayer in congregation on Friday, it is disliked (makruh). Second, it discusses the issue of sujud al-sahw (prostration for forgetfulness) during Jumu'ah and Eid prayers, clarifying that the preferred Hanafi view is to omit it. We will unpack the reasoning behind both rulings and their practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
Read the passage and identify the two separate hukms: (1) dislike of congregational Dhuhr for the excused on Friday, and (2) the ruling on sujud al-sahw in Jumu'ah and Eid.
2
Analyze the first ruling: dislike of congregational Dhuhr
Focus on the condition 'in the city' and the exception for villagers. Understand why it is disliked but the prayer remains valid. Note the mention of prisoners and the recommended action to delay or pray alone.
The text indicates the dislike is severe (makruh tahrimi).
3
Understand the second ruling: sujud al-sahw in Jumu'ah and Eid
Examine the objection and response. Why does the chosen view say it is better to leave sujud al-sahw in these prayers? The reason given is 'lest people fall into fitnah'.
The ruling applies to both Jumu'ah and Eid prayers.
4
Distinguish between validity and hatefulness
Note that even though the act is disliked, the prayer is still valid because all conditions are met. This is a key fiqh principle: karaha does not render the prayer invalid.
The text explicitly states 'أفاد بالكراهة أن الصلاة صحيحة'.
5
Apply the rulings to modern scenarios
Consider a sick person or a traveler on Friday. Should they join a Dhuhr congregation? According to this ruling, it is better for them to pray alone. Also, if an imam forgets a prostration during Jumu'ah, he should not perform sujud al-sahw to avoid confusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكره للمعذور والمسجون أداء الظهر بجماعة في المصر يومها، ومن و صلية كمريض ورقيق ومسافر وكذا؟ [؟] قيد بـ"المصر"؛ لأن الجماعة غير مكروهة في حق أهل السواد؛ لأنه لا جمعة عليهم، أفاد بالكراهة أن الصلاة صحيحة لاستجماع شرائطها، ولو حذف المصنف المعذور والمسجون لكان أولى، فإن أداء الظهر بجماعة مكروه يوم الجمعة مطلقاً، ولو زاد وأداؤه منفرداً قبل صلاة "الإمام" لكان أولى؛ لما في "الخلاصة": ويستحب للمريض أن يؤخر الصلاة إلى أن يفرغ الإمام من صلاة الجمعة، وإن لم يؤخره يكره، هو الصحيح، وإنما صرح بـ"المسجون مع دخوله في المعذور للاختلاف في أهل السجن، فإن في السراج الوهاج": أن المسجونين إن كانوا ظلمة قدروا على إرضاء الخصوم، وإن كانوا مظلومين أمكنهم الاستغاثة، كان عليهم حضور بـ"الجماعة"؛ لما في "التفاريق": أن المعذور يصلي الظهر بأذان وإقامة وإن كان لا تستحب الجماعة، وقيد بـ " الظهر"؛ لأن في غيرها لا بأس أن يصلوا جماعة البحر الرائق بحذف: ٢٤١/٢] سجود السهو : إن قيل: إن هذا يشعر بأنه يسجد للسهو في الجمعة ،والعيد وهو خلاف المختار، أجيب بأن المختار عدم الوجوب فيهما وأن الأولى تركه؛ لئلا يقع الناس في فتنة، لا أن المختار عدم جوازه [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥٢٢]
And it is disliked for the excused and the prisoner to perform Dhuhr in congregation in the city on that day, and whoever prays? like a sick person, slave, traveler, etc. It is restricted by 'the city' because congregation is not disliked for the people of the countryside, because there is no Jumu'ah upon them. It indicates by the dislike that the prayer is valid due to meeting its conditions. And if the author had omitted the excused and the prisoner it would have been better, because performing Dhuhr in congregation is disliked on Friday absolutely. And if he added and performing it alone before the imam's prayer would be better; because in al-Khulasa: It is recommended for the sick person to delay the prayer until the imam finishes the Jumu'ah prayer, and if he does not delay, it is disliked; that is the correct view. And he specifically mentioned 'prisoner' even though it is included in the excused, due to the disagreement regarding the people of the prison. For in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: that if the prisoners are oppressors, they are able to satisfy the claimants, and if they are oppressed, they can seek help, so they were required to attend the congregation. In al-Tafariq: that the excused prays Dhuhr with adhan and iqamah even though congregation is not recommended. And it is restricted by 'Dhuhr' because in other prayers there is no harm in praying in congregation. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq with deletion: 241/2] Sujud al-sahw: If it is said: this indicates that he performs sujud al-sahw in Jumu'ah and Eid, and that is contrary to the chosen view. The answer is that the chosen view is that it is not obligatory in them, and it is better to leave it, lest people fall into fitnah, not that the chosen view is that it is not permissible. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 522]
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage contains two distinct rulings. First, it is disliked (makruh) for those excused from Jumu'ah (sick, traveler, slave, etc.) and for prisoners to perform the Dhuhr prayer in congregation on Friday within the city. The commentary explains that this dislike is restricted to the city; in villages where Jumu'ah is not held, congregational Dhuhr is not disliked. Even though the prayer is valid, it is better for these individuals to pray Dhuhr alone or delay it until after the imam finishes Jumu'ah. The mention of prisoners is because some scholars argued they might be able to attend Jumu'ah, but the text holds they are excused. The second ruling concerns sujud al-sahw (prostration for forgetfulness) during Jumu'ah and Eid prayers. The chosen view in the Hanafi school is that it is not obligatory to perform sujud al-sahw in these prayers; rather, it is better to omit it altogether to avoid confusion and fitnah among the congregation who may not understand why the imam is prostrating after the prayer. However, if someone does perform it, it is not prohibited.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): The two prostrations performed to compensate for forgetfulness in prayer; in Jumu'ah and Eid, the chosen view is to avoid it.
المعذور (al-ma'dhur): One who has a valid excuse preventing attendance at Jumu'ah, such as illness, being a slave, travel, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling regarding sujud al-sahw in Jumu'ah according to the chosen view in the text?
A) It is obligatory as in other prayers
B) It is not obligatory, and it is better to omit it
C) It is prohibited
D) It is recommended

Key Takeaway
For the excused, congregational Dhuhr on Friday is severely disliked but valid; sujud al-sahw in Jumu'ah and Eid is not obligatory and should be omitted to avoid fitnah.

Invalidation of Zuhr Before Friday Prayer: Conditions and Rulings
Ruling statement with commentary expansion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a Zuhr prayer performed before Friday prayer becomes invalid, and distinguish when it is merely disliked for excused persons.

Core Idea
Zuhr before Friday is invalid only if you physically depart while the imam is engaged.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the Friday prayer. The central issue: what happens if someone prays Zuhr on Friday before the Friday congregation, and then proceeds to join the Friday prayer? The matn and its commentary clarify when that earlier Zuhr is nullified and when it remains valid. Understanding these conditions is important for anyone who may face this situation or needs to advise others.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Read the first line: 'Whoever has no excuse and prays Zuhr before it [Friday prayer] commits a sin (haram).' This establishes that performing Zuhr before Friday without a valid excuse is prohibited in itself.
The prohibition is independent of whether Zuhr becomes invalid later.
2
Locate the condition for invalidation
The text then states: 'Then if he proceeds towards it while the imam is engaged in it, his Zuhr becomes invalid.' Identify the three conditions: (1) the person had prayed Zuhr, (2) he proceeds (physically departs), (3) the imam is already engaged in Friday prayer at the time of departure.
The commentary specifies 'proceeding' means departure from home, not mere intention.
3
Analyze the scope of invalidation
The commentary expands: even if the person fails to catch the Friday prayer (due to distance), his Zuhr is invalid if he set out while the imam was engaged. Also, the ruling applies equally to those with and without excuse – the invalidation depends on the act of proceeding, not the excuse status.
This shows the invalidation is a penalty for abandoning the Friday obligation by proceeding after having prayed Zuhr.
4
Distinguish the disliked case for excused persons
The matn adds: 'It is disliked for the excused person and the prisoner to perform Zuhr in congregation in the city on that day.' Understand that for those excused (sick, slave, traveler), praying Zuhr in congregation is makruh tanzihan, but the prayer itself is valid. Rural dwellers not obligated to Friday are exempt from this dislike.
The commentary justifies this to avoid confusion and fitna, and notes the preferred view regarding prostration of forgetfulness in Friday/Eid prayers.

الجماعة، وقيد
The Book of Prayer. Rulings of Friday. Whoever has no excuse and prays Zuhr before it [Friday prayer] commits a sin (haram). Then if he proceeds towards it [the Friday prayer] while the imam is engaged in it, his Zuhr becomes invalid. 'Before the Friday prayer' means 'to the Friday prayer'. Even if he does not catch it. And it is disliked (makruh) for the excused person and the prisoner to perform Zuhr in congregation in the city on that day. And the excused include the sick, the slave, and the traveler. Whoever catches it in the tashahhud or in the prostration of forgetfulness completes the Friday prayer. And Allah knows best. [Commentary:] 'Then if he proceeds' ... The meaning of 'proceeding' is departing from his house, so that it does not invalidate before that according to the preferred view. The condition 'proceeds' is because if he was sitting in the mosque after praying Zuhr, it does not become invalid until he begins with the imam by agreement. The condition 'to it' is because if he went out for a need or went out after the imam had finished, his Zuhr is not invalid by consensus. So invalidation is restricted to when he hopes to catch it, by going out while the imam is engaged, or even if he does not catch it due to distance while the imam was engaged at the time of going out. Then know that the implicit pronoun in 'proceeds' refers to the one who prayed Zuhr, not to the one without excuse, to be more beneficial and comprehensive, for there is no difference between the excused and others in the invalidation of his Zuhr by his proceeding. It is restricted to the proceeding of the one who prayed because if the follower did not proceed but his imam proceeded, the follower's Zuhr is not invalidated even if the imam's Zuhr becomes invalid; because its invalidation in the imam's case occurs after completion, so it does not harm the follower. (Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq abridged: 2/239). 'And it is disliked for the excused etc.' is restricted to 'the city' because congregation is not disliked for rural dwellers, as there is no Friday prayer upon them. The mention of 'disliked' indicates the prayer is valid because its conditions are met. If the author had omitted 'excused' and 'prisoner' it would be better, for performing Zuhr in congregation on Friday is disliked absolutely. If he added 'and performing it alone before the imam's prayer' it would be better; as in al-Khulasa: It is recommended for the sick to delay the prayer until the imam finishes the Friday prayer; if he does not delay, it is disliked – that is correct. He specifically mentioned 'prisoner' although he is included in 'excused' because of a difference regarding prison inmates. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: If the prisoners are oppressors able to satisfy the claimants, or if they are oppressed able to seek help, they must attend the congregation. (Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq abridged: 2/241). Prostration of forgetfulness: If it is said that this suggests prostrating for forgetfulness in Friday and Eid prayer – contrary to the preferred view – the answer is that the preferred view is that it is not obligatory, and it is better to omit it to avoid fitna, not that it is impermissible. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 522). The congregation, and restricted.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage from the matn of Nur al-Idah, with its commentary expansion, addresses the rulings concerning a person who prays Zuhr on Friday before the Friday prayer. The core ruling: For a person with no valid excuse, it is haram to pray Zuhr before Friday prayer. If such a person then proceeds towards the Friday congregation while the imam is already engaged in the Friday prayer, his earlier Zuhr prayer becomes invalid – meaning it is nullified and he must still join the Friday prayer. The commentary clarifies key terms: 'proceeds' (sa'a) means physically departing from one's residence towards the Friday prayer; mere intention or sitting in the mosque after praying Zuhr does not cause invalidation. The invalidation occurs only if he goes out with the hope of catching the Friday prayer (i.e., while the imam is still praying or has started). Even if he fails to catch it due to distance, his Zuhr is invalidated if he set out while the imam was engaged. Importantly, this applies equally to those with and without excuse – the invalidation is tied to the act of proceeding, not the excuse status. For the excused (sick, slave, traveler) and prisoners, it is disliked (makruh tanzihan) for them to pray Zuhr in congregation in the city on Friday, though the prayer itself is valid. For rural dwellers (ahl al-sawad) who are not obligated to Friday, performing Zuhr in congregation is not disliked. The commentary also addresses the prostration of forgetfulness in Friday and Eid prayers: the preferred Hanafi position is that it is not obligatory and is better omitted to avoid confusion, though it is not impermissible. This reflects the Hanafi concern for practical ease (raf' al-haraj) in congregational settings.

Key Terms
سعى (sa'a): Physically departing from one's residence towards the Friday prayer; not mere intention.
المعذور (al-madhhur): A person with a valid excuse such as illness, slavery, or travel, exempting them from Friday prayer obligation.
الأصح (al-asahh): The most correct or preferred opinion within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The person must have no excuse.
B) The person must physically depart towards the Friday prayer while the imam is engaged.
C) The person must fail to catch the Friday prayer.
D) The person must be a resident of the city.

Key Takeaway
Zuhr before Friday is invalid only if one physically departs while the imam is engaged; otherwise it remains valid, and for the excused, praying in congregation is disliked but valid.

Eid Prayer: Wajib or Sunnah? The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
States the relied-upon ruling that Eid prayer is obligatory and discusses the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Eid prayer, identify the intra-Hanafi disagreement, and explain the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Eid prayer is wajib in the Hanafi school, not merely sunnah — a ruling that carries practical consequences for making it up.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on Eid prayer. The matn asserts that it is wajib (obligatory) in the most correct view, but a narration from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani considers it sunnah. We will unpack the dispute, the conditions for obligation, and the practical difference (thamarah) between these positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling in the matn
Read the matn: 'صلاة العيد واجبة في الأصح'. Note that the author states the ruling as wajib and qualifies it as 'al-asahh' (most correct). Identify the act: Eid prayer.
The matn is from Nur al-Idah, a standard Hanafi fiqh text.
2
Locate the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The commentary mentions a different narration from Imam Muhammad in al-Jami' al-Saghir that considers Eid prayer sunnah. This is the internal dispute.
Imam Muhammad is one of the two main disciples of Abu Hanifa.
3
Understand the basis for the conflicting view
Imam Muhammad's argument: when two Eids (Eid and Friday) coincide, the earlier is sunnah and the later is fard. This implies Eid is sunnah relative to Friday. However, the majority interprets this as a relative comparison, not a categorical ruling.
The opposing view within the school is based on a specific incident.
4
Determine the mufta bihi and its justification
Later Hanafi authorities (e.g., al-Hidayah, al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) confirm that the preferred view is wajib. The conditions for Eid prayer are similar to Friday but more lenient (e.g., congregation can be just imam+one).
The tarjih is based on the strength of the evidence and the practice of the early community.
5
Apply the thamarah (practical consequence)
If one misses Eid prayer, according to the wajib view, one must make it up (qada) as four rak'ahs individually. According to the sunnah view, no qada is required.
This shows the practical impact of the ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب العيدين
صلاة العيدين
صلاة العيد واجبة في الأصح على من تجب عليه الجمعة بشرائطها سوى الخطبة،
فتصح بدونها مع الإساءة كما لو قدمت الخطبة على صلاة العيد.
كما يكون مسيئاً
العيدين: سمي عيداً؛ لأن الله تعالى فيه عوائد الإحسان إلى عباده، دينية ودنيوية، أو لأنه يعود ويتكرر بالفرح والسرور، وتفاؤلا بالعود على من أدركه كما سميت القافلة تفاؤلاً بقفولها أي رجوعها، أو لاجتماع الناس فيه. [حاشية الطحطاوي ومراقي الفلاح: ٥٢٧] في الأصح وفي رواية أخرى أنها سنة؛ لقول محمد في "الجامع الصغير" في العيدين يجتمعان في يوم واحد قال يشهدهما جميعاً، ولا يترك واحداً منهما، والأولى منهما سنة، والأخرى فريضة. [البحر الرائق: ٢٤٧/٢] بشرائطها ظاهره أنه لابد من الجماعة المذكورة في الجمعة على خلاف فيها، وليس كذلك؛ فإن الواحد هنا مع الإمام جماعة، فكيف يصح أن يقال: "بشرائطها؟ [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٥٢٨]
Chapter of the Two Eids. Eid prayer: The Eid prayer is wajib (obligatory) in the most correct view upon those upon whom Friday prayer is obligatory, with its conditions except the khutbah. So it is valid without it [the khutbah] but with detestability (isaa'ah), just as if the khutbah is advanced before the Eid prayer. It is also considered doing wrong. [Commentary:] The two Eids: called 'Eid because Allah the Exalted in them renews favors to His servants, religious and worldly, or because it returns and repeats with joy and happiness, and as an omen of return for those who witness it... In the most correct view, and in another narration it is sunnah; because Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir regarding two Eids coinciding on one day: 'One should attend both and not leave either; the first is sunnah and the other is fard.' (Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 2/247). 'With its conditions' apparently requires the congregation as mentioned for Friday, but there is a difference; it is not so, for the individual here with the imam constitutes a congregation. So how can it be said 'with its conditions'? (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 528).
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage begins the chapter on the two Eids (Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha). The matn states that the Eid prayer is wajib (obligatory) according to the most correct view (al-asahh) in the Hanafi school. It is obligatory upon those who are obligated to attend Friday prayer (i.e., free, adult, male, resident, healthy), with the same conditions (such as being in a city, congregation, etc.), except for the khutbah (sermon) which is not a condition for validity – the prayer is valid even without the khutbah, though doing so is disliked. The commentary provides important intra-Hanafi information: there is a differing narration from Imam Muhammad (in al-Jami' al-Saghir) indicating that Eid prayer is sunnah. However, the relied-upon view is that it is wajib, as stated in the matn. The commentary also refines the condition of congregation: unlike Friday prayer which requires a large gathering (minimum 3 besides the imam in some views), for Eid prayer, merely the imam and one follower constitutes a congregation. Thus the condition is not identical to Friday's – it is more lenient. This reflects the Hanafi legal principle that Eid prayer, while similar to Friday in obligation, has its own rulings (khutbah not integral, congregation minimal). The passage also gives a linguistic explanation of the word 'Eid' (festival) as a day of recurring divine favors.

Key Terms
واجبة (wajibah): Obligatory in the Hanafi sense – a duty established by a zanni (speculative) proof, where omission is sinful but its denial is not kufr.
الأصح (al-asahh): The most correct or preferred opinion within the Hanafi school, used to resolve internal ikhtilaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi view, Eid prayer is:
A) Sunnah mu'akkadah
B) Wajib
C) Fard
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Eid prayer is wajib in the Hanafi school, and missing it requires qada, unlike the sunnah view.

Thirteen Recommended Acts for Eid al-Fitr
Lists thirteen recommended acts for Eid al-Fitr with commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the thirteen recommended acts (mandubat) for Eid al-Fitr according to the Hanafi school and explain the recommended timing of sadaqat al-fitr.

Core Idea
Eid al-Fitr has thirteen sunnan – performing them brings the celebration in line with Prophetic practice and maximizes reward.

Eid al-Fitr is a day of joy and worship. The Hanafi school outlines thirteen recommended acts (mandubat) that enhance the celebration and follow the sunnah of the Prophet (peace be upon him). This lesson presents these acts as a memorization anchor, with special attention to the ruling on sadaqat al-fitr and the etiquette of the Eid prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overarching categories
Group the acts into personal preparation (eating, ghusl, miswak, perfume, clothes), charitable acts (sadaqat al-fitr, abundant charity), and procedural steps (Fajr prayer, proceeding to the musalla, takbir).
This helps in memorizing and understanding the holistic nature of Eid sunnan.
2
Understand the timing of sadaqat al-fitr
The passage distinguishes four timings for payment: before Eid day (allowed), before prayer on Eid day (recommended), after prayer on Eid day (allowed), and after Eid day (valid but sinful).
The mufta bihi is to pay before the prayer.
3
Note the rulings on takbir and the imam's role
The takbir is said quietly while walking to the musalla and stops upon arrival per one narration. The imam should go to the desert (jabbana) and appoint a deputy for the weak in the city.
This reflects the school's flexibility in accommodating different community needs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وندب في الفطر ثلاثة عشر شيئاً: أن يأكل، وأن يكون المأكول تمرا، ووتراً،
استحب
ويغتسل، ويستاك، ويتطيب، ويلبس أحسن ثيابه، ويؤدي صدقة الفطر إن وجبت
الاغتسال مسنون
أي التي يباح لبسها
عليه، ويظهر الفرح والبشاشة وكثرة الصدقة حسب طاقته، والتبكير وهو سرعة الانتباه، والابتكار وهو المسارعة إلى المصلى، وصلاة الصبح في مسجد حيه، ثم
يتوجه إلى المصلى ماشيا مكبرا سرا، ويقطعه إذا انتهى إلى المصلى في رواية،
التكبير
ويؤدي صدقة إلخ: معطوف على "يأكل" ، فيقتضي أن يكون الأداء مندوباً، وهو كذلك؛ لأن الكلام كله قبل الخروج إلى المصلى، فلصدقة الفطر أحوال أحدها قبل دخول يوم العيد، وهو جائز ثانيها: يومه قبل الخروج، وهو مستحب، ثالثها: يومه بعد الصلاة، وهو جائز، رابعها بعد يوم الفطر، وهو صحيح، ويأثم بالتأخير، إلا أنه يرتفع بالأداء كمن أخر الحج بعد القدرة، فإنه يأثم، ثم يزول بالأداء. [البحر الرائق: ٢٤٨/٢] ثم يتوجه إلى المصلى والسنة أن يخرج الإمام إلى الجبانة، ويستخلف من يصلي بالضعفاء في المصر بناءً على أن صلاة العيد في موضعين جائزة بالاتفاق، وعند محمد تجوز في ثلاثة مواضع وإن لم يستخلف له ذلك، =
And it is recommended (nadb) in Fitr (Eid al-Fitr) thirteen things: that he eats, and that what is eaten are dates, and an odd number; and he performs ghusl (bath), and uses a miswak, and applies perfume, and wears his best clothes (those which are permissible to wear), and pays sadaqat al-fitr if it is obligatory upon him, and shows joy and cheerfulness, and gives much charity according to his capacity, and al-tabkir (being quick to awaken), and al-ibtikar (hurrying to the prayer ground), and prays Fajr in his local mosque, then proceeds to the musalla (prayer ground) walking, saying takbir quietly, and he stops it (the takbir) when he arrives at the musalla according to one narration. [Commentary:] The takbir. 'And pays sadaqat al-fitr etc.' is conjoined to 'eats', implying that the payment is recommended, and it is so; because all the speech is before going out to the musalla. Sadaqat al-fitr has states: first, before the entry of the day of Eid – allowed; second, on the day before going out – recommended; third, on the day after prayer – allowed; fourth, after the day of Fitr – valid, but he sins by delaying, except that it is removed by payment, like one who delays Hajj after ability – he sins, then it is removed by performance. (Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 2/248). Then he proceeds to the musalla. And the sunnah is that the imam goes out to the desert (jabbana) and appoints a deputy to pray with the weak in the city, based on the permissibility of Eid prayer in two places by agreement. According to Muhammad, it is permissible in three places even if he does not appoint a deputy for that.
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage lists thirteen recommended (mandub or mustahabb) acts for the day of Eid al-Fitr. These acts are not obligatory but performing them enhances the celebration and follows the Prophetic practice. The list includes: 1) eating before going out for Eid prayer, 2) eating dates specifically, 3) eating an odd number of dates, 4) performing ghusl (ritual bath) – the commentary notes this is musann (sunnah), 5) using a miswak (toothstick), 6) applying perfume, 7) wearing one's best permissible clothes, 8) paying sadaqat al-fitr (if it has become obligatory) before going out – the commentary elaborates that while the payment is recommended at this time, it can be done earlier or even later, with varying degrees of reward; delaying until after Eid day without valid reason is sinful but the obligation is still discharged, akin to delaying Hajj, 9) displaying joy and cheerfulness, 10) giving charity abundantly, 11) al-tabkir (being swift to wake up), 12) al-ibtikar (hurrying to the prayer ground), and 13) praying Fajr in one's local mosque. After these, one proceeds walking to the musalla (open prayer area) while reciting takbir (Allahu Akbar) quietly, and ceasing the takbir upon arrival according to one narration. The commentary also mentions that the imam should go to the desert (outside the city) as a sunnah, but appoint a deputy to lead the prayer for the weak (elderly, sick) inside the city, since Eid prayer can be held in multiple locations by agreement of the Hanafi school, and Imam Muhammad adds a third location possibility even without an appointment. This shows the school's flexibility in accommodating the community while maintaining the sunnah of praying in an open space.

Key Terms
ندب (nadb): Legally recommended (mandub). The text uses 'nadb' to introduce the list, indicating these are recommended acts, not obligatory.
التبكير (al-tabkir): Being swift to wake up early on Eid day.
الابتكار (al-ibtikar): Hurrying to the prayer ground (musalla) early.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on paying sadaqat al-fitr after the Eid prayer on the day of Eid?
A) It is invalid and must be repeated.
B) It is valid but disliked (makruh).
C) It is valid without any sin.
D) It is haram.

Key Takeaway
The thirteen recommended acts for Eid al-Fitr enhance the celebration and follow the sunnah; paying sadaqat al-fitr before the prayer is best, but it remains valid later, though delaying beyond Eid day without excuse is sinful.
